بعلة الأصل: أي بالمعنى الذي يعمل به الأصل من غير نظر إلى أوصاف نفسه، فالزنا لما أقيم مقام الولد في حرمة المصاهرة يعمل بما يعمل به الولد من الأوصاف، ولا ينظر إلى الزنا بأنه حرام، ثم أكد بقوله: ألا ترى إلخ. وصف التراب: يعني إذا جعل التراب خلفاً للماء في إفادة التطهير لا ينظر إلى أوصاف التراب من التلويث وغيره، بل ينظر إلى كون الماء مطهراً. فكذلك هنا إلخ يعني كما لا ينظر إلى أوصاف التراب لقيامه مقام الماء، كذلك لا ينظر في أوصاف الزنا من الحرمة لقيامه مقام الولد الذي ليس فيه هذا الوصف في إيجاب حرمة المصاهرة، فيعمل الزنا وأسبابه في حرمة المصاهرة مثل ما يعمل الولد فيها. وحاصل الجواب أن السبب لحرمة المصاهرة هو الولد كما عرفت وهو ليس بمنهي عنه، وأما الوطء سواء كان بالحرام أو بالحلال فهو ليس بسبب لهذه الحرمة بالذات، وإنما هو سبب بالعرض ويجعله قائماً مقام الولد؛ لأن الوقوف على حقيقة العلوق متعذر، والوطء سبب ظاهر مفض إليه فأقيم مقامه، وجعل الولد كالحاصل تقديراً واحتياطاً، وكما أن الوطء الحلال مفض إليه، كذا الحرام مفض بلا تفاوت فكما جعل الوطء الحلال قائماً مقامه في حرمة المصاهرة كذلك الوطء الحرام جعل قائماً مقامه في ذلك، ولا ينظر إلى وصف الحرمة؛ لأنه إنما يعمل بحيثية النيابة لا من حيث الذات، كما أن التراب إنما يطهر الأحداث لأجل قيامه مقام الماء لا من حيث نفسه، وقال الشافعي محليه: لا تثبت حرمة المصاهرة بالزنا؛ لأنه حرام، فلا يكون سبباً لنعمة، وهي حرمة المصاهرة؛ لأنها تلحق الأجنبية بالأمهات، وقد من الله بها علينا حيث قال: ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ مِنَ الْمَاءِ بَشَراً فَجَعَلَهُ نَسَباً وَصِهْراً﴾ (الفرقان:٥٤)، وعندنا كما يثبت حرمة المصاهرة بالوطء الحلال كذلك يثبت بالزنا ودواعيه من القبلة واللمس والنظر إلى داخل الفرج بشهوة، فيحرم أب الواطئ وابنه على الموطؤة، ويحرم أم الموطؤة وبنتها على الواطئ. هذا توضيح المرام وتحقيق المقام.
And whatever stands in place of something else only operates by the cause of the original. Do you not see that when dust stood in place of water, consideration for purification is given to water being purifying, and the attribute of dust is dropped. So here the attribute of zina is disregarded because it stands in place of what does not have that attribute in establishing the prohibition of marriage relationship. By the cause of the original: i.e., by the meaning by which the original operates without looking at its own attributes. So when zina is made to stand in place of the child in establishing the prohibition of marriage relationship, it operates by the attributes by which the child operates, and no consideration is given to zina being unlawful. Then he emphasized with his statement: 'Do you not see...' etc. The attribute of dust: meaning that when dust is made a substitute for water in effecting purification, no consideration is given to the attributes of dust such as being dirty etc., but rather consideration is given to water being purifying. So likewise here etc. means just as no consideration is given to the attributes of dust because it stands in place of water, so also no consideration is given to the attributes of zina of unlawfulness because it stands in place of the child which does not have this attribute in establishing the prohibition of marriage relationship. So zina and its causes operate in the prohibition of marriage relationship just as the child operates in it. The summary of the answer is that the cause for the prohibition of marriage relationship is the child, as you know, and it is not prohibited. As for intercourse, whether unlawful or lawful, it is not itself a cause for this prohibition, but rather it is a cause incidentally and is made to stand in place of the child; because knowing the exact moment of conception is difficult, and intercourse is an apparent cause leading to it, so it is made to stand in its place, and the child is considered as if it has occurred by estimation and precaution. And just as lawful intercourse leads to it, so unlawful intercourse leads without difference. So just as lawful intercourse is made to stand in its place in the prohibition of marriage relationship, so also unlawful intercourse is made to stand in its place in that, and no consideration is given to the attribute of unlawfulness; because it operates by the quality of representation, not by its own essence, just as dust only purifies the states of impurity because of its standing in place of water, not by its own essence. And al-Shafi‘i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The prohibition of marriage relationship is not established by zina, because it is unlawful, so it cannot be a cause for a blessing, and that is the prohibition of marriage relationship, because it attaches the unrelated woman to the mothers, and Allah has blessed us with it where He said: 'And it is He who has created from water a human being and made him a lineage and a marriage relationship' (al-Furqan: 54). And according to us, just as the prohibition of marriage relationship is established by lawful intercourse, so also it is established by zina and its causes, such as kissing, touching, and looking with desire into the private part of the vulva. So the father of the man and his son become prohibited to the woman, and the mother of the woman and her daughter become prohibited to the man. This is a clarification of the intent and verification of the station.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the principle of qaa'im maqam (substitution) in Hanafi usul. It explains that when something stands as a substitute for something else, it takes the legal ruling based on the 'illah (cause) of the original, not its own attributes. The author supports this with two examples: tayammum and zina. For tayammum, dust purifies not because of its own quality but because it stands in place of water. For zina, the prohibition of marriage relationship (mahramiyyah) is established even though zina is unlawful, because it stands in place of the child (the actual cause) due to the difficulty of ascertaining paternity. The passage then records a madhhab dispute: Imam al-Shafi'i denied that zina creates mahramiyyah, arguing that a sin cannot be a cause for a blessing, citing the Quranic verse that presents marriage relationship as a blessing. The Hanafi response is that the cause is the intercourse itself as a substitute for the child, and the prohibition is not a 'blessing' but a legal ruling; the attribute of unlawfulness is disregarded because the substitute acts by the cause of the original. The passage concludes by listing the specific relatives who become mahram through both zina and lawful intercourse.

Key Terms
قائم مقام (qaa'im maqam): Something that stands in place of another in legal effect, operating by the cause of the original rather than its own attributes.
علة الأصل ('illat al-asl): The effective cause of the original ruling that determines the legal effect; the substitute is measured by this cause.
حرمة المصاهرة (hurmat al-musaharah): The prohibition of marriage relationship through affinity, established by intercourse (both lawful and unlawful) leading to specific in-laws.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between Hanafi and Shafi'i on this issue?
A) Hanafi considers zina as a blessing; Shafi'i does not.
B) In Hanafi, the father and son of the man become mahram to the woman; in Shafi'i, they do not.
C) In Hanafi, the woman must observe iddah; in Shafi'i, she does not.
D) There is no practical difference.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, through the principle of substitution, holds that zina establishes mahramiyyah, overriding the attribute of sinfulness.

The Definition of Sabab (Cause) and Three Scholarly Positions
Defining 'sabab' and presenting three madhahib on causation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sabab, distinguish it from independent causation, and identify the three scholarly positions on causes in Shariah.

Core Idea
A sabab is a sign set by Allah, not an independent cause of obligation.

This lesson unpacks the usul al-fiqh concept of 'sabab' (cause). You will learn its precise definition and then explore three major scholarly views on how causes relate to legal rulings. The Hanafi position holds that causes are markers (alamaat) established by the Lawgiver, while other schools either deny causation entirely or limit it to certain types of rulings. Understanding this distinction is crucial for sound legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Define sabab linguistically and technically
First, grasp the linguistic meaning (means to an end) and the technical usul definition: an apparent, precise attribute indicated by revealed evidence as a marker for a ruling.
The rope example illustrates the linguistic sense.
2
Identify the three madhahib on causation
Separate the three positions: (1) Hanafi and others affirm causation as signs; (2) some usuliyyun deny causes entirely; (3) Ash'aris differentiate between rights of servants and acts of worship.
Note the arguments and counter-arguments for each.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the second school
Understand why the Hanafis reject the denial: causes are not independent obligers; they are made signs by Allah. The example of killing via a sword shows attribution to the killer without negating the instrument's role.
The Dar al-Harb exemption is based on hardship, not denial of causation.
4
Evaluate the rejection of the Ash'ari distinction
The text calls the Ash'ari distinction 'weak' because if some rulings can be attributed to causes by evidence, consistency demands the same for all rulings.
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf: practical differences in how rulings are justified.

وفي غير المنصوص عليه يتعلّق بالوصف الذي جعل علةً ويكون ذلك علامة لثبوت الحكم في الفرع بايجاب الله تعالى مستدلّين بأن الإيجاب صفة خاصة له تعالى كصفة التخليق وفي إضافة الإيجاب إلى الأسباب الله تعالى وبأن الأسباب لو كانت عللا للأحكام لما تصوّر الانفكاك بينها وبين الأحكام والحال أنه يوجد؛ لأن الأسباب كانت موجودةً قبل الشرع ولم تكن الأحكام، وكذا من أسلم في دار الحرب ولم يهاجر إلينا يتحقق الأسباب في لما جاز إضافة بعض الأحكام إلى الأسباب بالدليل جاز إضافة سائرها إلى الأسباب بالدليل، وهذه أمثلة للأسباب.
Chapter on explaining the causes of the Shariah. [Causes of the Shariah] i.e., established in the Shariah. Chapter on explaining the causes of the Shariah. Know that the fundamentals (usul) and branches (furu') of the religion are legislated by causes which the Shariah made causes for them. 'Chapter on explaining' etc., i.e., explaining the ways by which the legislated matters are known and established. 'Sabab' linguistically is that by which one can reach the objective; hence the rope is called 'sabab' because it enables reaching the objective. In the Shariah, it is applied to every apparent, precise description which the revealed evidence (dalil sam'i) indicates is a marker for establishing a legal ruling, i.e., the revealed evidence shows that the Lawgiver made it a sign for the establishment of a certain ruling. There are three schools regarding this: The first school is the way of most of our companions (Hanafis) and some Shafi'is, and the majority—the author explained it with his statement: 'Know' etc. The fundamentals of religion (usul al-din) are faith in Allah and His attributes, and its branches (furu') are the rest of the legal rulings, acts of worship, transactions, expiations, and penalties. 'Causes for them' i.e., for those fundamentals and branches. The summary is that the legal rulings have causes to which they are attributed, while the obliger and legislator is Allah alone, not the cause; because the one who obliges rulings is only Allah. The second school is that of some usuliyyun (theologians) who deny causes entirely and say: The ruling on what is explicitly mentioned is established by the apparent text, and on what is not explicitly mentioned, it is attached to the description that is made the 'illa, and that is a sign for the establishment of the ruling in the branch by the obligation of Allah—they argue that obligation is a specific attribute of Allah like the attribute of creation, and that attributing obligation to causes is (wrong). And they argue that if causes were effective causes of rulings, then separation between them and rulings would not be conceivable, but yet it exists; because causes existed before the Shariah and rulings did not exist. Similarly, one who becomes Muslim in Dar al-Harb and does not emigrate to us—the causes are realized in his case, yet the acts of worship are not obligatory upon him. The author pointed to the answer with his statement: 'The Shariah made them causes for them'—for we do not say that causes are obligatory by themselves such that it would necessitate removing (obligation) from Allah; because obligation can only be conceived from an obliger. Rather, the cause is what leads to the ruling. So attributing the ruling to the cause does not prevent attributing it to something else, as you see in killing: it actually occurs by an instrument like a sword, yet it is attributed to the killer such that blood-money (qisas) is obligatory upon him. And causes are not made obliging except by Allah making them so. Thus we say: before the Shariah came, Allah did not make them causes. As for the dropping of worship obligations from one who believed but did not emigrate to us, it is based on removing hardship. The third school is that of the majority of Ash'aris: they differentiated between the rights of servants and penal punishments on one hand and acts of worship on the other. They said: The former have causes to which their obligation is attributed, because they result from the servant's acquisition, so they are attributed to him. As for the latter (acts of worship), their obligation is only attributed to Allah's command and address. We say: This distinction is weak; because when it is permissible to attribute some rulings to causes by evidence, it is permissible to attribute all of them to causes by evidence. And these are examples of causes.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'sabab' (cause) in usul al-fiqh and presents three scholarly positions on the role of causes in Shariah. The author first gives the linguistic and technical definition: linguistically, a sabab is a means to an end; technically, it is an apparent and precisely defined attribute that the revealed evidence indicates as a marker for a ruling, established by the Lawgiver. Three madhahib are discussed: (1) The majority of Hanafis and some Shafi'is affirm that rulings have causes (asbab) to which they are attributed, but the true obliger is Allah alone. Rulings are attributed to causes in a metaphorical sense, just as killing is attributed to the killer even though the sword is the instrument. (2) Some usuliyyun deny causes entirely, arguing that obligation is an attribute of Allah alone, and that causes existed before Shariah without rulings; they also cite the example of a Muslim in Dar al-Harb who is exempt from worship despite fulfilling causes. The author refutes them by stating that causes are not independent obligers; they are merely signs made by Allah. The exemption in Dar al-Harb is based on removing hardship, not denial of causation. (3) The majority of Ash'aris distinguish between rights of servants/punishments and acts of worship; the former have causes attributed to the servant, the latter only to Allah. The author rejects this as weak because if some rulings can be attributed to causes by evidence, then all can. The passage sets the Hanafi position that causes are valid as signs, but the ultimate source of obligation is Allah.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): An apparent and precise attribute that the revealed evidence indicates is a marker (alama) for the establishment of a legal ruling.
أصل (asl): The fundamentals of religion, i.e., faith in Allah and His attributes.
فرع (far'): The branches of the religion: all legal rulings including worship, transactions, expiations, penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A sabab is a divinely appointed sign that indicates when a ruling applies, but the source of all obligation is Allah alone.

Cause Repetition through Descriptor Renewal (Taqdir)
Explains how a ruling repeats due to estimative renewal of the cause's descriptor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a cause is treated as repeated (taqdiran) when its descriptor renews, and use it to explain the repetition of sadaqat al-fitr and zakat.

Core Idea
A cause is estimatively repeated when its descriptor renews, making the ruling repeat.

This passage from a usul commentary delves into a critical Hanafi principle: how a non-repeating cause can still produce a repeating obligation. The key lies in the descriptor (wasf) of the cause. If the descriptor renews over time—like the need for maintenance for a person or the growth potential of wealth—the cause is legally considered renewed. This concept, called taqdir, allows the Hanafi school to explain annual obligations like sadaqat al-fitr and zakat without relying on time as the direct cause. Understanding this principle is essential for comprehending the structure of repetitive legal duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core puzzle
Why does a person owe sadaqat al-fitr every year even though the cause (the person) remains the same? Understand that the cause's descriptor (need for maintenance) is time-dependent.
Time is a condition (shart), not the cause (sabab).
2
Examine the analogy to zakat
Compare with zakat: the wealth (nisab) is the cause; its descriptor (growth, nama') renews each year. The obligation repeats due to the renewal of the descriptor, not the wealth itself.
Hawl is the condition; the cause is the wealth with the attribute of growth.
3
Understand taqdir (estimative repetition)
Hanafis treat the cause as 'repeated by estimation' (taqdiran) when its descriptor renews. This bridges the gap between a static cause and a recurring ruling.
Taqdir is a legal fiction applied to maintain continuity.
4
Apply to 'ushr and kharaj
The same principle applies: land is the cause, but the descriptor (actual produce or ability to cultivate) renews each season, leading to annual tax obligations.
For 'ushr, actual produce; for kharaj, potential for cultivation.
5
Refute the objection
Opponents might say time is the cause because the obligation repeats with time. The Hanafi response: time is merely a condition; the true cause is the person's need, which renews estimatively.
The condition (time) marks when the obligation is due, but the basis is the cause's descriptor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان أسباب الشرائع
وتكرّر الوجوب بتكرّر الفطر بمنزلة تكرّر وجوب الزكاة بتكرّر الحول.
السبب بتجدد الوصف بمنزلة المتجدد بنفسه
لأن الوصف الذي لأجله كان الرأس سبباً وهو المؤونة يتجدد بتجدّد الزمان، كما أن النماء الذي لأجله كان المال سبباً لوجوب الزكاة، يتجدد بتجدد الحول، ويصير السبب بتجدّد الوصف بمنزلة المتجدد بنفسه. وعلى هذا تكرر العشر والخراج مع اتحاد السبب، وهو الأرض النامية في العشر حقيقةً بالخارج، وفي الخراج حكما بالتمكن من الزراعة.
والأصل في وجوب المؤونة هو الرأس؛ لأنه يلي عليه دون الوقت؛ إذ الرأس هو المحتاج إلى المؤونة دون الوقت، ولما كان يرد عليه أن الترجيح للوقت؛ لأن وجوب الصدقة يتكرّر بتكرره، وهذا علامة السبب لا يوجد في الرأس؛ لأنه لا تكرّر فيه أجاب عنه بقوله : وتكرّر الوجوب إلخ : يعني تكرر وجوب الصدقة ليس بتكرر الشرط الذي هو الفطر، بل بسبب تكرر السبب وهو الرأس، وهو وإن لم يكن متكرّراً حقيقةً لكنه جعل متكرراً تقديراً؛ لأجل تكرر الفطر أي وقته، كما أن المال الذي هو سبب الزكاة جعل متكرّرا تقديراً لأجل تكرر الحول الذي هو شرط كأنه متكرّر ، فكذا الحال في الرأس. المؤونة يتجدد إلخ: يعني لما صار الرأس سبباً لوجوب الصدقة بوصف المؤونة كما عرفت وهي تتجدّد بتجدد وقت الفطر كان الرأس بمنزلة المتجدد بنفسه لتجدد وصفه، كما أن النصاب سبب لوجوب الزكاة بوصف النماء، والنماء يتجدّد ويتكرّر بتكرر الحول صار المال متكرراً بنفسه لتكرر وصفه، حتى يتكرر وجوب الزكاة في نصاب واحد بتكرر الحول. وعلى هذا: الطريق وهو أن السبب يتكرر بتكرّر الوصف تكرر العشر إلخ. مع اتحاد السبب إلخ: يعني مع أن السبب للعشر والخراج واحد وهو الأرض النامية حقيقةً في العشر، والأرض النامية تقديراً في الخراج بأن يتمكن النماء من الزراعة يتكرّر وجوبهما بسبب تكرر وصف السبب، وهو الخارج حقيقة في العشر، والتمكن في الخراج، وذلك لأن بتكرر الوصف جعل السبب متكرّرا تقديراً فيتكرر الحكم بتكرّره التقديري، فإذا حدث الخارج من الأرض تحقيقاً يجب العشر، وإن اصطلمت الأرض آفة يسقط تيسيرًا بحال المسلم، وبتكرر الوجوب يتكرر النماء، وإذا وجد التمكن من الزراعة وجب الخراج، سواء زرع الأرض أو عطلها؛ لأنه يليق بحال الكافر المتوغل في الدنيا.
المؤون في "المغرب" مانه يمونه أي قام بكفايته.
Chapter on Explanation of the Causes of Legal Rulings.
And the repetition of obligation by repetition of the breaking of fast is like the repetition of the obligation of zakat by repetition of the year.
The cause, by the renewal of its descriptor, is in the position of what is renewed itself.
Because the descriptor for which the head (person) is a cause—which is maintenance (mu'una)—renews with the renewal of time, just as the growth (nama') for which wealth is a cause for the obligation of zakat renews with the renewal of the year. The cause becomes, by the renewal of the descriptor, like what is renewed itself. And upon this is the repetition of 'ushr and kharaj with the unity of the cause, which is the productive land—in 'ushr, actually by the produce; in kharaj, legally by the ability to cultivate.
And the basis for the obligation of maintenance is the head (person); because it pertains to him, not to time, since the head is in need of maintenance, not time. And when it was objected that priority is given to time because the obligation of charity repeats by its repetition, and this is a sign of the cause not found in the head because it does not repeat, he answered by his statement: 'and the repetition of obligation etc.': meaning that the repetition of the obligation of charity is not by repetition of the condition (shart) which is the breaking of fast, but rather by repetition of the cause (sabab) which is the head. And although it is not repeated in reality, it is made repeated by estimation (taqdiran) because of the repetition of the breaking of fast, i.e., its time. Just as wealth, which is the cause of zakat, is made repeated by estimation because of the repetition of the year which is a condition, as if it were repeated, so too the case with the head. 'Maintenance renews etc.': he means: since the head became a cause for the obligation of charity by the descriptor of maintenance as you know, and it renews with the renewal of the time of the breaking of fast, the head is in the position of being renewed itself due to the renewal of its descriptor. Just as the nisab is a cause for the obligation of zakat by the descriptor of growth, and growth renews and repeats with the repetition of the year, wealth becomes repeatedly itself due to the repetition of its descriptor, such that the obligation of zakat repeats in a single nisab with the repetition of the year. And upon this: the way—that the cause repeats by repetition of the descriptor—'ushr repeats etc. With the unity of the cause etc.: meaning that although the cause for 'ushr and kharaj is one, i.e., productive land—in 'ushr actually, and in kharaj by estimation, such that growth is possible from cultivation—their obligations repeat due to the repetition of the descriptor of the cause, which is the produce actually in 'ushr, and the ability in kharaj. And that is because by the repetition of the descriptor, the cause is made repeated by estimation, so the ruling repeats by its estimative repetition. So if produce actually issues from the land, 'ushr becomes obligatory; if an affliction destroys the land, it is dropped as a facility for the condition of the Muslim. And by the repetition of obligation, growth repeats. And if ability to cultivate is found, kharaj becomes obligatory, whether he planted the land or left it barren, because it befits the condition of the disbeliever deeply engrossed in worldly life.
Al-mu'un in "al-Mughrib" is derived from 'mana-hu' meaning he provided for his needs.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a detailed scholastic commentary on a rule in usul al-fiqh concerning the repetition of legal obligations. The core issue is how a cause (sabab) can be considered 'repeated' so that the ruling (hukm) repeats even though the cause itself is not physically renewed. The author uses the example of sadaqat al-fitr (charity of breaking the fast) and zakat (obligatory alms). In sadaqat al-fitr, the cause is the person (head) who needs maintenance; the condition (shart) is the occurrence of the day of fitr. The obligation repeats each year because the descriptor of the cause—the need for maintenance—renews with time. Similarly, for zakat, the cause is the wealth (nisab) and the descriptor is growth (nama'), which renews with each passing year (hawl). Although the wealth itself may not be new, it is treated as repeatedly causing obligation because its descriptor renews. This principle is then applied to 'ushr (tithe on agricultural produce) and kharaj (land tax). For 'ushr, the cause is productive land, and the descriptor is the actual produce; for kharaj, the descriptor is the potential for cultivation. In both, the cause is considered repeated by the renewal of the descriptor, so the tax obligations repeat. The commentary also addresses an objection: why prioritize the head over time? The answer is that the obligation is tied to the cause (head) which has the descriptor that renews, not to the condition (time) alone. Thus the ruling follows the estimative repetition of the cause.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): That which necessitates a ruling by its existence, here specifically the person (head) for fitr or wealth for zakat
وصف (wasf): Descriptor or attribute of the cause that is subject to renewal, e.g., need for maintenance or growth
تقديراً (taqdiran): By legal estimation or presumption, treating something as existent for legal purposes even if not physically so

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis in this passage, what is the basis for the repetition of sadaqat al-fitr?
A) The repetition of the day of fitr (time)
B) The estimative renewal of the cause (head) via its descriptor (mu'una)
C) The change in nisab each year
D) The increase in the number of heads

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a ruling repeats when the cause's descriptor repeats, even if the cause itself is static, achieved through the principle of taqdir.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Hanafi Classification of Rukhsah: Qasr as Isqat
Defining rukhsah and proving qasr as isqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between rukhsah isqat and rukhsah tarkhis, apply it to qasr al-salat, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Qasr is a pure dropping of the obligation, not a permission: the traveler must pray two rak'ahs.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi view of rukhsah (concession) as a category of legal rulings. The key focus is the classification of qasr al-salat (shortening prayer in travel) as a rukhsah isqat (dropping of the original obligation). We will trace the definition of rukhsah, its types, and the proof from the hadith of sadaqah, and contrast this with the Shafi'i understanding that qasr is a permission (tarkhis) with choice.

Guided Path
1
Define rukhsah and its types in Hanafi usul
Understand the two types: isqat (dropping) and tarkhis (permission). In isqat, the original obligation ('azima) is completely removed and its performance is not permissible. In tarkhis, the original obligation remains valid but a lighter alternative is permitted.
Rukhsah isqat is a stronger form; tarkhis allows choice.
2
Identify the core example: qasr al-salat
Locate the passage where the author states that qasr is a 'rukhsah isqat' according to the Hanafi school. Note that the traveler's prayer is reduced from four to two rak'ahs, and performing four is not allowed.
The text says: 'For the exception occurring in His statement...' leading to the ruling.
3
Analyze the dalil: the hadith of sadaqah
Examine the hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) called qasr a 'sadaqah'. Understand that a sadaqah of something that cannot be owned (like waiving retaliation) is a pure dropping (isqat) that does not require acceptance by the recipient.
The hadith is narrated by Ya'la ibn Umayyah via Umar.
4
Examine the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school argues from Quran 4:101 that 'no blame' indicates permissibility, and from the word 'accept' in the hadith that acceptance is required, making it a permission. The Hanafi response is that the condition of fear is incidental, and 'accept' means 'act upon'.
The Hanafi rebuttal also uses the athar from Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Aisha.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical difference: if a traveler prays four rak'ahs intentionally, Hanafis consider it invalid (mixing nafl with fard), while Shafi'is consider it valid as optional.
This difference arises from the classification of qasr.

فصل في العزيمة والرخصة

القصر رخصة إسقاط. المكره والمضطر أصلاً للاستثناء، حتى لا يسعهما الصبر عنهما، وكذلك الرجل سقط غسله في مدة المسح أصلاً لعدم سراية الحدث إليه، وكذلك قصر الصلاة في حق المسافر رخصة إسقاط عندنا. ولهذا قلنا: إن ظهر المسافر وفجره سواء لا يحتمل الزيادة عليه. للاستثناء الواقع في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَدْ فَصَّلَ لَكُمْ مَا حَرَّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِلَّا مَا اضْطُرِرْتُمْ إِلَيْهِ﴾ (الأنعام: ۱۱۹)، فقوله: "إلا ما اضطررتم" استثناء من قوله: "ما حرّم عليكم"، فكأنه قيل: وقد فصل لكم ما حرم عليكم في جميع الأحوال إلا حال الضرورة، فتبدّلت الحرمة بالإباحة في حقهما، ولم يبق الحرمة مشروعة وعزيمة. الصبر عنهما: أي عن الخمر والميتة عند الضرورة، فإن لم يأكل الميتة ولم يشرب الخمر في هذا الوقت ومات يموت آثماً، فإطلاق اسم الرخصة على أكلها وشربها مجاز، من حيث لم يبق الحرمة في حقهما أصلاً، ولكن حرمتهما باقية في حق غيرهما، فحصل له شبهة حقيقة الرخصة، فلذا صار هذا القسم أنقص في المجازية. وعن أبي يوسف والشافعي رحمهما الله: أنه لا تسقط الحرمة ولكن يؤاخذ بها كما في إجراء كلمة الكفر بالإكراه، فيكون من قبيل القسمين الأولين. ودليلهما قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنِ اضْطُرَّ غَيْرَ بَاغٍ وَلا عَادٍ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ (البقرة: ۱73)، فإطلاق المغفرة دليل صريح على قيام الحرمة؛ لأن الغفران يترتب على ارتكاب الممنوع. والجواب أن المضطرّ قلما يكتفي بقدر الضرورة، والتجاوز عن هذا المقدار ممنوع، فلذا أورد المغفرة بقوله: "غفور رحيم". ويظهر ثمرة الخلاف فيما إذا حلف لا يأكل حراماً، فأكل الميتة في حالة الاضطرار يحنث عندهما، لا عندنا. لعدم سراية الحدث إليه لأن استتار القدم بالخف يمنع سراية الحدث إلى القدم ولا يجب غسل شيء من البدن بدون الحدث في الطهارة الحكمية، فثبت أن الغسل الذي هو العزيمة ساقط في هذا الموضع، فإطلاق اسم الرخصة عليه بطريق المجاز، ولكنه مشروع في حال عدم التخفف، فكان أنقص في المجازية، فكان كسقوط العينية والحرمة فيما تقدم. رخصة إسقاط أي إسقاط العزيمة حتى لا يجوز العمل بها. الزيادة عليه وهو الركعتان وذلك لأن السبب لم يوجب في حقه إلا الركعتين، فإن صلى في الظهر أربعاً كانت الأخريان نافلة، ولا يجوز خلط النفل بالفرض قصداً. وعند الشافعي رخصة طرفية، والأولى فيها العمل بالعزيمة. ودليله قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا ضَرَبْتُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَنْ تَقْصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلاةِ إِنْ خِفْتُمْ أَنْ يَفْتِنَكُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا﴾ (النساء: ۱۰۱)، علق القصر بالخوف، ونفي فيه الجناح، وإنه للإباحة دون الوجوب.

وإنما جعلناها إسقاطاً محضاً استدلالاً بدليل الرخصة ومعناها. أما الدليل فما روي عن عمر أنه قال: أنقصر الصلاة ونحن آمنون؟ فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "هذه صدقة تصدق الله بها عليكم، فاقبلوا صدقته". سماه صدقة، والتصدق بما لا يحتمل التمليك إسقاط محض لا يحتمل الرد، كالعفو عن القصاص. وأما المعنى فهو أن الرخصة لطلب الرفق متعين في القصر، فسقط الإكمال أصلاً. نفي الجناح إنما هو لتطيب أنفسهم لمظنة أن يخطر ببالهم أن عليهم جناحاً في القصر، وإن قيد الخوف اتفاقي لا يتوقف القصر عليه كما ستعلم. ودليلنا ما بينه المصنف بقوله: وإنما جعلناها إلخ. هذه صدقة إلخ وهذا حديث يعلى بن أمية قال: سألت عمر بن الخطاب، قلت: ﴿فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَنْ تَقْصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلاةِ إِنْ خِفْتُمْ أَنْ يَفْتِنَكُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا﴾ (النساء: ۱۰۱)، وقد أمن الناس؟ فقال لي عمر: عجبت منه، فسألتُ رسول الله عن ذلك فقال: "صدقة تصدق الله بها عليكم فاقبلوا صدقته". رواه مسلم [رقم: ۱۵۷۳] والترمذي مع فرق يسير. ولأبي حنيفة أيضاً أثر عمر بن الخطاب قال: صلاة السفر ركعتان، وصلاة الضحى ركعتان، وصلاة الفطر ركعتان وصلاة الجمعة ركعتان تمام من غير قصر على لسان محمد. أخرجه النسائي وابن ماجة. [رقم: ۱۰۶۳] وأثر ابن عباس قال: قد فرض الله الصلاة على نبيكم في الحضر أربعاً، وفي السفر ركعتين، وفي الخوف ركعة. مسلم [رقم: ۱۵۷۵] وأثر عائشة هما متفق عليه، وحديث ابن عمر أخرجه البخاري. كالعفو عن القصاص: وحاصل الدليل أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سمى هذا القصر صدقة، والتصدق بشيء لا يحتمل التمليك بوجه ما، كالعفو عن القصاص وغيره يكون إسقاطاً محضاً لا يحتمل الرد حتى لا يتوقف على قبول العبد، وإن كان المتصدق ممن لا تلزم إطاعته، فإن كان ممن تلزم إطاعته وهو الله تعالى فأولى بعدم الرد، فعلى هذا يكون معنى قوله: "فاقبلوا صدقته": فاعملوا بها، كما يقال فلان قبل الشرائع أي اعتقدها وعمل بها. فاندفع ما قال الشافعي: إن الصدقة لا تتم إلا بقبول المتصدق عليه، ولهذا قال فاقبلوا، فقبل القبول بقي على ما كان. وقوله: "بما لا يحتمل التمليك" احتراز عن الصدقة بالدين على من عليه الدين؛ لأنها تحتاج إلى قبول المديون حتى ترتد برده؛ لأن الدين يحتمل التمليك من المديون ولا يحتمل من غيره؛ لأنه مال من وجه دون وجه، فلا يكون التصدق به إسقاطاً محضا. أن الرخصة لطلب إلخ والحاصل أن الاستدلال بمعنى الرخصة على وجهين: أحدهما وهو أن الرخصة الحقيقة إذا ثبتت في شيء ثبت الاختيار للعبد بين الإقدام على الرخصة وبين الإتيان بالعزيمة؛ لأن العزيمة أيضاً تتضمن اليسر أما فضل ثواب كما في الإكراه على إجراء كلمة الكفر، وأما يسراً آخر
Section on Determination and Concession. The shortening of prayer is a concession of dropping (the obligation). The coerced and the compelled (are) originally for exception, such that they cannot forbear them. Similarly, the man's washing is dropped during the period of wiping due to the non-transmission of impurity to him. Similarly, shortening prayer for the traveler is a concession of dropping according to us. Hence we say: the noon and dawn prayers of the traveler are equal, not admitting increase upon it. For the exception occurring in His statement: 'And He has detailed for you what He has forbidden to you except what you are compelled to' (al-An'am 6:119). His statement 'except what you are compelled' is an exception from His statement 'what He has forbidden to you'. It is as if it was said: He has detailed for you what He has forbidden to you in all circumstances except the case of necessity, so the prohibition changed to permissibility in their right, and the prohibition did not remain as a determined obligation. Forbearing them: i.e., wine and carrion at the time of necessity. If one does not eat carrion and does not drink wine at this time and dies, he dies sinful. So applying the name of concession to eating and drinking them is metaphorical, since the prohibition did not remain in their right at all, but their prohibition remains in the right of others, so a semblance of the reality of concession occurred for him. Thus this category became lower in metaphor. From Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them): that the prohibition is not dropped, but one is held accountable for it, as in uttering words of disbelief under duress, so it is from the first two categories. Their proof is His statement: 'But whoever is compelled, neither desiring nor transgressing, there is no sin upon him. Indeed, Allah is Forgiving and Merciful' (al-Baqarah 2:173). The mention of forgiveness is explicit evidence for the existence of prohibition, because forgiveness is consequent upon committing the prohibited. The answer: that the compelled rarely suffices with the amount of necessity, and exceeding this amount is prohibited, hence forgiveness is mentioned with His statement 'Forgiving, Merciful'. And the fruit of the difference appears in the case if one swears not to eat what is forbidden, then eats carrion in a state of necessity – he breaks the oath according to them, not according to us. Due to the non-transmission of impurity to him, because the covering of the foot by the khuff prevents transmission of impurity to the foot, and washing of any part of the body is not obligatory without impurity in the legal purity. Thus it is established that washing, which is the determination, is dropped in this place, so applying the name of concession to it is metaphorical, but it is legislated in the state of not having a khuff. So it was lower in metaphor, and it was like dropping of the specific obligation and prohibition in what preceded. Concession of dropping means dropping of the determination such that acting upon it is not permissible. The increase upon it: i.e., the two rak'ahs, because the cause obligated only two rak'ahs for him. If he prays four in al-zuhr, the last two are supererogatory, and mixing supererogatory with obligatory intentionally is not permissible. According to al-Shafi'i, it is a concession of facility, and acting upon the determination is preferable. His proof is His statement: 'And when you travel in the land, there is no blame upon you for shortening the prayer, if you fear that those who disbelieve may afflict you' (al-Nisa 4:101). He attached shortening to fear, and denied blame, and it indicates permissibility, not obligation. And we only made it pure dropping by way of inference from the proof of concession and its meaning. As for the proof: what is narrated from Umar that he said: 'We shorten the prayer while we are safe?' The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'This is a charity which Allah has given to you, so accept His charity.' He called it charity, and donating something that does not admit ownership is pure dropping that does not admit revocation, like waiving a retaliation. As for the meaning: that concession for seeking ease is determined in shortening, so completion dropped entirely. The denial of blame is only to put their minds at ease due to the suspicion that they would feel blame for shortening, and the condition of fear is incidental – shortening is not dependent on it as you will know. And our proof is what the author stated with his statement: 'And we only made it...'. This is the hadith of Ya'la b. Umayyah who said: I asked Umar b. al-Khattab: 'There is no blame upon you for shortening the prayer if you fear...' and people are safe? Umar said: I wondered about that, so I asked the Messenger of Allah about it, and he said: 'A charity which Allah has given to you, so accept His charity.' Reported by Muslim and al-Tirmidhi with a slight difference. Also Abu Hanifa has the athar of Umar b. al-Khattab who said: The prayer of travel is two rak'ahs, the prayer of Duha is two rak'ahs, the prayer of al-Fitr is two rak'ahs, and the prayer of Jumu'ah is two rak'ahs, complete without shortening according to the tongue of Muhammad. Reported by al-Nasa'i and Ibn Majah. And the athar of Ibn Abbas: Allah has prescribed the prayer for your Prophet in residence as four, in travel as two, and in fear as one. Muslim. And the athar of A'isha – both agreed upon, and hadith of Ibn Umar reported by al-Bukhari. Like waiving a retaliation: The gist of the proof is that the Prophet (ﷺ) called this shortening a charity, and donating something that does not admit ownership in any way, like waiving a retaliation and similar, is pure dropping that does not admit revocation, so it does not depend on acceptance by the slave. And if the donor is one whose obedience is not required, then if he is one whose obedience is required – i.e., Allah Almighty – then non-revocation is even more appropriate. On this basis, the meaning of his statement 'accept His charity' is: act upon it, as it is said: 'He accepted the laws' i.e., believed in them and acted upon them. Thus what al-Shafi'i said is refuted: that charity is only complete with the acceptance of the recipient, and therefore he said 'accept', and before acceptance it remains as before. His statement 'that does not admit ownership' is a precaution regarding charity of a debt owed by someone else; because it requires acceptance by the debtor such that it is revoked by his rejection, because a debt admits ownership from the debtor but not from others, since it is wealth from one perspective but not another. Thus donating it is not pure dropping. The conclusion: inference from the meaning of concession is two-fold: first: when the reality of concession is established in something, the slave has choice between proceeding with the concession and performing the determination; because the determination also includes ease – either extra reward as in duress to utter words of disbelief, or another ease.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the concept of rukhsah (concession) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, specifically its classification and application to qasr al-salat (shortening prayer in travel). The author begins by stating that qasr is a 'rukhsah isqat' (concession of dropping the obligation), distinguishing it from other types of rukhsah. Three scenarios are initially compared: (1) the coerced and compelled person for whom prohibitions are lifted due to necessity (example of wine and carrion), (2) the one who wipes over khuff instead of washing feet, where the washing obligation is dropped, and (3) qasr for travelers. The core point is that in these cases, the original obligation ('azima) is completely lifted, not merely made optional. The text then explores a dispute: Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i hold that the prohibition (hurma) remains even under necessity, based on Quran 2:173 where forgiveness is mentioned, implying sin. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the compelled rarely limits himself to exact necessity, so forgiveness covers transgression of proper limits. A practical difference (thamara) is shown: if one swears not to eat forbidden food and eats carrion under necessity, he breaks the oath according to them but not according to Hanafis. The discussion shifts to qasr specifically. The Hanafi position is that qasr is a pure dropping (isqat mahd) and not a mere permission (tarkhis). This is proved by the hadith of Umar where the Prophet called it a 'sadaqah' (charity). Since charity of this type (something that cannot be owned, like waiving a retaliation) is a pure dropping that does not require acceptance, qasr is likewise not a choice but a replacement obligation. Further evidence includes athar from Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Aisha affirming that prayer in travel is two rak'ahs as a prescribed duty, not a concession. The author refutes al-Shafi'i's argument that Quran 4:101 indicates permission (with 'no blame') rather than obligation, by noting that the condition of fear is incidental, and the hadith of sadaqah clarifies the nature. Finally, the text contrasts this with the general meaning of rukhsah: normally a concession implies choice between the easier act and the original determination, but in qasr, the original (four rak'ahs) is not permissible, showing it is a pure dropping.

Key Terms
العزيمة (al-ʿazīmah): The original, stricter legal ruling that is not alleviated by necessity.
الرخصة (al-rukhṣah): A legal concession that relaxes or drops the original obligation due to necessity or hardship.
الإسقاط (al-isqāṭ): The complete removal of the obligation ('azima) so that it is no longer valid to perform it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the nature of qasr al-salat in travel?
A) It is a rukhsah tarkhis where the traveler may choose between shortening and full prayer.
B) It is a rukhsah isqat where the obligation of four rak'ahs is completely dropped and two are obligatory.
C) It is a dispensation that applies only if there is fear of enemies.
D) It is a permission that requires acceptance by the traveler.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qasr is a rukhsah isqat: a pure dropping of the obligation, making two rak'ahs mandatory in travel.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Takhyir and Rukhsa: When Choice Brings Ease
Explaining the usul rule on takhyir and rukhsa with three cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that takhyir produces a genuine rukhsa only when the alternatives differ in legal reality, and identify exceptions based on conditions (intent of the suspending condition and financial ability).

Core Idea
Choice between two rulings is a concession only if they differ in nature, not just in number.

This passage examines a foundational usul principle: when a person is granted a choice (takhyir) between two legal options, does that choice constitute a genuine concession (rukhsa) or merely a technical possibility? The Hanafi answer depends on whether the alternatives are the same in legal reality (haqiqa) or different. Using three key cases – the traveler’s prayer, the slave’s Friday prayer, and a conditional vow of fasting – the author illustrates when takhyir brings ease and when it does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usul rule
Extract the general principle: takhyir produces rukhsa only if the two options are legally distinct (different in hukm/ha‘qiqa). If they are identical in essence, choosing the longer/harder one brings no ease.
The rule is announced in the first line: the traveler's and resident's prayers are 'one' (type), so choice between 2 and 4 does not realize ease.
2
Analyze the first case: traveler's prayer
The traveler may pray qasr (2 rak'ahs) or complete (4). But both are called 'zuhr' and share the same legal reality; only the number differs. Therefore, choosing 4 over 2 does not yield ease – ease is only in the shorter option. Hence no genuine rukhsa.
This sets up the baseline: quantitative difference alone does not create a concession.
3
Contrast with the slave's Friday prayer
A slave may choose between attending Friday prayer (2 rak'ahs) or praying zuhr (4). These are two different obligations (Friday vs. zuhr) with different legal natures. Thus choice here does bring ease, because the alternatives are legally distinct.
The author explicitly rejects an objection that the slave is obligated to Friday; he cites 'Ghayat al-Tahqiq' that the slave is commanded to Friday, but the choice still exists in principle.
4
Examine the conditional vow of fasting
If an insolvent person says 'If I enter the house, I must fast a year' (vow), he has a choice between fasting a year (as vow) or fasting three days (as expiation for an oath). The objection: this is a choice between many and few without ease. The answer: the year's fast is pure worship (qurba), while the three days are expiation (kaffarah) containing a punitive element; they differ in legal reality. Hence the choice involves ease.
Also note the conditions: the choice exists only if the suspending condition is not intended to happen (e.g., 'if I enter' when he does not intend to enter) and if he is insolvent (cannot give other expiation).
5
Synthesize the rule and its conditions
Conclude: Takhyir is a genuine rukhsa only when the two alternatives are legally distinct (differ in hukm/ha‘qiqa). The quantitative difference alone does not create ease. Additional conditions: if the suspending condition is intended, the original obligation (vow) must be fulfilled; if the person is wealthy, the expiation via fasting is not an option, so no choice.
This completes the analysis of the usul rule.

فصل في العزيمة والرخصة
وأما ظهر المسافر والمقيم فواحد فبالتخير بين القليل والكثير لا يتحقق شيء من معنى الرفق
وهو الركعتان
وظهر المقيم وهو أربع ركعات فواحد حتى صح بناء أحدهما على الآخر. لا يتحقق شيء إلى آخره لتعين الرفق في الأقل عدداً، فتأمل. وقد يجاب بأنا لا نسلم أن العبد مخير بل الواجب عليه الجمعة خاصة عند الأذان، كما في الحر حتى يكره له التخلف، كذا في "غاية التحقيق". بثلاثة أيام يعني على الجواب الذي ذكرنا في العبد يخرج. جواب آخر عن اعتراض آخر يرد على الأصل المذكور، وهو أن من قال إن دخلت الدار فعلي صوم سنة، فدخل وهو معسر فهو على قول محمد وأبي حنيفة رحمهما الله مخير بين صوم السنة باعتبار أنه نذر فعليه وفاء النذر، وبين صوم ثلاثة أيام باعتبار أنه كفارة يمينه، فهذا تخير بين القليل والكثير من غير رفق؛ إذ لا سنة بل الرفق في الأقل عدداً متعين. والجواب ما بينه المصنف بقوله: لأنهما أي السنة وصوم ثلاثة أيام حكماً وإن اتفقا صورة؛ لأن صوم السنة قربة مقصودة خالية عن معنى الزجر والعقوبة وصوم الثلاثة كفارة متضمنة معنى العقوبة والزجر، فصح التخير طلباً للرفق عنده، وإليه يشير بقوله: أحدهما قربة إلخ وهذا التخير إنما يتحقق إذا كان التعليق بشرط لا يريد وقوعه كما في قوله المذكور، فإن كان التعليق بشرط يريد وقوعه، مثل أن يقول: إن شفى الله مرضي فعلي كذا، فلا تخير بل الواجب عليه الوفاء بالنذر وهو صوم السنة. وقوله: "وهو معسر" احتراز عن موسر، فإنه لو كان موسراً لا يتعين في حقه التكفير بالصوم، فلا يتحقق التخير بين صوم السنة وبين صوم الثلاثة، فلا يتأتي التخريج. فتأمل فيه إشارة إلى أن الجواب يتم بإثبات الرفق في كل واحد منهما، سواء كانا متحدين أو متغايرين، فلا حاجة إلى إثبات المغايرة. فتدبر. الأصل: وهو التخير إذا لم يتضمن رفقا لا يليق بالعبودية. سنة.
A chapter on 'Azima and Rukhsa. As for the zuhr of the traveler and the resident, they are one, so by choosing between the few and the many, none of the meaning of ease is realized. It is the two rak'ahs. And the zuhr of the resident is four rak'ahs, so one is valid based on the other being built upon it. 'None of the meaning' etc. because ease is determined in the few in number, so reflect. And it may be answered that we do not concede that the slave is given a choice; rather, the Friday prayer is obligatory upon him specifically at the time of the call, as in the free person, so that it is disliked for him to lag behind, as in 'Ghayat al-Tahqiq'. By three days, meaning according to the answer we mentioned in the slave. Another answer to another objection directed at the mentioned principle, which is that whoever says 'If I enter the house, then upon me is a fast of a year', then he enters while he is insolvent, then according to the saying of Muhammad and Abu Hanifa, he is given a choice between fasting a year, considering that it is a vow so he must fulfill the vow, and between fasting three days, considering that it is the expiation of his oath. So this is a choice between the few and the many without ease, since there is no ease in the year, rather ease is determined in the few in number. And the answer is what the author clarified by his saying: because they, i.e., the year and fasting three days, are different in legal status even if they agree in form; because fasting a year is an intended act of worship free from the meaning of deterrence and punishment, while fasting three is an expiation containing the meaning of punishment and deterrence, so the choice is valid seeking ease. And he indicates by his saying: 'one of them is worship, etc.' And this choice is only realized if the suspension is on a condition he does not intend to occur, as in the mentioned statement. If the suspension is on a condition he intends to occur, like saying: 'If Allah cures my sick one, then upon me is such', then there is no choice, rather he must fulfill the vow which is fasting a year. And his saying: 'while he is insolvent' is a caveat excluding the wealthy, because if he were wealthy, expiation by fasting would not be determined for him, so the choice between fasting a year and fasting three days would not be realized, and the derivation would not apply. Reflect on it, indicating that the answer is complete by establishing ease in each of them, whether they are identical or different, so there is no need to establish difference. Contemplate. The principle: it is the choice when it does not include ease that is not befitting for servitude. Year.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the principle of 'azima (strict obligation) and rukhsa (concession/ease) within Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by addressing the case of the zuhr prayer: a traveler prays 2 rak'ahs (qasr) while a resident prays 4. Although both are called 'zuhr', they are treated as one type in terms of the ruling. The issue arises when comparing the traveler's choice to shorten his prayer: he has a choice between 2 and 4? But actually, the traveler is obligated to shorten (qasr) when traveling, so there is no genuine choice that brings ease; the ease is in the fewer number. The author then addresses an apparent objection: if a slave is given a choice in Friday prayer (to attend Friday or pray zuhr), then why not here? The answer clarifies that the slave's choice is between two different things (Friday and zuhr) which are different in nature, so choice brings ease. In contrast, the traveler's two prayers (qasr and full) are essentially the same type, differing only in number, so choosing the longer brings no ease; ease is only in the shorter, so it's determined. The passage then extends this reasoning to a vow: if someone says 'Upon me is a fast of a year if I enter the house' and then enters while insolvent, he has a choice between fasting a year (as a vow) or three days (as expiation for an oath made by the statement). The objection: this is a choice between many and few without ease. The answer: the year's fast is an act of worship (qurba) free of punitive element, while the three days are expiation (kaffara) containing deterrence. They are different in legal status, so choice involves ease (one may choose the easier one). This choice only applies if the condition is something he does not intend to occur; if he intended the occurrence, he must fulfill the vow. Additionally, the choice exists only if he is insolvent (cannot afford other expiation). The text ends with a reflection that the answer works by establishing ease in each option, whether they are identical or different.

Key Terms
العزيمة (al-'azima): الحكم اللازم الذي لم يتغير بسبب عذر
الرخصة (al-rukhsa): الحكم الذي شرع للتخفيف عند وجود عذر
التخير (al-takhyir): الاختيار بين بديلين شرعيين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the traveler's choice between 2 and 4 rak'ahs NOT a genuine rukhsa?
A) Because the traveler is not permitted to pray 4 rak'ahs.
B) Because both options share the same legal reality (zuhr), differing only in number; ease is already in the shorter.
C) Because the traveler must always pray 2 rak'ahs.
D) Because the choice is between two different types of prayer.

Key Takeaway
Takhyir is a genuine rukhsa only when the alternatives differ in legal reality (haqiqa), not merely in quantity.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Preferring Qiyas Over a Non-Faqih Narrator's Report
Explaining the principle of preferring qiyas over a non-faqih narrator's report

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle for preferring qiyas over a non-faqih narrator's report and apply it to the hadith al-musarrah.

Core Idea
A non-faqih's report is set aside for qiyas unless necessity demands otherwise.

This passage explains a key Hanafi usul rule: when a hadith narrated by a non-faqih contradicts qiyas, the Hanafi school gives precedence to qiyas. The author presents the rationale, proofs, and the famous example of hadith al-musarrah, contrasting with the Maliki position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Locate the statement: if a non-faqih narrator's report agrees with qiyas, it is acted upon; if it contradicts, it is left except for necessity.
2
Understand the exception
The exception is darurah (necessity) to keep the door of qiyas open, not the usual fiqh necessity.
Darurah here means if the hadith were accepted, qiyas would be abandoned entirely.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is the Quranic verse (al-Hashr:2) commanding i'tibar, interpreted as qiyas.
Also the reasoning that qiyas is probable in its origin (asl) while khabar is certain in origin but doubtful in transmission.
4
Apply to the example
The hadith al-musarrah fixes a sa' of dates as compensation, but qiyas requires compensation by value.
Since Abu Hurayra (narrator) is not a faqih, the hadith is not acted upon.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Malik accepts the hadith because the narrator is reliable; Hanafis disagree due to lack of fiqh.
This leads to a practical difference in the right of return.

Source Text

قلنا: ولما فرغ من تقسيم الحديث باعتبار قلة رواته وكثرته واتصاله وانفصاله شرع في تقسيمه باعتبار حال الراوي بأنه إما معروف أو مجهول، والمعروف إما معروف بالفقه أو بالعدالة والمجهول على خمسة أنواع. في الاجتهاد كلمة "في" بمعنى اللام والمعنى أن له تقدما على غيره درجة لأجل الاجتهاد. والعبادلة الثلاثة: والعبادلة جمع عبدل، مرحم عبد الله، والمراد بهم عبد الله بن مسعود وعبد الله بن عمر وعبد الله بن عباس، وقيل: عبد الله بن زبير بدل عبد الله بن مسعود وقال الكرماني: العبادلة أربعة: عبد الله بن زبير، وعبد الله بن عباس، وعبد الله بن عمر، وعبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص . اشتهر بالفقه والنظر: مثل أبي بن كعب وأبي الدرداء ما يترك به القياس خلافاً لمالك؛ لأن عنده القياس مقدّم على خبر الواحد إذا خالفه، كما روي أن أبا هريرة لما روى مرفوعاً: "من غسل الميت فليغتسل، ومن حمله فليتوضأ" . الأصل الثاني السننة مثل أبي هريرة وأنس بن مالك ما. فإن وافق حديثه القياس عمل به، وإن خالفه لم يترك إلا للضرورة وانسداد باب الرأي، وذلك مثل حديث أبي هريرة في المصراة.
قالت عائشة: أو ينجس موتى المسلمين؟ وما على رجل لوحمل عوداً . (أخرجه أبو منصور البغدادي في كتابه من طريق محمد بن عمرو بن يحيى بن عبد الرحمن بن حاطب فتأمل. ونحن نقول : القياس محتمل بأصله في كل وصف؛ إذ كل وصف من أوصاف النص يحتمل أن يكون هو المؤثر في الحكم ويحتمل أن لا يكون وخبر الواحد يقين بأصله، وإنما الشبهة في طريق وصوله والاحتمال الثابت في الأصل أقوى من الاحتمال الثابت في الطريق بعد اليقين بالأصل فلا يعارض الخبر.
وانسداد باب الرأي قوله : وانسداد" عطف تفسيري لقوله: "للضرورة"، والمعنى إنما يترك حديث غير الفقيه إذا خالف القياس للضرورة، وهي أنه لو عمل بالحديث وقت المخالفة أيضاً لانسدّ باب القياس من كل وجه، وقد أمر الله تعالى بالقياس بقوله: ﴿فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ﴾ (الحشر : ۲)، والحال أن الراوي غير فقيه، ويحتمل أنه نقل ذلك الحديث بالمعنى؛ لأنه كان شائعاً ذائعا فيهم فيمكن أنه أخطأ فيه، ولم يدرك مراد رسول الله الله فحينئذ كيف يعتمد على قوله ويترك به القياس الثابت بقوله تعالى فلهذه الضرورة تركنا هذا الحديث وعملنا بالقياس حديث أبي هريرة الله وهو ما روى أبو هريرة أن النبي الله قال: "لا تصروا الإبل والغنم فمن ابتاعها بعد ذلك فهو بخير النظرين بعد أن يحلبها، إن رضيها أمسكها وإن سخطها ردّها وصاعاً من تمر". رواه مسلم[رقم:٣٨١٥]وأبو داود، [رقم:٣٤٤٣] والتصرية تفعيل من الصرعى، وهو في اللغة الجمع، يقال: صرّيت الماء وصريته إذا جمعته والمراد به في الحديث جمع اللبن في الضرع بالشد وترك الحلب مدة ليحلب المشتري بعد ذلك، فيغتر بكثرة لبنه ويشريه بثمن غال.
فهذا الحديث مخالف للقياس من كل وجه؛ لأن القياس في ضمان العدوانات والبياعات كلها أن يكون مقدراً بالمثل في المثلي، وبالقيمة في ذوات القيم، فضمان اللبن المشروب إما باللبن مثله وإما بالقيمة، ولو كان التمر قيمة فيه فينبغي أن يكون بحسب اللبن، لا أنه يجب صاع التمر قل اللبن أو كثر ، فإذا لم يعمل بالحديث لكونه مخالفاً للقياس فليس للمشترى ولاية الردّ بسبب التصرية من غير شرط؛ لأن البيع يقتضي سلامة المبيع، وبقلة اللبن لاتفوت وصف السلامة؛ لأن اللبن ،ثمرة، وبعدمها لا ينعدم وصف السلامة، فبقلتها ،أولى، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له.
* فتأمل : إشارة إلى أنه لا يحسن إيراد هذه الرواية كأن أبا هريرة لم يكن مجتهداً.
We say: When he finished dividing the hadith by the number of narrators and continuity and discontinuity, he began dividing it by the condition of the narrator: that he is either known or unknown. The known is either known for fiqh or for 'adalah, and the unknown is of five types. 'Fi al-ijtihad' – the word 'fi' means 'lam', meaning he has precedence over others in rank due to ijtihad. The three Abdullahs: 'al-`Abadilah' is plural of `Abdullah; what is meant are `Abdullah ibn Mas`ud, `Abdullah ibn `Umar, and `Abdullah ibn `Abbas; also said: `Abdullah ibn Zubayr instead of `Abdullah ibn Mas`ud. Al-Kirmani said: the `Abadilah are four: `Abdullah ibn Zubayr, `Abdullah ibn `Abbas, `Abdullah ibn `Umar, and `Abdullah ibn `Amr ibn al-`As. 'Famous for fiqh and insight' like Ubayy ibn Ka`b and Abu al-Darda' – his (report) is abandoned for qiyas, contrary to Malik, because with him qiyas is given precedence over khabar al-wahid if it contradicts it, as narrated that when Abu Hurayra narrated the marfu` hadith: 'Whoever washes the dead should take a bath, and whoever carries him should perform wudu'... (narration references) and Ahmad said: nothing authentic in this chapter. = [Page 142] Chapter of Sunnah 121 The second source is the Sunnah like Abu Hurayra and Anas ibn Malik. If his hadith agrees with qiyas, it is acted upon; if it contradicts it, it is not abandoned except for necessity and the closing of the door of opinion, such as the hadith of Abu Hurayra about al-musarrah. Aisha said: 'Do the dead of the Muslims become impure? What is there upon a man if he carries a piece of wood?' (Abu Mansur al-Baghdadi narrated it in his book via Muhammad ibn `Amr ibn Yahya ibn `Abd al-Rahman ibn Hatib, so reflect.) And we say: Qiyas is probable in its origin in every attribute; for every attribute of the text may be the effective cause in the ruling or may not be. And khabar al-wahid is certain in its origin; only the doubt is in its chain of transmission. The probability established in the origin (qiyas) is stronger than the probability established in the chain after certainty of the origin, so it does not oppose the report. 'And the closing of the door of opinion' – his statement 'wa-insidad' is an explanatory conjunction of his statement 'li-darurah', meaning that the hadith of the non-faqih is only left for qiyas due to necessity, which is that if one acted upon the hadith at the time of contradiction, the door of qiyas would be closed entirely, while Allah has commanded qiyas by His saying: 'So take heed, O people of vision' (al-Hashr:2). And the narrator is not a faqih, and it is possible that he transmitted the hadith by meaning because it was widespread among them, so he may have erred in it and not grasped the intention of the Messenger of Allah. So how then can his word be relied upon and qiyas established by Allah's word be abandoned? Due to this necessity we have left this hadith and acted upon qiyas. The hadith of Abu Hurayra: the Prophet said: 'Do not tie up the udders of camels and sheep. He who buys them after that has the choice after milking them: if he is pleased he keeps them, and if he is displeased he returns them along with a sa` of dates.' Narrated by Muslim [3815] and Abu Dawud [3443]. And 'tasriyah' is taf`il from 'sarâ' meaning in language to collect; the intent in the hadith is collecting milk in the udder by tying and leaving milking for a period so that the buyer milks later and is deceived by its abundance and buys it at a high price. So this hadith contradicts qiyas in every respect because the qiyas regarding guarantees and sales is that it is measured by the like in fungible goods and by value in non-fungibles. So the guarantee of the drunk milk is either by milk like it or by value. If dates were the value, it should be proportionate to the milk, not that a sa` of dates is obligatory whether the milk is little or much. So when the hadith is not acted upon because it contradicts qiyas, the buyer does not have the right of return due to tasriyah without a condition, because the sale requires soundness of the sold item, and the lack of milk does not negate the attribute of soundness, because milk is a product, and by its absence the attribute of soundness is not absent, so by its being little even more so. This is the view of Abu Hanifah. * 'So reflect' is an indication that it is not proper to cite this narration as if Abu Hurayra were not a mujtahid.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the discussion on narrators, now focusing on the non-faqih narrator. It first returns to the classification and clarifies the term 'fi al-ijtihad' and the identity of the three/four Abdullahs. Then it addresses the ruling on the report of a non-faqih narrator like Abu Hurayra and Anas: if it agrees with qiyas, it is acted upon; if it contradicts, it is abandoned only for necessity (darurah) and to keep the door of qiyas open. The author then provides the example of the hadith al-musarrah, which contradicts qiyas in sales. According to qiyas, compensation should be based on the value of the milk, but the hadith specifies a fixed sa' of dates. Since the narrator (Abu Hurayra) is not considered a faqih mujtahid, the Hanafis do not act upon this hadith and instead follow qiyas, giving the buyer no right of return for the defect of tasriyah. The passage includes a subtle critique that Abu Hurayra may not be considered a mujtahid, hence his report is not preferred over qiyas.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning: deriving the ruling of a new case from an original case due to a shared effective cause.
الضرورة (al-ḍarūrah): Necessity: the only condition under which the report of a non-faqih may be preferred over qiyas, to avoid completely closing the door of qiyas.
التصرية (al-taṣriyah): The act of tying the udders of an animal to accumulate milk in order to deceive a buyer.
صاع من تمر (ṣāʿ min tamr): A specific measure of dates, approximately 3 kg, prescribed in the hadith as compensation for the drunk milk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis not act upon the hadith al-musarrah (about tying udders) despite it being authentic?
A) Because the narrator Abu Hurayrah is not considered trustworthy
B) Because the hadith contradicts qiyas and the narrator is not a faqih
C) Because they do not accept khabar al-wahid as hujjah
D) Because the hadith is abrogated

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers qiyas over the report of a non-faqih narrator to maintain the primacy of analogical reasoning commanded by the Qur'an.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Resolving Conflicting Sunnahs: The Hanafi Hierarchy and Taqrir al-Usul
Presents rule for conflicting sunnahs and applies to donkey's water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy for resolving conflict between two sunnah evidences and identify when taqrir al-usul (settling principles) is invoked.

Core Idea
When two sunnahs conflict, resort first to qiyas, then Companion sayings; if still unresolved, settle each thing on its original ruling.

When two hadiths appear contradictory, the mujtahid cannot simply pick the one he prefers. The Hanafi school provides a clear hierarchy: first analogical reasoning (qiyas), then the sayings of the Companions, and if these too fail, we return each matter to its original legal state. This lesson explores that hierarchy through two key examples: the eclipse prayer and the donkey's leftover water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting sunnahs
Start by isolating the two hadiths that appear to contradict each other. In the eclipse prayer example, one hadith reports one rukuʿ per rakʿah, another reports four rukuʿ per two rakʿahs.
Both are sunnahs, so they are equal in rank.
2
Apply the first resort: qiyas
The sunnahs cancel each other, so we look to the next evidence in the hierarchy: qiyas. Analogize the eclipse prayer to normal obligatory prayers, which have one rukuʿ per rakʿah. This resolves the conflict in favor of the hadith with one rukuʿ.
If qiyas itself conflicts (as in the donkey's water case), move to the next step.
3
If qiyas fails, apply second resort: Companion sayings
If qiyas is inconclusive, consult the sayings of the Companions. In the donkey's water case, Companion opinions conflict (Ibn Umar says impure, Ibn Abbas says pure), so this level also fails.
Some scholars reverse the order of qiyas and Companion sayings; the Hanafi view prioritizes qiyas.
4
Resort to taqrir al-usul (settling principles)
When all higher evidences are inconclusive, preserve the original legal ruling. Water is originally pure, so donkey's leftover water remains pure. However, due to conflict, its purifying power is doubtful, so tayammum must be added to wudu.
This balances the original purity of water with the original impurity of the human.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence of the hierarchy: in the eclipse prayer, the Hanafi view performs two rakʿahs with one rukuʿ each, while the opposing view (prioritizing Aisha's hadith) performs four rukuʿ. This difference arises from the order of resort.
This shows how usul principles directly affect fiqh rulings.

Source Text
