فصل في المعارضة
وبين السنتين المصير إلى القياس وأقوال الصحابة له على الترتيب في الحجج إن أمكن؛
لأن التعارض لما ثبت بين الحجتين تساقطتا لاندفاع كل واحدة منهما بالأخرى، فيجب
الحجتان جميعا
المصير إلى ما بعدهما من الحجة، وعند تعذر المصير إليه يجب تقرير الأصول،
[ابن ماجة، رقم: ٨٤٧] وروى ابن ماجة عن جابر قال قال رسول الله : " من كان له إمام فقراءة الإمام له قراءة". [ابن ماجة، رقم ٨٥٠] وروى محمد في موطاه على شرط الشيخين عن جابر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "من صلى خلف الإمام فإن قراءة الإمام قراءة له. [موطأ محمد، رقم: ۱۱۷] وكذا روى جماعة عن أبي حنيفة ليه مرفوعاً على شرط الشيخين هذا الحديث، وإذا ثبت هذا فلا تنظر إلى ما قيل إنه لا بدّ من قراءة الفاتحة خلف الإمام،
كما روى أبو داود وغيره عن محمد بن إسحاق؛ لأنه ضعيف ضعفه أحمد بن حنبل وغيره من كبار المحدثين. وبين السنتين إلخ أي إذا وقع التعارض بين السنتين يصار إلى القياس أولاً، ثم إلى أقوال الصحابة له على ما قيل، وقال بعضهم على العكس، وقيل: يقدّم أقوال الصحابة لله على القياس فيما لايدرك بالقياس، والقياس مقدّم فيما يدرك به.
على الترتيب إلخ: متعلّق بالمجموع، فالمعنى حكم المعارضة بين الآيتين المصير إلى السنة وبين السنتين المصير إلى القياس وأقوال الصحابة لكن على الترتيب الثابت بين الحجج حتى يقدّم أقوال الصحابة على القياس، ويحتمل وجهاً آخر أيضاً، فمثاله ماروى أبو داود والترمذي في الشمائل والنسائي عن عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص أنه قال: انكسفت الشمس على عهد رسول الله الله فقام رسول الله الله لم يكد يركع، ثم ركع فلم يكد يرفع، ثم رفع فلم يكد يسجد ، ثم سجد فلم يكد يرفع ثم رفع فلم يكد يسجد ، ثم سجد فلم يكد يرفع ، ثم رفع وفعل في الركعة الأخرى مثل ذلك الحديث. فهذا يدلّ على أنه عليه السلام صلّى ركعتين، كل ركعة . بركوع وسجدتين وروت عائشة لهما أنه عليه السلام صلاها بأربع ركوعات وأربع سجدات، كما أخرجه أبو داود وغيره، فيتعارضان فيصار إلى القياس ،بعده، وهو الاعتبار بسائر الصلوات.
نفي
إن أمكن المصير على الوجه المذكور، ثم استدلّ على قوله: وحكم المعارضة الخ" بقوله: لأن إلخ. بعدهما: أي بعد الحجتين المتعارضتين من الحجة الأخرى التي لا تكون من جنسهما، كما لو وقع التعارض بين الآيتين، فيصار إلى السنة التي هي حجة أخرى ليست من جنسهما، وذلك لأنها لو كانت من جنسهما لثبت الترجيح بكثرة الأدلة، وذلك غير جائز كما أشرنا إليه سابقاً إليه أي إلى ما بعدهما من الحجة بأن تعارضت السنتان وأقوال الصحابة والقياس أيضا، و لم يوجد دليل بعده فحينئذ يجب إلخ. تقرير الأصول: أي إثبات كل
شيء على أصله بأن يقروا الحكم على ما كان عليه ورود الدليلين.

باب السنة
فصل في المعارضة
كما في سؤر الحمار لما تعارضت الدلائل ولم يصلح القياس شاهداً؛ لأنه لا يصلح
أي القياس
لنصب الحكم ابتداءً قيل: إن الماء عُرف طاهراً في الأصل فلايتنجس بالتعارض
و لم يزل به الحدث، فوجب ضمُّ التيمم إليه، وسمّي مشكوكاً. أي بذلك الماء
أي سؤر الحمار
لما تعارضت الدلائل: لأنه روى البخاري وغيره أن النبي الهلال هل هي عن لحوم الحمر الأهلية، وأذن في لحموم الخيل نهى يوم خيبر. وروى غالب بن فهر أنه قال الرسول الله له: لم يبق من مالي إلا حميرات، فقال: كل من سمين مالك. أخرجه الطحاوي في معاني الآثار بطرق متنوعة [رقم: ٥٥٢٠ ] . فإذا وقع التعارض في لحومها وقع الاشتباه في سؤرها؛ لأنه متولّد من اللحم، وأقوال الصحابة عليهم أيضاً متعارضة في تلك المسألة، فإن ابن عمر كان يكره التوضئ بسؤر الحمار والبغل، ويقول: إنه رجس وابن عباس كان يقول : إن الحمار يأكل القت والتبن، فسؤره طاهر، لا بأس بالتوضئ به كذا في "غاية التحقيق". شاهداً : أي دليلا لواحد منهما. والحاصل أن القياسين أيضا متعارضان؛ لأن السؤر إذا يقاس على العرق يحكم بطهارته؛ لأن العرق طاهر في الرواية الظاهرة، وإذا يقاس على اللبن يحكم بنجاسته؛ لأن اللبن نجس في أصح الروايتين، وقد يقال: لا يمكن قياسه على سؤر الكلب في النجاسة بجامع التولد من اللحم؛ لكون الضرورة في الحمار دون الكلب، وكذا لايمكن قياسه على سؤر الهرة ليكون طاهراً لكون الضرورة في الهرة أكثر مما في الحمار. ابتداءً: أي بغير العلة الثابتة المشتركة بين الأصل والفرع، أي لو قلنا: إنه نجس أو طاهر قياساً على سؤر الكلب أو الهرة يلزم إثبات الحكم بالقياس ابتداءً أي بغير علة، أما على تقدير الأول فلأن القياسين إذا تعارضا تساقط علتهما، فبقي القياس بغير علة، وأما على تقدير الثاني فظاهر، وإثبات الحكم بالقياس بدون العلة غير جائز. قيل: جواب لقوله: "لما تعارضت . الماء الذي هو سؤر الحمار. فلايتنجس بخلط لعاب الحمار، فإن نجاسته مشكوكة وطهارة الماء يقينية بالتعارض: الواقع بين طهارته ونجاسته، فوجب استعماله لكونه طاهراً في الأصل الحدث: أي حدث الآدمي إذا توضأ به؛ لكون الآدمي محدثاً في الأصل إليه أي إلى الوضوء. فإن قيل: إذا قرّرتم كل شيء على أصله، فوجب عليكم أن تقولوا: إن الماء مطهر كما هو طاهر في أصله، فإذا كان مطهراً فما الحاجة إلى ضمّ التيمم إليه؟ قلتُ: أبقيناه على أصل واحد وهو كونه طاهراً؛ ليمكن تقرير الآدمي على أصله؛ إذ لو أبقيناه على أصله الآخر أيضاً لفات أصل الآدمي ،الحدث، فعملنا بهما مهما أمكن. مشكوكاً وفي بعض النسخ مشكلاً، أي إنما سمى سؤر الحمار مشكوكاً
وهو
أو مشكلاً لأجل التعارض، فإذا نظرنا إلى أدلة توجب كونه طاهراً حكمنا بطهارته كسائر المياه، وإذا نظرنا إلى أدلة توجب كونه نجسا حكمنا بنجاسته، فوقع الشك والإشكال فيه لهذا الوجه، لا لأجل أن حكمه مجهول بل
Chapter of Sunnah. Section on Contradiction. And between two sunnahs, resort to qiyas and the sayings of the Companions — on the order of evidences — if possible. Because when contradiction is established between two proofs, they both fall away due to each repelling the other, so it is necessary to resort to the proof that comes after them both. And when resort to it is impossible, then it becomes necessary to settle the principles. Ibn Majah narrated from Jabir that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the imam is recitation for him.' And Muhammad narrated in his Muwatta' on the condition of the two Shaykhs from Jabir from the Prophet: 'Whoever prays behind an imam, the recitation of the imam is recitation for him.' Similarly, a group narrated from Abu Hanifa, raised to the Prophet on the condition of the two Shaykhs, this hadith. And when this is established, then do not look at what was said that one must recite al-Fatiha behind the imam, as narrated by Abu Dawud and others from Muhammad ibn Ishaq, because it is weak — Ahmad ibn Hanbal and others from the major hadith scholars declared it weak. 'And between two sunnahs' etc. means: if conflict occurs between two sunnahs, one resorts first to qiyas, then to the sayings of the Companions — as is said. And some said the opposite. And it was said: the sayings of the Companions are given precedence over qiyas in matters not perceivable by qiyas, and qiyas is given precedence in matters perceivable by it. 'On the order' etc.: it is attached to the whole, so the meaning is: the ruling of contradiction between two verses is to resort to sunnah, and between two sunnahs is to resort to qiyas and the sayings of the Companions, but on the established order among evidences, such that the sayings of the Companions are given precedence over qiyas. And another aspect is also possible. Its example is what Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi in al-Shama'il, and al-Nasa'i narrated from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr ibn al-'As that he said: The sun eclipsed during the time of the Messenger of Allah, so the Messenger of Allah stood up and hardly bowed, then he bowed and hardly raised his head, then he raised and hardly prostrated, then he prostrated and hardly raised his head, then he raised and hardly prostrated, then he prostrated and hardly raised his head, then he raised and did likewise in the other rak'ah. This indicates that he prayed two rak'ahs, each rak'ah with one bowing and two prostrations. And 'A'ishah narrated that he prayed it with four bowings and four prostrations, as recorded by Abu Dawud and others. So they contradict, and one resorts to qiyas after it, which is analogy with other prayers. 'If possible' refers to resorting in the mentioned manner. Then he argued for his saying 'and the ruling of contradiction etc.' by saying 'because' etc. 'After them both' means after the two contradictory proofs, from the other proof which is not of their kind, as when contradiction occurs between two verses, then one resorts to sunnah which is another proof not of their kind. Because if it were of their kind, then preponderance would be established by the abundance of evidences, and that is not permissible, as we pointed out earlier. 'To it' means to what is after them both of proof, meaning if there is contradiction between two sunnahs, and the sayings of the Companions and qiyas as well, and no proof exists after them, then it becomes necessary to settle the principles. 'Settling the principles' means establishing each thing upon its original state, by settling the ruling as it was before the arrival of the two proofs. As in the case of the donkey's leftover water, when the evidences conflicted and qiyas was not suitable as a witness; because qiyas is not suitable for establishing a ruling initially. It was said: water is known to be pure originally, so it does not become impure due to conflict, and it does not remove ritual impurity, so it became necessary to combine tayammum with it, and it is called doubtful. 'That water' means the donkey's leftover water. 'When the evidences conflicted' because al-Bukhari and others narrated that the Prophet forbade eating the flesh of domestic donkeys and permitted horses' flesh on the day of Khaybar. And Ghalib ibn Fahd narrated that the Messenger of Allah said: 'I have nothing left of my property but some little donkeys, so eat from the fat of your property.' Recorded by al-Tahawi in Ma'ani al-Athar with various chains. So when conflict occurred concerning their flesh, confusion occurred concerning their leftover water, because it is derived from the flesh. And the sayings of the Companions also conflicted in this issue: Ibn 'Umar disliked performing wudu with the leftover water of donkey and mule, saying it is impure; while Ibn 'Abbas said: The donkey eats green fodder and hay, so its leftover water is pure, there is no harm in performing wudu with it. Thus in Ghayat al-Tahqiq. 'As a witness' means a proof for one of them. The summary is that the two qiyases also conflict: because if the leftover water is analogized to sweat, it is ruled pure, because sweat is pure in the apparent narration; and if analogized to milk, it is ruled impure, because milk is impure in the most authentic of the two narrations. And it may be said: It cannot be analogized to dog's leftover water in impurity due to commonality of being derived from flesh, because necessity in the donkey is less than in the dog; similarly, it cannot be analogized to cat's leftover water to be pure, because necessity for the cat is greater than for the donkey. 'Initially' means without an established common cause between the original and the branch. That is, if we say it is impure or pure by analogy to dog's or cat's leftover water, it results in establishing the ruling by qiyas initially, i.e. without a cause. As for the first estimation, because when two qiyases conflict, their causes fall away, leaving qiyas without cause; and as for the second estimation, it is apparent. And establishing a ruling by qiyas without a cause is not permissible. 'It was said' is a response to his saying 'when they conflicted'. The water which is the donkey's leftover water does not become impure by mixing with the donkey's saliva, because its impurity is doubtful and the purity of water is certain due to the conflict occurring between its purity and impurity. So it became necessary to use it because it is pure originally. 'Ritual impurity' means the impurity of a human if he performs wudu with it, because the human is originally impure. 'To it' means to wudu. If it is said: When you settle each thing on its original state, then you must say that the water is purifying as it is pure originally. So if it is purifying, what need is there to combine tayammum with it? I say: We kept it on one original state, which is its purity, so that the human can be settled on his original state; for if we kept it on its other original state as well, the original state of the human (impurity) would be lost. So we acted upon both as much as possible. 'Doubtful' and in some copies 'problematic' — meaning the donkey's leftover water is called doubtful or problematic because of the conflict. When we look at evidences that require it to be pure, we rule it pure like other waters; and when we look at evidences that require it to be impure, we rule it impure. So doubt and confusion arose concerning it for this reason, not because its ruling is unknown. Rather,
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage from the Chapter of Sunnah discusses the Hanafi usul rule for resolving conflict between two sunnah texts. The author, following classical Hanafi methodology, states that when two sunnahs (hadiths) appear contradictory, we first resort to qiyas (analogical deduction) and then to the sayings of the Companions (aqwal al-sahaba) — in that order. This is a specific application of the general principle that when two evidences of equal rank conflict, they are deemed to cancel each other out, and we must look to the next available evidence in the hierarchy. The hadith cited about the imam's recitation sufficing for the follower is introduced to illustrate the authoritative weight of a sound hadith against weaker narrations that require recitation of al-Fatiha behind an imam. Then, the author provides a concrete example: the solar eclipse prayer. There are two conflicting reports: one from Abdullah ibn Amr indicating two rak'ahs with one ruku' each (like normal prayer), and another from Aisha indicating four ruku' in two rak'ahs. Since these are both sunnahs, they conflict, so we resort to qiyas: we analogize the eclipse prayer to other prayers (which have one ruku' per rak'ah), thus preferring the report of two ruku' total. The discussion then moves to a more complex case: the leftover water (su'r) of a donkey. Here, multiple evidences conflict: hadith about donkey meat, conflicting Companion opinions, and conflicting analogies (to sweat vs. milk). Since qiyas fails to provide a clear cause (the analogies cancel each other out), and no stronger evidence is available, the scholar must 'settle the principles' (taqrir al-usul): each thing is kept on its original ruling. Water is originally pure, so the donkey's leftover water remains pure. However, because of the conflicting evidences, its purifying capability is doubted; it can be used for wudu but not completely remove impurity, so tayammum must be added. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of resolving conflicting evidence by preserving original legal states when no preferred ruling can be deduced.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'āruḍ): Conflict or contradiction between two evidences that are equal in strength, leading to their cancellation
سؤر الحمار (su'r al-ḥimār): The leftover water from which a donkey has drunk
تقرير الأصول (taqrīr al-uṣūl): Settling each thing upon its original legal ruling when no decisive evidence is available

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi method presented, what should one do when two sunnahs conflict?
A) Choose the hadith with more narrators.
B) Resort to qiyas, then Companion sayings, then settle principles.
C) Combine the two hadiths by interpreting one in light of the other.
D) Suspend ruling until further evidence is found.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul hierarchy for conflicting sunnahs is: qiyas first, then Companion sayings, and failing that, settle each thing on its original ruling (taqrir al-usul).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Conflicting Qiyas and the Necessity of Taharry
Clarifies that conflicting qiyas do not fall away; the mujtahid must choose with taharry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that conflicting qiyas do not fall away, and identify when taharry is required and when conflict is not genuine.

Core Idea
Conflicting qiyas do not cancel; the mujtahid must choose with taḥarry, guided by firāsa.

When two analogical proofs (qiyas) conflict in the same case, a critical question arises: does the conflict void both? The Hanafi school answers decisively: no. The proofs remain valid, and the mujtahid must investigate his heart (taḥarry) to give precedence to one. This lesson unpacks why istiṣḥāb is not the default and how to define genuine conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State that conflicting qiyas do not fall away, and the mujtahid must choose one with taḥarry.
2
Understand the reasoning
Analogical proof retains its probative force even if the mujtahid errs; thus it is better to act on a qiyas than on istiṣḥāb, which is not a primary proof.
3
Distinguish from the Shafi'i view
Recognize that al-Shafi'i allows arbitrary choice without investigation, while Hanafis require taḥarry.
4
Define genuine conflict
True mu'arada only occurs between equal proofs; if one is stronger, conflict does not arise.
5
Apply the definition
Examples: no conflict between mutawatir and ahad, or between general and specific.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا وقع التعارض بين القياسين لم يسقطا بالتعارض ليجب العمل بالحال، بل يعمل المجتهد بأيهما شاء بشهادة قلبه؛ لأن القياس حجة يعمل به سواء أصاب المجتهد الحق به أو أخطأ ، فكان العمل بأحدهما وهو حجة اطمأن قلبه إليها بنور الفراسة أولى من العمل بالحال، ثم التعارض إنما يتحقق بين الحجتين بإيجاب كل واحد منهما هو معلوم، وهو وجوب التوضئ وضمّ التيمم إليه. إذا وقع التعارض إلخ: أي إذا وقع التعارض بين القياسين لا نقول بتساقطهما؛ لأنه يضطرّ حينئذ إلى دليل شرعي يعرف به حكم تلك الحادثة، ولا دليل بعد القياس يصار إليه إلا العمل بالحال، أي بالاستصحاب الذي هو عبارة عن إبقاء الشيء على ما كان قبله لعدم الدليل المزيل، وهو ليس حجة عندنا، وإنما يصار إليه للضرورة كما في سؤر الحمار. بشهادة قلبه أي بالتحري، وهو شرط عندنا خلافاً للشافعي بشه، فإن عنده يعمل بأيهما شاء من غير تحرّ وتفكر، ولذا صار له في مسألة واحدة قولان أو أكثر في زمان واحد، وأما مايروى عن أئمتنا من قولين في مسألة واحدة فهو بحسب الزمانين المختلفين، فأحدهما صحيح والآخر فاسد ثم استدلّ على أنه يجب العمل بأحدهما بالتحري ولا يصار إلى الاستصحاب بقوله : لأن إلخ. أخطأ يعني القياس في حق العمل به حجة، سواء أصاب المجتهد فيه أو أخطأ، فإذا كان القياس حجة في كل حال. بأحدهما : أي بأحد القياسين وقت التعارض وهو أي الحال أن أحدهما حجة في حق العمل إليها: أي إلى الحجة، الجملة صفة الحجة بنور الفراسة: متعلق بقوله : "اطمأن". من العمل بالحال: حاصله العمل بأحد القياسين عند التعارض أولى من العمل بالحال؛ لأن القياس (سواء كان المجتهد فيه مخطئاً أو مصيباً) حجة، وعند التعارض لا يزول حجيته فحينئذ لوعمل بأحدهما بغير التحرّي كان العمل به أولى من العمل بالحال الذي ليس بحجة، فإذا كان العمل به بنور الفراسة أي بالتحرّي كان أولى من الأولى، فلذا يعمل بأحدهما ولا يعمل بالحال، والفراسة نظر القلب بنور يقع فيه، وفي الصحاح الفراسة بالكسر اسم من قولك: تفرّست فيه خيراً أي أبصرتُ وعلمت. ولما فرغ عن حكم المعارضة شرع في ركنها وشرطها. بين الحجتين المتساويتين، لا مزيّة لأحدهما على الآخر في الذات والصفة وهذا يشير إلى ركن المعارضة، فعلى هذا لا يتحقق بين المشهور والآحاد والمتواتر من الأحاديث، وبين العام المخصوص البعض والخاص من الكتاب معارضة حقيقة؛ لأن أحدهما فوق الآخر في الذات، وكذا لا يتحقق بين المفسّر والمحكم والإشارة والعبارة من الكتاب معارضة أصلاً لعدم المساواة في الوصف.
As for when conflict occurs between two analogies, they do not fall away due to conflict, necessitating resorting to the current state (al-hal). Rather, the mujtahid may act upon whichever of the two he wishes, based on the testimony of his heart. Because analogy is a proof that is acted upon, whether the mujtahid hits the truth or errs. So acting upon one of them, while it is a proof that his heart is at ease with through the light of discernment (firasa), is more appropriate than acting upon the current state. Then, conflict is only realized between two proofs such that each necessitates something known, which is the obligation of wudu and attaching tayammum to it. 'When conflict occurs etc.': i.e., when conflict occurs between two analogies, we do not say they cancel each other out, because that would then require a legal proof to know the ruling of that incident, and there is no proof after analogy except acting upon the current state, i.e., istishab, which is keeping something as it was before due to the absence of a removing proof. And it is not a proof according to us; rather, it is resorted to only out of necessity, as in the case of the donkey's leftover water. 'By the testimony of his heart' means by investigation (taharry), and it is a condition according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, for according to him he may act upon whichever he wishes without investigation and reflection. Therefore, he may have two or more opinions on a single issue at one time. As for what is narrated from our imams of two opinions on a single issue, it is according to different times, so one is correct and the other is invalid. Then he argues that it is obligatory to act upon one of them by investigation and not to resort to istishab, by his saying: 'because...'. 'Errs' means analogy is a proof with respect to acting upon it, whether the mujtahid hits the truth or errs. So when analogy is a proof in any case. 'Upon one of them': i.e., upon one of the two analogies at the time of conflict, and the state (al-hal) is that one of them is a proof with respect to action. 'To it': i.e., to the proof; the clause is a description of the proof. 'By the light of discernment': attached to his saying 'is at ease'. 'Than acting upon the current state': its upshot is that acting upon one of the two analogies at the time of conflict is more appropriate than acting upon the current state; because analogy (whether the mujtahid errs or hits) is a proof, and at the time of conflict its probative value does not disappear. So if he were to act upon one of them without investigation, that action would be more appropriate than acting upon the current state, which is not a proof. And if he acts upon it by the light of discernment, i.e., by investigation, that is more appropriate than the first. Therefore, he acts upon one of them and does not act upon the current state. And 'firasa' is the heart's viewing by a light that settles in it. In al-Sihah, 'firasa' (with kasra) is a noun from your saying 'tafarrastu fihi khayran', meaning I perceived and knew. When he finished discussing the ruling of conflict, he began discussing its pillar and condition. 'Between two equal proofs, with no superiority of one over the other in essence and attribute'—this points to the pillar of conflict. According to this, conflict is not realized between the mashhur and the ahad, nor between the mutawatir and ahad hadiths, nor between the general that has been partially specified and the specific from the Book, because one is superior to the other in essence. Similarly, conflict is not realized between the mufassar and the muhkam, nor between the ishara and the ibara of the Book, because of lack of equality in description.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This section lays down the Hanafi rule for dealing with conflicting analogical proofs (qiyas). The author emphatically states that conflicting qiyas do not cancel each other out. Instead, the mujtahid must engage in 'taharry' (investigation of the heart) to determine which analogy is more likely correct, based on inner conviction and the light of discernment (firasa). This is because qiyas retains its probative value even if the mujtahid errs; it is a valid proof in itself. Resorting to 'al-hal' (istishab) is only permissible when no other proof exists, as in the earlier example of the donkey's water. The text then distinguishes the Hanafi position from that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who, according to the author, allows the mujtahid to choose any one of the conflicting proofs without investigation, which can lead to multiple contradictory opinions on the same matter at the same time. In contrast, Hanafi scholars hold that a mujtahid may have two opinions only if they correspond to different time periods; otherwise, one is correct and the other erroneous. Finally, the passage defines the essential condition for true conflict (mu'arada): the two proofs must be equal in rank and strength (in essence and attribute). Thus, conflict does not arise between a stronger and a weaker proof (e.g., mutawatir vs. ahad, or general vs. specific), because one overrides the other by virtue of its inherent superiority.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharry): Investigation of the heart to determine which of conflicting proofs is more likely correct, based on inner conviction and insight.
الفراسة (al-firasa): The light of discernment in the heart that guides the mujtahid to the correct proof.
الاستصحاب (al-istishab): Presumption of continuity of the previous state; in Hanafi usul, it is not a primary proof but resorted to only when no other proof is available.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a mujtahid do when two analogical proofs (qiyas) conflict?
A) Abandon both and resort to istishab (presumption of continuity).
B) Perform taharry (investigation of the heart) and act upon the one he finds more convincing.
C) Arbitrarily choose one without any investigation.
D) Wait for a new revelation or textual evidence.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, conflicting qiyas do not fall away; the mujtahid must perform taharry to select one, and istishab is only a last resort.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Rule of Conflicting Qiyas and the Duty of Taharrī
Rules for handling conflicting analogies and conditions for true conflict

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for conflicting qiyas by stating that they do not cancel, and identify the conditions for true conflict (ta'arud).

Core Idea
Conflicting qiyas do not cancel; the mujtahid must choose by inner conviction (taharrī), not fall back to istishab.

When two analogical deductions (qiyas) conflict in a legal issue, a common misconception is that both become invalid. The Hanafi school teaches otherwise: each qiyas retains its authority as a proof (hujja), and the mujtahid must exert personal ijtihad (taharrī) to select the stronger one. This lesson unpacks the rule, its conditions, and its contrast with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on conflicting qiyas
Identify the Hanafi rule: when two qiyas conflict, they do not cancel each other. The mujtahid is not forced to fall back to istishab (status quo). Instead, he must choose one of the qiyas by taharrī (inner conviction).
This rule is based on the principle that qiyas remains a hujja (legal proof) even if the mujtahid errs in its application.
2
Define the pillar (rukn) of ta'arud
The rukn of conflict is the equality of the two proofs in strength (quwwa) both in essence (dhat) and attribute (sifa). Without this equality, there is no true conflict.
For example, a mutawatir text and an ahad hadith do not conflict meaningfully because they are unequal in strength.
3
List the conditions (shurut) for true conflict
The shurut are: (1) unity of time, (2) unity of place/situation, (3) contradictory rulings (one commands, the other forbids the same act), and (4) equality in strength as per the rukn.
If rulings differ by time or place, there is no conflict; e.g., wine was halal initially then haram later.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school allows the mujtahid to choose arbitrarily between conflicting proofs without taharrī, whereas the Hanafi school requires taharrī as a condition for valid ijtihad.
The Hanafi view insists that without taharrī, the mujtahid's choice is not grounded in evidence, potentially leading to multiple contradictory opinions in the same time.
5
Apply the rule to a hypothetical scenario
Given two qiyas of equal strength that lead to opposite rulings on the same case, the mujtahid must engage in taharrī—reflecting on the evidence and using inner insight (firasa)—to determine which qiyas is more likely correct. He cannot simply pick any or resort to istishab.
This ensures that the chosen ruling is based on a deliberate weighing of proofs.

Chapter of Sunnah, Section on Conflict. If two analogies conflict: And when conflict occurs between two analogies, they do not fall due to conflict necessitating action by the current state. Rather, the mujtahid acts with whichever he wishes by the testimony of his heart, because analogy is a proof by which one acts whether the mujtahid hits the truth or misses. Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Usul al-Fiqh explains the Hanafi rule for when two analogical deductions (qiyas) conflict. The author first establishes that conflicting qiyas do not cancel each other out, so the mujtahid is not forced to fall back on istishab (presumption of continuity). Instead, he must exercise taharrī (personal ijtihad based on inner conviction) to choose one of the two analogies, because qiyas retains its authority as a proof even if mistaken in reality. The text contrasts this with the Shafi'i position, where the mujtahid may choose arbitrarily without taharrī. The commentary then clarifies the conditions for true conflict (ta'arud): the two proofs must be equal in strength (rkn), and they must require opposite rulings in the same time and place (shart). Examples illustrate that differences in time or place, or non-contradictory rulings, do not constitute true conflict. Finally, the commentator summarizes that the pillar of conflict is mutual opposition of two proofs, and its condition is unity of time and place.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction as a legal proof; it is a hujja even if the mujtahid errs in its application.
التعارض (al-ta'arud): Apparent conflict between two evidences each requiring an opposite ruling in the same time and place, with equal strength.
التحري (al-taharrī): The mujtahid's effort to determine which conflicting evidence is more likely based on inner conviction and insight (firasa).
الاستصحاب (al-istishab): Continuation of a previous legal status due to absence of evidence to change it.
الركن (al-rukn): The essential element of conflict: equality of the two evidences in strength (in essence and attribute).

Preponderance by Number and Quality: Groups vs. Individuals
Critiquing preponderance by number and social qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on preponderance by number and qualities and apply the analogy to testimony to evaluate conflicting reports.

Core Idea
Preponderance by number or gender is only valid for groups, not individuals—analogy to testimony.

When two equally evidence-based reports conflict, we need a method to prefer one. Some scholars argue that numerical strength or qualities like being male or free should tip the scale. The Hanafi school, however, restricts such factors to complete groups (quorum met) and rejects them for individuals, drawing a parallel to the rules of testimony. This lesson unpacks that critique and its foundation.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two reports
Identify one report that affirms an attribute (e.g., impurity, prohibition) and another that negates it. The affirmative is based on observed evidence; the negation may be based on default or on separate evidence.
This sets the stage for understanding how evidence outweighs default.
2
Examine the negation report's basis
Determine whether the negation report relies on the original default (e.g., water is pure) or on direct evidence (e.g., careful handling of water). If it is mere default, it is invalid for contradiction.
Only negation with evidence can compete with an affirmative based on evidence.
3
Identify the invalid preponderance view
Recognize the position of Abdullah al-Jurjani and a narration from al-Karkhi that preponderance can be by greater number or by masculinity/freedom generally, even for individuals.
This is the 'invalid preponderance' the author critiques.
4
Apply the Hanafi restriction
Understand that number can give preponderance only when comparing two groups (e.g., four narrators vs. three). Masculinity and freedom only matter when comparing two complete groups (two men vs. two women; two free men vs. two slaves), not for individuals.
The quorum (nisab) must be met in both reports for these qualities to be relevant.
5
Trace the analogy to testimony
The Hanafi position is derived by qiyas (analogy) from the rules of testimony (shahada), where gender and freedom affect credibility only when the testimonial group is complete (two witnesses).
This explains why the same factors are limited to groups in report preponderance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الناس من رجّح بفضل عدد الرواة؛ لأن القلب إليه أميل، وبالذكورة والحرية في العدد دون الأفراد؛ فإذا تعارض الخبران فيه بأن يقول أحد إنه نجس أو حرام، ويقول الآخر: طاهر أو حلال، فخبر الأول مثبت للحرمة والنجاسة العارضتين ولا شك أنه مبني على دليل وهو أنه رأى سبب الحرمة والنجاسة، وخبر الثاني ناف للحرمة والنجاسة المذكورتين فخبر النفي يشتبه حاله لم يدر أن الراوي أخبر بالأصل أو بدليل، فلا بد من أن يتفحص حاله، فإن كان خبره بمجرد أن الأصل فيهما الطهارة أو الحل، فلا يقبل؛ لأنه نفي بغير دليل، فلا يصلح المعارضة، فيعمل حينئذ بخبر النجاسة والحرمة؛ لأنه مثبت وإن كان بدليل بأن أخذ الماء مثلا من نهر جار وأدخله بنفسه في أناء طاهر ولم يفارقه بعد، حتى يتوهم أنه ألقى النجاسة فيه أحد، فحينئذ كان خبره بنفي النجاسة والطهارة بدليل. النجاسة والحرمة حيث يكون مبنياً على دليل بين الخبرين: أحدهما خبر بنجاسة الماء وحرمة الطعام، والآخر خبر بنفيهما. بالأصل: وهو الحل والطهارة. ثم بين المصنف حال الترجيح الفاسد بقوله: ومن الناس: وهو عبد الله الجرجاني من أصحابنا وأبو الحسن الكرخي في رواية من رجّح أحد الخبرين المتعارضين على الآخر بفضل عدد الرواة بأن يكون عدد أحدهما ثلاثة والآخر أربعة فيترجّح ذو الأربعة على الآخر. أميل: وذلك لأن الترجيح إنما يكون لقوة تكون في أحد الخبرين ولاتوجد في الآخر، وفي كثرة الرواة نوع قوة؛ لأن قول الجماعة أقوى في الظن وأقرب إلى إفادة العلم، وأبعد عن السهو عن قول الاثنين أو الثلاثة. في العدد: بأن يكون رواة أحد الخبرين رجلين والآخر امرأتين أويكون رواة أحدهما حرين والآخر عبدين، فحينئذ يترجح خبر الرجلين على خبر الامرأتين وخبر الحرين على خبر العبدين عند التعارض بينهما؛ لأن خبر الرجلين الحرين حجة تامة دون خبر العبدين والامرأتين وإن كان في خبر العبدين والامرأتين نصاب الخبر وهو العدد وأقله الاثنان، لكن لما ثبت وصف الذكورة والحرية في أحدهما دون الآخر، فيترجّح به على غيره كما في الشهادة. دون الأفراد : أي لا عبرة بوصف الذكورة والحرية الثابت في الأفراد ؛ لأن نصاب الخبر وهو العدد في كليهما مفقود، فخبر كل واحد منهما ليس بحجة، فلا يترجح خبر الحر الواحد على خبر العبد الواحد والامرأة الواحدة.
And among people is one who gives preponderance by virtue of number of narrators, because the heart is more inclined to it, and by masculinity and freedom in groups, not in individuals. So when two reports contradict each other regarding this—one says it is impure or forbidden, the other says it is pure or permissible—the first report affirms the supervening prohibition and impurity, and there is no doubt it is based on evidence, namely that he saw the cause of prohibition and impurity. The second report negates the mentioned prohibition and impurity, so the status of the negation report is ambiguous, not known whether the narrator reported based on the original or on evidence. So his case must be examined: if his report is merely that the original in them is purity or permissibility, then it is not accepted because it is negation without evidence, so it is not valid for contradiction. Then the report of impurity and prohibition is acted upon because it is affirmative. If it is by evidence, such as taking water from a flowing river and putting it himself into a pure vessel and not leaving it thereafter, so that one might suspect that someone threw impurity into it—then his report negating impurity and purity (i.e., negating impurity) is by evidence. The impurity and prohibition where it is based on evidence between the two reports: one report affirming impurity of water and prohibition of food, the other negating them. By the original: which is permissibility and purity. Then the author explained the state of invalid preponderance by his statement: 'And among people'—namely Abdullah al-Jurjani from our companions and Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi in one narration—who gives preponderance to one of two conflicting reports over the other by virtue of number of narrators, such that one has three and the other four, so the one with four is given preponderance. Inclined: because preponderance is only due to strength in one report not found in the other, and in plurality of narrators there is a kind of strength, because the statement of the group is stronger in probability and closer to yielding knowledge, and further from forgetfulness than the statement of two or three. In groups: such that the narrators of one report are two men and the other two women, or the narrators of one are two free men and the other two slaves, then the report of the two men is given preponderance over the two women, and the report of the two free men over the two slaves when they conflict, because the report of two free men is a complete proof unlike that of two slaves and two women, even though in the report of two slaves and two women the quorum of report (minimum number of two) exists. But because the attribute of masculinity and freedom is established in one and not the other, it is given preponderance by it over the other as in testimony. As for individuals: i.e., no consideration is given to the attribute of masculinity and freedom established in individuals, because the quorum of report (the number) is lacking in both, so each individual's report is not a proof, so the report of one free man is not given preponderance over the report of one slave or one woman.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage addresses the method of preponderance (tarjih) when two equally evidence-based reports conflict—specifically, the view that preponderance can be by greater number of narrators or by qualities like being male or free. The author identifies this as a 'invalid preponderance' (ترجيح فاسد) held by some Hanafi scholars like Abdullah al-Jurjani and a narration from Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi. The text argues that while number can be a factor for groups (e.g., four narrators preferred over three), the qualities of masculinity and freedom only matter when comparing groups (e.g., two men vs. two women), not individuals (one man vs. one woman). This is analogized to testimony (شهادة) where such qualities matter only when the quorum is met. The passage reiterates the earlier principle: affirmation based on evidence typically outweighs negation based on default, unless the negation also has evidence. The author explains that if a negation report is ambiguous, the narrator's state must be examined: if he relied on default assumptions, it is invalid; if he had direct evidence (like observing no impurity after carefully handling water), it can stand. Overall, the passage critiques a mechanical reliance on numbers and social status, emphasizing that the substance of evidence is primary.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of giving preference to one of two conflicting proofs due to some strength
الذكورة والحرية (al-dhukura wa al-hurriyya): Masculinity and freedom as qualities considered for preponderance in group narrations
نصاب الخبر (nisab al-khabar): The minimum number of narrators required for a report to be considered a proof (usually two)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented, in which scenario can masculinity or freedom give preponderance to one report over another?
A) When comparing two individual narrators, one free male and one female slave.
B) When comparing two groups, e.g., two free men vs. two slaves.
C) Never, because these qualities are irrelevant.
D) Only when the reports are about purity and impurity.

Key Takeaway
Preponderance by number or quality (gender, freedom) is valid only for complete groups (quorum met), not for individual narrators—a rule established by analogy to testimony.

Definition and Components of Qiyas
Introduces the chapter on qiyas and its five components.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas and identify its five components (essence, condition, pillar, ruling, defense) as per the Hanafi usul framework.

Core Idea
Qiyas is defined by five aspects; its pillar is the effective cause ('illah), not the extension of the ruling.

This passage opens the chapter on Qiyas in a Hanafi usul work. It explains why knowing the meaning of qiyas is necessary before discussing its conditions, pillar, ruling, and defense. The passage also highlights a key Hanafi position: the 'illah must be effective (mu'aththira), not merely formal (tardiyya), as the Shafi'is hold. Understanding these components is essential for performing correct analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five components
The passage lists the five topics covered in the chapter: essence (nafs al-qiyas), condition (shart), pillar (rukn), ruling (hukm), and defense (daf'). These make up the complete treatment of qiyas.
The author justifies this structure by noting that without knowing the meaning, research is futile.
2
Distinguish linguistic and technical meaning
The 'essence' includes both the linguistic (measuring) and technical (extending a ruling due to shared cause) definitions. Recognizing this duality is fundamental.
3
Define the pillar (rukn)
The pillar is the 'illah (effective cause), the attribute common to the original and new case. The passage states explicitly, 'What is meant by the pillar is the cause.'
Note that the pillar is not the original or new case themselves, but the connecting link.
4
Understand the ruling (hukm) of qiyas
The ruling is the extension of the original ruling to the new case. However, the passage clarifies that this extension is the result of qiyas, not qiyas itself. Qiyas is the identification of the cause.
This distinction is crucial: qiyas = cause-identification; extension = effect.
5
Recognize the defense (daf') as dialectical engagement
The defense involves repelling objections from the Shafi'is, who accept formal (tardiyya) causes. The Hanafis require effective (mu'aththira) causes. This debate is the basis of the science of disputation (munazara).
The passage indicates that the entire field of munazara originates from this debate.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس تعريف القياس] ۱۹۱ البحث في القياس باب القياس وهو يشتمل على بيان نفس القياس وشرطه وركنه وحكمه ودفعه. نفس القياس: أي معناه لغة وشرعاً، فإنه سيبين معناه اللغوي والشرعي. وشرطه فيبيّن المصنف في هذا الباب شرط القياس وركنه وحكمه ودفعه كما سيأتي، ووجه حصر الباب في تلك الأمور الخمس أن الشيء إذا لم يعرف معناه اللغوي والاصطلاحي لايصح البحث عنه؛ لأن البحث عن المهمل عبث وبعد تعين معناه إما أن يعتبر باعتبار ما هو مانع ودافع له أو لا، وعلى التقدير الثاني إما أن يعتبر باعتبار ما يتوقف على ذلك الشيء أو لا، بل يتوقف الشيء عليه، والمراد بالركن العلة التي هي الوصف الجامع بين الأصل والفرع؛ إذ هي ركن القياس كما سيأتي، والمراد بالبحث عن الركن البحث بما يتعلق بالعلة من الأحكام والشروط على ما يأتي في بيان ركنه لا بيان أن ركنه العلة؛ لأن ركنه يعلم من بيان نفسه، والمراد من حكم القياس الأثر الثابت به، وهو تعدية الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع وهي نتيجة القياس فالقياس تبين أن العلة في الأصل هذا ليثبت الحكم في الفرع لا تعدية الحكم وإثباته في الفرع؛ لأن هذا المعنى معلول للقياس، والقياس علة، والعلة غير المعلول، والمراد بالدفع دفع الاعتراضات الواردة على العلل المؤثرة من أصحاب الشافعي، فإن للشافعية عللاً طردية ولنا مؤثرة فنحن ندفعها على وجه تلجئهم إلى القول بالتأثير، والشافعية تدفع العلل المؤثرة، ثم نجيبهم عن الدفع، فهذا البحث هو أساس المناظرة، وقد اقتبس علم المناظرة من هذا البحث، وسيأتي الوضوح، فانتظر.
Chapter on Qiyas: Definition of Qiyas. Research in Qiyas. Chapter on Qiyas. It includes the explanation of the essence of qiyas, its condition, its pillar, its ruling, and its defense. The essence of qiyas: that is, its linguistic and legal meaning, for he will explain its linguistic and legal meaning. Its condition: the author will explain in this chapter the condition of qiyas, its pillar, its ruling, and its defense as will come. The reason for confining the chapter to these five matters is that if a thing's linguistic and terminological meaning is not known, research about it is invalid because research about something vague is futile. After its meaning is determined, either it is considered in terms of what prevents and repels it or not. On the second assumption, either it is considered in terms of what depends on that thing or not, rather the thing depends on it. What is meant by the pillar is the cause ('illah), which is the description common between the original and the branch, for it is the pillar of qiyas as will come. What is meant by research on the pillar is research concerning the 'illah of rulings and conditions, as will come in the explanation of its pillar, not to state that its pillar is the 'illah, because its pillar is known from the explanation of itself. What is meant by the ruling of qiyas is the effect established by it, which is the extension of the ruling from the original to the branch, and that is the result of qiyas. So qiyas is to make clear that the cause in the original is such that the ruling is established in the branch; it is not the extension of the ruling and its establishment in the branch, because that meaning is the effect of qiyas, and qiyas is the cause, and the cause is not the effect. What is meant by defense is repelling objections that come against effective causes from the followers of al-Shafi'i. For the Shafi'is have formal (tardiyya) causes, and we have effective (mu'aththira) causes. So we repel them in a way that compels them to accept the concept of effectiveness. And the Shafi'is repel the effective causes, then we answer their repulsion. This research is the basis of disputation, and the science of disputation has been extracted from this research. Clarity will come, so wait.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Qiyas (analogical reasoning) and outlines its five essential components: (1) the essence/nature of qiyas (its linguistic and technical definition), (2) its conditions, (3) its pillar (rukn), (4) its ruling (hukm), and (5) its defense (daf') against objections. The commentator explains why these five are necessary: one cannot discuss something without knowing its meaning; after that, one must consider what precludes it (conditions), what constitutes its core (pillar), what it produces (ruling), and how to defend it against challenges. Importantly, the 'pillar' of qiyas is identified as the 'illah (effective cause), which is the shared attribute between the original case (asl) and the new case (far'). The 'ruling' of qiyas is the result—the extension of the original ruling to the new case—but qiyas itself is the act of identifying the cause, not the extension itself. The 'defense' refers to the dialectical engagement with the Shafi'i school: Shafi'is are said to use 'tardiyya' (formal/correlational) causes, while Hanafis require 'mu'aththira' (effective) causes that genuinely influence the ruling. The passage indicates that the entire science of munazara (disputation) originates from this debate over causal effectiveness. The commentator promises further clarity later.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): Linguistically: measuring; technically: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared effective cause.
العلة (al-ʿilla): The effective cause (attribute) that is the basis for the original ruling and is shared with the new case, making the ruling extendable.
الركن (al-rukn): The pillar of qiyas; which is the 'illah (cause) that connects the original and branch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the pillar (rukn) of qiyas?
A) The original case (asl)
B) The new case (far')
C) The effective cause ('illah)
D) The ruling extended

Key Takeaway
The pillar of qiyas is the effective cause ('illah), not the extension of the ruling; qiyas is the identification of the cause.

Definition and Conditions of Qiyas
Defines qiyas linguistically and technically, and begins conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qiyas, distinguish between its linguistic and technical meanings, and identify the first condition (negative) of a valid qiyas.

Core Idea
Qiyas manifests a ruling via a shared cause; it does not create it.

This passage opens the chapter on qiyas by establishing its meaning and first condition. Understanding what qiyas truly is—and is not—is essential before any analogical reasoning. The author lays out the linguistic root (taqdir), the technical definition (showing the like of a ruling via a like of the cause), and the foundational condition that the original case must not be specific to its ruling by another text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning of qiyas
Find the author's statement on the literal meaning: 'al-qiyas huwa al-taqdir' (measurement). Note the example 'qis al-na'la bi al-na'l'. This is the majority (aktharun) view.
Opposing view: Ibn al-Hajib says musawa (equality).
2
Understand the technical meaning
The jurists use qiyas when they take the ruling of a branch from an original due to a shared attribute (the 'illa). This is 'showing' (ibana) the like of the ruling, not establishing it.
Qiyas is a manifester (muzhir), not an establisher (muthbit).
3
Analyze the formal definition from Shaykh Abu Mansur
The definition: 'Ibanatu mithli hukmi ahadil madhkurin bi mithli illatin fil akhar'. Note why 'mithl' (like) is used: to avoid the false implication that the ruling or cause transfers from original to branch.
The word 'madhkurin' includes analogies between existing and non-existing cases (e.g., insane person analogized to a child).
4
Recognize the structure of conditions
The author states there are four conditions: two negative (adamyan) and two positive (wujudyan). The first negative condition is that the original is not specific (i.e., its ruling is not limited to it) by another text.
Non-existence (adam) precedes existence (wujud) in order of discussion.
5
Apply the first negative condition to an example
Example: rice compared to wheat in the prohibition of unequal sale of the same genus. Wheat is the original (mahall al-hukm) because the text explicitly prohibits it. Rice is the branch. The condition requires that the original's ruling is not exclusive to it by a specific text.
The passage cuts off here; further conditions will follow.

اعلم اختلف العلماء في معناه اللغوي، فذهب ابن الحاجب وأتباعه إلى أن معناه المساواة، يقال: فلان يقاس بفلان أي يساويه، وذهب الأكثرون إلى أن معناه لغة التقدير وهذا أظهر؛ لأن القياس صفة القائس، والمساواة صفة المقيس أو المقيس عليه، والضمير في قوله: 'اجعله' يرجع إلى النعل نظراً إلى ظاهر اللفظ وإن كان مؤنثا سماعيًا، ثم شرع في المعنى الاصطلاحي والفقهاء إذا أخذوا إلخ والمراد من الأخذ إثبات مثل حكم الأصل في الفرع، والحاصل إذا أظهروا حكم الفرع من الأصل المقيس عليه بسبب اشتراك الوصف الذي هو علة الحكم في الأصل والفرع. قياساً وهذا معنى القياس في اصطلاح الفقهاء، والمناسبة بين المعنيين أي اللغوي والاصطلاحي ظاهر بينه المصنّف بقوله: لتقديرهم الفرع إلخ : فالمعنى الاصطلاحي موافق للمعنى اللغوي في التقدير إلا أن في اللغة التقدير مطلق، وفي المعنى الاصطلاحي . التقدير بين الأصل والفرع في العلة ،والحكم فظهر أن المساواة في العلة والحكم بين الأصل والفرع شرط للقياس، وهذا ليس بحد حقيقي للقياس، بل الحد المنقول عن الشيخ أبي المنصور حله: إبانة مثل حكم أحد المذكورين بمثل علة في الآخر، واختار لفظ الإبانة دون الإثبات؛ لأن القياس مظهر وليس بمثبت بل المثبت هو الله تعالى. وذكر مثل الحكم ومثل العلة اجتناباً عن لزوم القول بانتقال الأوصاف، فإنه لو لم يذكر لفظ المثل يلزم انتقال حكم الأصل الذي هو أيضاً وصف إلى الفرع والعلة التي هي الوصف من الأصل إلى الفرع، وهذا باطل، وذكر لفظ 'المذكورين' ليشمل القياس بين الموجودين وبين المعدومين كقياس عديم العقل بسبب الجنون على عديم العقل بسبب الصغر في سقوط الخطاب عنه بالعجز. وأما شرطه أي القياس ،فأربعة، الاثنان منها عدميان والاثنان منها ،وجوديان، قدم العدميين على الوجوديين لكون العدم مقدّما على الوجود، فالأول من العدميين فأن لا يكون إلخ. الأصل: اعلم الأصل في القياس عند جمهور العلماء من الفقهاء هو محلّ الحكم المنصوص عليه، كما إذا قيس الأرز على البر في تحريم البيع بجنسه متفاضلاً، كان الأصل هو البر؛ لأنه محل لحكم الحرمة في البيع بجنسه متفاضلاً، والنص قد ورد فيه، أن

And when he finished the discussion of ijma, he began the discussion of qiyas and placed it after ijma because it is lower in strength. The essence of qiyas: that is its meaning alone, linguistically and legally, for he will explain its linguistic and legal meaning. And its condition: the author explains in this chapter the condition of qiyas, its pillar, its ruling, and its rebuttal as will follow. And the reason for limiting the chapter to these five matters is that if a thing's linguistic and terminological meaning is not known, research about it is not sound; because research about an ambiguous thing is futile. After its meaning is determined, it is either considered with regard to what is a preventer and repeller of it or not. And on the second supposition, either it is considered with regard to what depends on that thing or not, but rather the thing depends on it. And what is meant by the pillar is the cause which is the description uniting the original and the branch; for it is the pillar of qiyas as will come. And what is meant by research on the pillar is research on what pertains to the cause of rulings and conditions as will come in the explanation of its pillar, not the explanation that its pillar is the cause; because its pillar is known from the explanation of itself. And what is meant by the ruling of qiyas is the effect established by it, which is the extension of the ruling from the original to the branch, and it is the result of qiyas. So qiyas is to show that the cause in the original is this, so that the ruling is established in the branch, not the extension of the ruling and its establishment in the branch; because this meaning is the effect of qiyas, and qiyas is the cause, and the cause is other than the effect. And what is meant by rebuttal is the rebuttal of objections raised against the effective causes by the followers of al-Shafi'i; for the Shafi'is have non-effective (tardiyya) causes and we have effective causes. So we rebut them in a way that forces them to accept effectiveness, and the Shafi'is rebut the effective causes, then we respond to their rebuttal. So this discussion is the foundation of disputation, and the science of disputation was derived from this discussion, and clarity will come, so wait. As for the first, qiyas linguistically is taqdir (measurement); it is said: 'qis al-na'la bi al-na'l' meaning measure it by it and make it its equivalent. And the jurists, when they derive the ruling of the branch from the original, call that qiyas, due to their estimation of the mentioned derivation of the branch from the original in ruling and cause. Know that scholars differed regarding its linguistic meaning: Ibn al-Hajib and his followers held that it means musawa (equality), it is said: 'fulan yuqasu bi fulan' i.e., he equals him. And the majority held that it linguistically means taqdir, and this is more apparent, because qiyas is an attribute of the measurer, and musawa is an attribute of the measured or that which is measured against. And the pronoun in his statement 'ij'alhu' refers to the sandal in view of the apparent wording, although it is feminine by common usage. Then he began the technical meaning: 'and the jurists when they take...' etc. And what is meant by 'taking' is establishing the like of the ruling of the original in the branch. The summary is that when they show the ruling of the branch from the original measured upon it due to the sharing of the description which is the cause of the ruling in the original and the branch, it is called qiyas, and this is the meaning of qiyas in the terminology of the jurists. And the connection between the two meanings, the linguistic and the terminological, is apparent, which the author explained by his statement: 'due to their estimation of the branch...' etc. So the terminological meaning agrees with the linguistic meaning in taqdir, except that in language taqdir is absolute, and in the terminological meaning it is taqdir between the original and the branch in the cause and the ruling. So it appears that musawa (equality) in the cause and ruling between the original and the branch is a condition for qiyas, and this is not a real definition of qiyas. Rather, the definition transmitted from Shaykh Abu Mansur is: 'Ibanatu mithli hukmi ahadil madhkurin bi mithli illatin fil akhar' (showing the like of the ruling of one of the mentioned [cases] by a like of the cause in the other). And he chose the word 'ibanah' (showing) instead of 'ithbat' (establishing) because qiyas is a manifester, not an establisher; the establisher is Allah. And he mentioned 'like' of the ruling and 'like' of the cause to avoid the necessary implication of transfer of attributes; for if he did not mention the word 'like', it would necessitate the transfer of the ruling of the original, which is also a description, to the branch, and the transfer of the cause, which is the description, from the original to the branch, and this is false. And he mentioned the word 'al-madhkurin' (the mentioned) to include qiyas between existing things and non-existing things, like the analogy of one without intellect due to insanity on one without intellect due to childhood in the falling of address (khitab) due to incapacity. And as for its condition i.e., of qiyas, there are four, two of which are negative and two positive. He placed the negative before the positive because non-existence precedes existence. So the first of the negative conditions is that it should not be... etc. The original: know that the original in qiyas according to the majority of jurists is the locus (mahall) of the ruling that is explicitly mentioned, such as when rice is compared to wheat in the prohibition of selling a genus for the same genus with inequality; the original is wheat, because it is the locus of the ruling of prohibition in selling a genus for the same genus with inequality, and the text has come regarding it, that... =
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on qiyas, explaining its five aspects: definition, condition, pillar, ruling, and rebuttal. The author first gives the linguistic meaning as 'taqdir' (measurement), citing the example 'qis al-na'la bi al-na'l'. A dispute is noted: Ibn al-Hajib and his followers say qiyas means equality (musawa), but the majority (aktharun) say it means taqdir, which is more apparent because qiyas is an attribute of the measurer. The technical meaning is then given: jurists call it qiyas when they derive the ruling of the branch from the original due to a shared attribute (the 'illa). The connection between the two meanings is that both involve estimation, but in the technical sense it is specifically estimation of the branch from the original in the cause and ruling. The author then cites a formal definition from Shaykh Abu Mansur: 'Ibanatu mithli hukmi ahadil madhkurin bi mithli illatin fil akhar' (showing the like of the ruling of one of the mentioned [cases] by a like of the cause in the other). Key points: qiyas manifests rulings, it does not establish them (the establisher is Allah); the word 'like' is used to avoid the false notion of transfer of attributes; the phrase 'al-madhkurin' covers analogies between existing and non-existing cases (e.g., one lacking intellect due to insanity analogized to a child). Finally, the author begins discussing conditions, noting there are four (two negative, two positive). The first negative condition is that the original is not specific to its ruling by another text. An example is given: rice is compared to wheat in the prohibition of unequal sale of the same genus; the original (wheat) is the locus of the explicit ruling. The text cuts off before completing the condition.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Linguistically: taqdir (measurement). Technically: showing the like of the ruling of one of the mentioned cases by a like of the cause in the other.
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause; the attribute that unites the original and the branch and is the basis for extending the ruling.
التقدير (al-taqdir): Estimation or measurement; the linguistic meaning of qiyas according to the majority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the word 'mithl' (like) used in the technical definition of qiyas?
A) To emphasize that the ruling must be exactly the same
B) To avoid the implication that the ruling and cause transfer from the original to the branch
C) To indicate that qiyas is only used in cases of complete similarity
D) To limit qiyas to existing things only

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is the manifestation of a like ruling via a like cause, resting on estimation (taqdir), not transfer.

8 min
Linguistic and Technical Definition of Qiyas
Defines qiyas linguistically and technically with scholarly dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and technical definitions of qiyas according to the Hanafi school, and explain why the technical definition uses 'manifestation' (ibana) instead of 'proof' (ithbat).

Core Idea
Qiyas means estimation, not equality — it is a manifestor, not a prover.

This passage introduces the foundational concept of qiyas (analogy) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It first clarifies the linguistic meaning — a point of scholarly disagreement — then presents the technical definition with careful precision. Understanding this definition is crucial because it sets the epistemological boundaries of qiyas: it is a tool for manifesting rulings, not creating them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic dispute
Find the two contending meanings of qiyas in Arabic: estimation (taqdir) vs. equality (musawat). Note which view the author prefers and why.
The author argues that qiyas is a characteristic of the measurer, while equality is a characteristic of the measured.
2
Extract the technical definition
Locate the technical definition from Shaykh Abu al-Mansur: 'The manifestation of the like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned by the like of a cause in the other.' Identify each key term (ibana, mithl, mazkurin).
The term 'ibana' is chosen over 'ithbat' to avoid attributing legislation to the mujtahid.
3
Analyze the role of 'like' (mithl)
Understand why 'mithl' is used in the definition. Without it, the definition would imply transfer of attributes, which is invalid.
Transfer (intiqal) would mean the ruling literally moves from asl to far', which is impossible.
4
Examine the condition for qiyas
Note the condition mentioned: the original must not be specified (makhsus) in its ruling by another text. Understand why this invalidates qiyas.
If the asl is makhsus, it cannot serve as a reliable basis for analogy.
5
Apply the definition to a sample
Think of a simple qiyas, e.g., extending the prohibition of barley to rice. Identify the asl, far', cause, and ruling. Confirm the definition applies.
This shows qiyas as a manifestor of a ruling already implicit in the Shariah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
شروط القياس
أما الأول فالقياس هو التقدير لغةً، يقال: قس النعل بالنعل أي قدره به واجعله نظير الآخر. والفقهاء إذا أخذوا حكم الفرع من الأصل سموا ذلك قياساً؛ لتقديرهم الأخذ المذكور الفرع بالأصل في الحكم والعلة.
[شروط القياس]
وأما شرطه فأن لايكون الأصل مخصوصاً بحكمه بنص آخر،
الأول: هو بيان نفس القياس فشرع أولا في بيان معناه اللغوي، فقال: فالقياس هو إلخ: اعلم اختلف العلماء في معناه اللغوي، فذهب ابن الحاجب وأتباعه إلى أن معناه المساواة، يقال: فلان يقاس بفلان أي يساويه، وذهب الأكثرون إلى أن معناه لغة التقدير وهذا أظهر؛ لأن القياس صفة القائس، والمساواة صفة المقيس أو المقيس عليه، والضمير في قوله: "اجعله" يرجع إلى النعل نظراً إلى ظاهر اللفظ وإن كان مؤنثا سماعيًا، ثم شرع في المعنى الاصطلاحي والفقهاء إذا أخذوا إلخ والمراد من الأخذ إثبات مثل حكم الأصل في الفرع، والحاصل إذا أظهروا حكم الفرع من الأصل المقيس عليه بسبب اشتراك الوصف الذي هو علة الحكم في الأصل والفرع. قياساً وهذا معنى القياس في اصطلاح الفقهاء، والمناسبة بين المعنيين أي اللغوي والاصطلاحي ظاهر بينه المصنّف بقوله: لتقديرهم الفرع إلخ : فالمعنى الاصطلاحي موافق للمعنى اللغوي في التقدير إلا أن في اللغة التقدير مطلق، وفي المعنى الاصطلاحي . التقدير بين الأصل والفرع في العلة ،والحكم فظهر أن المساواة في العلة والحكم بين الأصل والفرع شرط للقياس، وهذا ليس بحد حقيقي للقياس، بل الحد المنقول عن الشيخ أبي المنصور حله: إبانة مثل حكم أحد المذكورين بمثل علة في الآخر، واختار لفظ الإبانة دون الإثبات؛ لأن القياس مظهر وليس بمثبت بل المثبت هو الله تعالى. وذكر مثل الحكم ومثل العلة اجتناباً عن لزوم القول بانتقال الأوصاف، فإنه لو لم يذكر لفظ المثل يلزم انتقال حكم الأصل الذي هو أيضاً وصف إلى الفرع والعلة التي هي الوصف من الأصل إلى الفرع، وهذا باطل، وذكر لفظ "المذكورين" ليشمل القياس بين الموجودين وبين المعدومين كقياس عديم العقل بسبب الجنون على عديم العقل بسبب الصغر في سقوط الخطاب عنه بالعجز.
Chapter of Qiyas. Conditions of Qiyas. As for the first, qiyas is estimation (taqdir) linguistically. It is said: 'Measure the sandal with the sandal' meaning estimate it by it and make it the counterpart of the other. And the jurists, when they take the ruling of the branch (far') from the original (asl), they call that qiyas; due to their estimation of the aforementioned taking of the branch from the original in the ruling and the cause. [Conditions of Qiyas] As for its condition, it is that the original not be specified in its ruling by another text. First: It is an explanation of qiyas itself. So he began first in explaining its linguistic meaning, and said: 'So qiyas is...' Know that the scholars have differed in its linguistic meaning. Ibn al-Hajib and his followers held that its meaning is equality: 'So-and-so is measured with so-and-so' meaning he equals him. And the majority held that its meaning linguistically is estimation, and this is more apparent because qiyas is a characteristic of the measurer (qa'is), whereas equality is a characteristic of the measured (maqis) or the measured upon (maqis 'alayh). And the pronoun in his statement 'make it' refers to the sandal in view of the apparent wording even though it is a feminine noun by convention. Then he proceeded to the technical meaning: 'and the jurists when they take...' And the intent of 'taking' is proving the like of the ruling of the original in the branch. And the outcome: when they manifest the ruling of the branch from the original measured upon due to the sharing of the attribute which is the cause of the ruling in the original and the branch, they call that qiyas. And this is the meaning of qiyas in the terminology of the jurists. The appropriateness between the two meanings, i.e., linguistic and technical, is apparent, which the author clarified by his statement: 'due to their estimation of the branch...' So the technical meaning agrees with the linguistic meaning in estimation, except that in language estimation is absolute, and in the technical meaning it is the estimation between the original and the branch in the cause and the ruling. So it became apparent that equality in the cause and the ruling between the original and the branch is a condition for qiyas. And this is not a real definition of qiyas; rather the definition transmitted from Shaykh Abu al-Mansur is: 'The manifestation of the like of the ruling of one of the two mentioned [cases] by the like of a cause in the other.' And he chose the word 'manifestation' (ibana) instead of 'proof' (ithbat) because qiyas is a manifestor and not a prover; rather the prover is Allah the Exalted. And he mentioned 'the like of the ruling' and 'the like of the cause' to avoid the necessity of saying the transfer of attributes; for if he had not mentioned the word 'like', it would necessitate the transfer of the ruling of the original, which is also an attribute, to the branch, and the transfer of the cause, which is the attribute, from the original to the branch, and this is invalid. And he mentioned the word 'the two mentioned' to include qiyas between existing things and between non-existing things, like comparing one lacking intellect due to insanity to one lacking intellect due to minority in the dropping of address (khitab) from him due to incapacity.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage defines qiyas both linguistically and technically. Linguistically, the author prefers 'estimation' (taqdir) over 'equality' (musawat), arguing that qiyas is an action of the measurer, whereas equality describes the relationship between the measured items. Technically, qiyas is the process of establishing a similar ruling in a new case (far') based on a shared cause ('illah) with the original case (asl). The text distinguishes between qiyas as a manifestor (muzhir) rather than a prover (muthbit), emphasizing that the true legislator is Allah. The definition avoids the error of attribute transfer by using 'like' (mithl) and includes analogies between non-existent entities. This is a standard Hanafi definition, highlighting the mujtahid's role in revealing rulings through analogy.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Linguistically: estimation (taqdir); technically: manifestation of the like of a ruling in a branch case due to a shared cause with the original
التقدير (al-taqdir): Estimation or measuring; the linguistic meaning of qiyas according to the majority
الإبانة (al-ibana): Manifestation; the term used in the technical definition to indicate that qiyas reveals a ruling rather than creating it

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Shaykh Abu al-Mansur choose the word 'ibana' (manifestation) over 'ithbat' (proof) in the technical definition of qiyas?
A) Because 'ithbat' implies the mujtahid creates the ruling.
B) Because qiyas reveals a ruling that is already present in the Shariah.
C) Because 'ibana' is easier for beginners.
D) Because 'ithbat' is reserved for Quranic proofs.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas in Hanafi usul is a manifestor of rulings through estimation of shared causes, not a creator of rulings, and its linguistic root is estimation (taqdir), not equality.
