Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Conditions of the Description in Qiyas: Salāḥiyyah and Iʿtidāl
Explaining the necessity of ṣalāḥiyyah and ʿadālah in the cause of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between suitability (mulāʾamah) and effectiveness (taʾthīr) and explain why the Hanafi school requires both for a valid qiyas cause.

Core Idea
A valid legal cause in qiyas must be both suitable and effective—suitability alone does not suffice for the Hanafis.

This passage delves into the conditions that a description (waṣf) must meet to serve as a legal cause (ʿilla) in qiyas. The author uses the analogy of a witness to explain that the description requires both validity (ṣalāḥiyyah) and probity (ʿadālah). The central debate with the Shāfiʿīs revolves around whether effectiveness (taʾthīr) is an additional requirement beyond mere suitability (mulāʾamah). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Find in the text where the author states that a description must have ṣalāḥiyyah (validity) and ʿadālah (probity). Note that ṣalāḥiyyah is equated with suitability (mulāʾamah).
2
Understand the analogy to a witness
Explain why the description is compared to a witness: just as a witness must be valid (sane, adult, Muslim, free) and upright (pious), so too must the description be suitable and effective.
3
Compare Hanafī and Shāfiʿī views on taʾthīr
Identify the disagreement: Shāfiʿīs consider mulāʾamah sufficient and include taʾthīr within it; Ḥanafīs distinguish mulāʾamah from taʾthīr and require both.
The text explicitly states: 'After suitability, the description cannot be used except after it is effective according to us.'
4
Apply to the guardianship example
Analyze the example of the young non-virgin (thayyib ṣaghīrah). Ḥanafīs use minority (ṣighar) as the cause because it is both suitable and effective (inability); Shāfiʿīs use virginity (bakārah) and thus do not impose guardianship on a young non-virgin.
5
Examine the cat hadith analogy
The author analogizes the description of minority to the description of circling (ṭawāf) for the cat. Both are suitable and effective due to necessity. This shows how qiyas works when the description meets both conditions.
The cat hadith is: 'The cat is not impure; it is among those that circle you.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
ركن القياس
الحكم المعلّل به، ونعني بصلاح الوصف ملائمته، وهو أن يكون على موافقة العِلل المنقولة عن رسول الله وعن السلف.
مثال تعليل بوصف ملائم: كقولنا في الثيب الصغيرة: إنها تزوّج كرهاً؛ لأنها صغيرة
وذلك المعنى كون الوصف صالحاً معدولاً به: أي بالوصف. الحاصل الوصف الذي يجعل علة لحكم النص لا بد له من أمرين أحدهما الصلاحية التي أشار إليها بقوله: "الصالح"، والثاني العدالة التي أشار إليها بقوله: "المعدل إلخ"، وإنما شرط هذان الأمران؛ لأن الوصف بمنزلة الشاهد، فكما لا بد للشاهد من وصف الصلاحية وهي العقل والبلوغ والإسلام والحرية ووصف العدالة وهي الديانة فكذا لا بد للوصف المذكور من هذين الوصفين. ثم شرع في بيان الوصفين فبدأ أولاً بذكر الصلاحية فقال: ونعني إلخ ملائمته وهي الموافقة للحكم بأن يصح إضافة الحكم إليه ولا يكون نائياً عنه كالإسلام، فإنه لا يصح نسبة الفرقة بإسلام أحد الزوجين إليه، كما نسب إليه الشافعي محله، بل العلة في ذلك هو إباء أحد الزوجين عن الإسلام، فهذا الوصف لا يأبى أن يكون الفرقة منسوبة إليه، بخلاف الإسلام، فإنه عرف عاصماً للحقوق لا قاطعاً لها. وهو : أي حصول الملائمة في الوصف. أن يكون على موافقة إلخ بأن يكون علة هذا المجتهد موافقة لعلة استنبط بها النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والصحابة والتابعون الكرام، ولا تكون متنائية عنها؛ لأنهم كانوا يعلّلون بالأوصاف الملائمة للأحكام لا النائية عنها. فقوله: "أن يكون إلخ" على سبيل التمثيل، وليس معناه أن الملائمة هو كون الوصف معتبراً عند الشارع؛ إذ لا يكون الفرق بين الملائمة والتأثير بل معناه ما قلنا نعم عند الشافعية: الملائمة أخصّ من المناسبة؛ لأن المناسبة كون الوصف على منهاج المصالح بحيث لو أضيف إليه الحكم لانتظم كالإسكار لحرمة الخمر، فإن الإسكار وصف يزيل العقل الذي عليه مدار التكليف بخلاف سائر أوصاف الخمر؛ لكونها تقذف بالزبد وتحفظ في الدن، فإن ذلك لا يصلح لحرمة الخمر والملائمة كون الوصف معتبراً عند الشرع، والمناسب قد يكون معتبراً عند الشرع وقد لايكون، فلما أصحاب الشافعي بالله الملائمة في الوصف فلا حاجة لهم بعد ذلك إلى التأثير ، فلهذا يكتفون بهذا القيد وهو الملائمة، فبعد الملائمة لا يجب العمل بالوصف إلا بعد كونه مؤثراً عندنا؛ إذ الملائمة عندنا مرادفة للمناسبة التي لم يوخذ في معناها التأثير، ومخيلا أي مواقعا خيال الصحة في القلب عند الشافعي بطله؛ إذ التأثير موجود في الملائمة عنده، فافهم هذا المقام، فإنه من مزال الإقدام.

اعتبر
كقولنا في الثيب إلخ: اختلف في علة ولاية النكاح، فعندنا الصغر علة، وعند الشافعي البكارة، فالصغيرة البكر يولى عليها اتفاقاً لوجود العلة عندنا وعنده والبكر البالغة يولى عليها عنده لا عندنا والصغيرة الثيب لايولى عليها عنده لعدم العلة، ويولي عليها عندنا أي يزوّجها الولي بلا رضاها فأشبهت البكر: الصغيرة؛ لأنها وصف الصغر موجود في كلتيهما، فكما أن البكر الصغيرة يولى عليها، فكذا الثيب الصغيرة. بوصف ملائم وهو الصغر، فإنه يليق أن يضاف إليه ولاية النكاح ولاية المناكح جمع منكح بضم الميم وفتح الكاف، فهو مصدر ميمي من الإنكاح أو بفتح الميم والكاف فهو ظرف زمان ومكان، أي ولاية تثبت في وقت النكاح أو في مكانه، وقيل: جمع منكوحة فهو ضعيف؛ لأن القياس مناكيح، وذلك لأن ولاية النكاح إنما ثبت بسبب عجز المولاة عليها، والعجز إنما يتحقق في الصغيره؛ إذ هي عاجزة عن التصرف في نفسها ومالها ولا تهتدي إليه سبيلا دون البكر؛ إذ البكر البالغة تعلم منافعها ومضارها فلا حاجة إلى الولاية فيها، وإليها أشار المصنف بقوله: لما يتصل إلخ. العجز عن التصرف فهذا الوصف مؤثر في ولاية النكاح.
الحكم المعلّل به: وهو عدم نجاسة الهرة، فإنه حكم ثابت في قوله عليه: "الهرة ليست بنجسة" معلّل بالطواف، فعلة عدم نجاستها هي الطواف كما قال عليه: إنما هي أي الهرة (من) (الطوافين أي ذكور الطوافين (والطوافات)، فهذه الجملة وقعت موقع التعليل، فالحاصل أن علة ولاية النكاح عندنا الصغر، فهو موافق لوصف الطواف الذي علّل به النبي مع عدم نجاسة الهرة لكونهما مندرجين تحت جنس واحد وهو الضرورة، فكما أن الطواف في الهرة صار علة لعدم نجاسة الهرة للضرورة، وهي ههنا تعذر الاحتراز وصون الأواني عنها، فكذا الصغر في ولاية النكاح صار علة الولاية هنا العجز، فهذا التعليل موافق التعليله، فكما أن في تعليله وصف الطواف ملائم لحكم عدم النجاسة، فكذا وصف الصغر ملائم للولاية، فكلا الوصفين صالحان لأن ينسب إليهما الحكم، وهذا معنى العمل بالوصف: بأن يجعل علة للحكم في الأصل ويثبت به الحكم في الفرع قبل الملائمة: التي مرّ ذكرها الشرط الأول للوصف، فبعدها يتوقف الوصف على الشرط الثاني عند أبي حنيفة حاله وهو التأثير سیجی بيانه، وعلى الإخالة عند الشافعي لله، وسره ما ذكرت آنفاً، فتذكره. أمر شرعي لأن العلل الشرعية المثبتة للحكم التي كلامنا فيها إنما يتعرّف صحتها من جانب الشرع إذا كانت موافقة للعلل المنقولة من السلف قبل ظهور هذا المعنى كيف يعمل بالوصف؛ لأن هذا المعنى أي الملائمة في الوصف بمنزلة الصلاحية للشاهد وبدون الصلاحية لا يقبل شهادة، فكذا ههنا. للضرورة وهي آنفاً، وهي كما الملائمة.
Chapter of Qiyas
The Pillar of Qiyas
The ruling that is qualified by the description, and by the validity of the description we mean its suitability, which is that it be in accordance with the transmitted causes from the Messenger of Allah and from the Salaf.
Example of reasoning with a suitable description: Like our statement regarding a young non-virgin woman: She is married off unwillingly because she is young.
And that meaning is that the description is valid and upright. Summary: The description that is made the cause for a textual ruling necessarily has two matters: one is validity which he indicated by his saying 'the valid', and the second is uprightness which he indicated by his saying 'the upright etc.' These two matters are required because the description is like a witness; just as the witness requires the quality of validity (sanity, puberty, Islam, freedom) and the quality of uprightness (piety), so too the mentioned description requires these two qualities. Then he proceeded to explain the two qualities, beginning first with validity, saying: 'And we mean etc.' its suitability is its congruence with the ruling such that it is correct to ascribe the ruling to it and it is not remote from it, like Islam; for it is not correct to attribute separation due to one of the spouses embracing Islam to it, as al-Shafi'i attributed to it in its place; rather the cause in that case is the refusal of one spouse to accept Islam. So this description does not refuse that separation be attributed to it, unlike Islam, for it is known as a preserver of rights, not a cutter of them. And it (suitability) is the occurrence of congruence in the description. His saying 'That it be in accordance etc.' means that the cause of this mujtahid be in accordance with the cause derived by the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the noble Companions and Followers, and not be remote from them; because they used to reason with descriptions suitable to rulings, not remote ones. So his saying 'That it be etc.' is by way of example, and its meaning is not that suitability is that the description be considered by the Lawgiver; for then there would be no difference between suitability and effect. Rather its meaning is what we said. Indeed, according to the Shafi'is, suitability is more specific than appropriateness; because appropriateness is that the description be in line with benefit such that if the ruling were attached to it, it would be coherent, like intoxication for the prohibition of wine; for intoxication is a description that removes the intellect upon which obligation revolves, unlike other descriptions of wine, because they cause foaming and preservation in containers; that does not suit the prohibition of wine. Suitability is that the description is considered by the Lawgiver, and the appropriate may or may not be considered by the Lawgiver. So since the Shafi'is [rely on] suitability in the description, they have no need after that for effect. Hence they suffice with this restriction, which is suitability. After suitability, the description cannot be used except after it is effective according to us; for suitability with us is synonymous with appropriateness which did not include effect in its meaning. And 'mukhayyilan' means that it causes the imagination of correctness in the heart according to al-Shafi'i; he rejected it, for effect is present in suitability according to him. Understand this station, for it is a place of slipping.

Consider
Our saying regarding the young non-virgin etc.: There is disagreement about the cause of guardianship in marriage. According to us, minority is the cause, and according to al-Shafi'i, virginity is the cause. So a young virgin is under guardianship by agreement because the cause exists according to us and him, and a mature virgin is under guardianship according to him not us, and a young non-virgin is not under guardianship according to him due to lack of cause, and she is under guardianship according to us, i.e., the guardian marries her without her consent, so she resembles the young virgin; because the description of minority exists in both. So just as the young virgin is under guardianship, so too the young non-virgin. With a suitable description, which is minority, for it is befitting that guardianship in marriage be attached to it. 'Manaakih' is plural of 'munkah' with damma on the meem and fatha on the kaf, which is a verbal noun of 'inkaah' or with fatha on the meem and kaf, it is a noun of time or place, i.e., guardianship established at the time of marriage or in its place. It is said: plural of 'mankuuhah', but this is weak because the qiyas would be 'manakiih'. This is because guardianship in marriage is established due to the inability of the one under guardianship, and inability is realized only in the minor, for she is unable to act for herself and her property and cannot find a way, unlike the virgin; because a mature virgin knows her benefits and harms, so there is no need for guardianship over her. And the author indicated this by his saying: 'due to what is connected etc.' Inability to act, so this description is effective in guardianship in marriage.
The ruling that is qualified by the description: It is the impurity of the cat, for it is an established ruling in his statement (peace be upon him): 'The cat is not impure,' explained by circling, so the cause of its non-impurity is circling, as he said: 'Indeed it is among the circlers (male circlers) and (female circlers).' This sentence occurs as explanation. So the conclusion is that the cause of guardianship in marriage according to us is minority, and it is in accordance with the description of circling which the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to explain the non-impurity of the cat, because both fall under one genus, which is necessity. Just as circling in the cat became the cause for the non-impurity of the cat due to necessity, which here is the difficulty of avoiding and protecting vessels from it, so too minority in guardianship in marriage became the cause for guardianship here due to inability. So this reasoning is in accordance with that reasoning. So just as in his reasoning, the description of circling is suitable for the ruling of non-impurity, so too the description of minority is suitable for guardianship. Both descriptions are valid for the ruling to be attributed to them. This is the meaning of 'acting by the description': to make it a cause for the ruling in the original and to establish the ruling in the branch before suitability: which was mentioned as the first condition for the description. After it, the description depends on the second condition according to Abu Hanifa, which is effect, and it will be explained, and on 'ikhālah' according to al-Shafi'i. And its secret is what I mentioned earlier, so remember it. A legislative matter because the legislative causes that establish the ruling, which we are discussing, are only known to be correct from the legislative side if they are in accordance with the transmitted causes from the Salaf before this meaning appears. How can the description be acted upon? Because this meaning, i.e., suitability in the description, is like the validity of the witness, and without validity, testimony is not accepted. So too here. Due to necessity, as mentioned earlier, and it is like suitability.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the pillar of qiyas, specifically the conditions required for a description (wasf) to be used as a legal cause (ʿilla). The author explains that the description must have two qualities: ṣalāḥiyyah (validity) and ʿadālah (probity), analogous to the qualifications of a witness. Ṣalāḥiyyah means the description is suitable (mulāʾim) for the ruling, i.e., it can be reasonably attributed to the ruling and is not remote. For example, minority (ṣighar) is suitable for guardianship in marriage because it implies inability, unlike Islam which cannot be a cause for separation (as al-Shāfiʿī holds—rather the cause is non-acceptance of Islam). The author then contrasts the Hanafi and Shāfiʿī positions: Shāfiʿīs require only mulāʾamah (suitability) and do not need an additional condition of taʾthīr (effectiveness), while Ḥanafīs argue that mulāʾamah alone is insufficient; the description must also be effective (muʾaththir). This is illustrated with two examples: (1) The young non-virgin (thayyib ṣaghīrah) is under guardianship according to Ḥanafīs because minority exists, while Shāfiʿīs require virginity, so they do not impose guardianship on a young non-virgin. (2) The cat's non-impurity is explained by the Prophet's statement that it is among those who circle (ṭawwāfūn), indicating necessity—Ḥanafīs analogize this to guardianship: just as the cat's circling is suitable and effective for non-impurity due to necessity (difficulty of avoidance), so minority is suitable and effective for guardianship due to inability. The commentator stresses that acting on a description before establishing its suitability is invalid because suitability is like the ‘adālah of a witness. The difference between mulāʾamah and taʾthīr is crucial: Ḥanafīs require both, while Shāfiʿīs suffice with mulāʾamah alone.

Key Terms
الملائمة (al-mulāʾamah): كون الوصف موافقاً للحكم بحيث يصح إضافته إليه ولا يكون نائياً عنه
التأثير (al-taʾthīr): كون الوصف مؤثراً في الحكم بأن يكون مناطاً له في الشرع
الصلاحية (al-ṣalāḥiyyah): شرط في الوصف كالعقل والبلوغ في الشاهد
العدالة (al-ʿadālah): الديانة والاستقامة في الوصف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what additional condition is required for a description (wasf) to be considered a valid legal cause (ʿilla) beyond being suitable (mulāʾim)?
A) It must be explicitly mentioned in the Quran.
B) It must be effective (muʾaththir) in the ruling.
C) It must be agreed upon by the majority.
D) It must be from the category of 'āmm.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a description must be both suitable and effective to serve as a legal cause in qiyas; effectiveness is not automatically included in suitability.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Condition of Athar for Valid Illa in Qiyas
Explaining Hanafi requirement of athar after mulaimah for wasf as illa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi requirement of athar to determine whether a wasf (descriptive attribute) is a valid illa (cause) in qiyas.

Core Idea
A suitable attribute must show its effect by prior law; suitability alone is not enough for causality.

In this passage, the Hanafi school establishes a crucial second condition for a descriptive attribute (wasf) to serve as a legal cause (illa) in analogical reasoning (qiyas). While both Hanafis and Shafi'is agree that the attribute must be suitable (mulā'im) to the ruling, the Hanafis insist on an additional requirement: 'athar' (effect) – textual or consensual evidence that the Lawgiver has already recognized this attribute as a cause in a similar case. The commentator explains this using the analogy of a witness who must not only be qualified but also demonstrate probity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions for a wasf as a valid illa
From the passage, note that the first condition is mulaimah (suitability) and the second, for Hanafis, is athar (effect). Understand that without mulaimah, the attribute cannot be considered at all.
Both schools agree on mulaimah.
2
Distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions after mulaimah
The Hanafi school requires athar: the attribute must have been recognized as a cause in a prior text (nass) or consensus (ijma). The Shafi'i school requires only ikhala (correlation): mere mental perception of suitability.
This difference leads to practical consequences in accepting qiyas.
3
Analyze the witness analogy
The commentator compares the attribute to a witness: suitability (mulaimah) is like the witness's general qualifications (sane, adult, free, Muslim). Athar is like probity (adala) – without demonstrated trustworthiness, the testimony is not accepted. Similarly, without athar, the attribute may be rejected even if suitable.
This analogy shows why athar is necessary: the Lawgiver may reject a suitable attribute.
4
Recognize the four types of evidence for athar
The passage lists four ways textual or consensual evidence can show the effect: (1) same attribute in same ruling, (2) same attribute in same genus of ruling, (3) same genus of attribute in same ruling, (4) same genus of attribute in same genus of ruling. Each type establishes that the Lawgiver has recognized the attribute as a cause.
These types cover varying degrees of similarity between the precedent and the new case.
5
Apply the athar condition to a new scenario
Given a potential wasf, first check if it is mulā'im. If yes, then search for a prior nass or ijma where this wasf (or its genus) has been used as a cause for a similar ruling. If found, the wasf is valid as illa; if not, it is rejected according to the Hanafi school.
This step solidifies the practical operation of the rule.

Source Text

باب القياس
ركن القياس
فأشبهت البكر، فهذا تعليل بوصف ملائم؛ لأن الصغر مؤثر في ولاية المناكح لما أي تعليل ولاية النكاح يتصل به من العجز تأثير الطواف؛ لما يتصل به من الضرورة في الحكم المعلّل به في أي الصغر في عدم نجاسة الهرة قوله: الهرة ليست بنجسة، إنما هي من الطوافين والطوافات عليكم. و لا يصح العمل بالوصف قبل الملائمة؛ لأنه أمر شرعي، أي الوصف عليها عنده لعدم العلة، ويولي عليها عندنا أي يزوّجها الولي بلا رضاها فأشبهت البكر: الصغيرة؛ لأنها وصف الصغر موجود في كلتيهما، فكما أن البكر الصغيرة يولى عليها، فكذا الثيب الصغيرة. بوصف ملائم وهو الصغر، فإنه يليق أن يضاف إليه ولاية النكاح ولاية المناكح جمع منكح بضم الميم وفتح الكاف، فهو مصدر ميمي من الإنكاح أو بفتح الميم والكاف فهو ظرف زمان ومكان، أي ولاية تثبت في وقت النكاح أو في مكانه، وقيل: جمع منكوحة فهو ضعيف؛ لأن القياس مناكيح، وذلك لأن ولاية النكاح إنما ثبت بسبب عجز المولاة عليها، والعجز إنما يتحقق في الصغيره؛ إذ هي عاجزة عن التصرف في نفسها ومالها ولا تهتدي إليه سبيلا دون البكر؛ إذ البكر البالغة تعلم منافعها ومضارها فلا حاجة إلى الولاية فيها، وإليها أشار المصنف بقوله: لما يتصل إلخ. العجز عن التصرف فهذا الوصف مؤثر في ولاية النكاح. الحكم المعلّل به: وهو عدم نجاسة الهرة، فإنه حكم ثابت في قوله عليه: "الهرة ليست بنجسة" معلّل بالطواف، فعلة عدم نجاستها هي الطواف كما قال عليه: إنما هي أي الهرة (من) (الطوافين أي ذكور الطوافين (والطوافات)، فهذه الجملة وقعت موقع التعليل، فالحاصل أن علة ولاية النكاح عندنا الصغر، فهو موافق لوصف الطواف الذي علّل به النبي مع عدم نجاسة الهرة لكونهما مندرجين تحت جنس واحد وهو الضرورة، فكما أن الطواف في الهرة صار علة لعدم نجاسة الهرة للضرورة، وهي ههنا تعذر الاحتراز وصون الأواني عنها، فكذا الصغر في ولاية النكاح صار علة الولاية هنا العجز، فهذا التعليل موافق التعليله الا الله، فكما أن في تعليله وصف الطواف ملائم لحكم عدم النجاسة، فكذا وصف الصغر ملائم للولاية، فكلا الوصفين صالحان لأن ينسب إليهما الحكم، وهذا معنى العمل بالوصف: بأن يجعل علة للحكم في الأصل ويثبت به الحكم في الفرع قبل الملائمة: التي مرّ ذكرها الشرط الأول للوصف، فبعدها يتوقف الوصف على الشرط الثاني عند أبي حنيفة حاله وهو التأثير سيأتي بيانه، وعلى الإخالة عند الشافعي، وسره ما ذكرت آنفاً، فتذكره. أمر شرعي لأن العلل الشرعية المثبتة للحكم التي كلامنا فيها إنما يتعرّف صحتها من جانب الشرع إذا كانت موافقة للعلل المنقولة من السلف قبل ظهور هذا المعنى كيف يعمل بالوصف؛ لأن هذا المعنى أي الملائمة في الوصف بمنزلة الصلاحية للشاهد وبدون الصلاحية لا يقبل شهادة، فكذا ههنا.
للضرورة وهي آنفاً، وهي كما الملائمة.
وإذا ثبت الملائمة لم يجب العمل به إلا بعد العدالة عندنا، وهي الأثر؛ لأنه يحتمل التي هي التأثير الردّ مع قيام الملائمة، فيتعرّف صحته بظهور أثره في موضع من المواضع، من الشارع بسبب أي الوصف العمل به أي بالوصف الصالح، بل يجوز بمعنى إن عمل به نفذ العمل عندنا وأما عند أصحاب الشافعي فلا يجب العلم بعد الملائمة إلا بالإخالة، وذلك لأنه لا يجب للقاضي أن يقضي بشهادة رجل صالح للشهادة مستور الحال ما لم يظهر ديانته. نعم إن قضى جاز فكذا الحال في الوصف فلا يجب أن يعمل به ما لم يظهر عدالته قيام الملائمة كالشاهد يحتمل الرد مع قيام الصلاحية، وهي كونه عاقلاً بالغاً حراً مسلماً؛ إذ بعض من العقلاء الأحرار المسلمين البالغين فاسق، فهو مردود الشهادة، فكذا بعض الأوصاف صالح لأن يجعل علة للحكم، ولكنه غير مقبول عند الشارع؛ إذ الوصف لا يكون علة بنفسه بل يجعل الشارع. موضع من المواضع وهو أن يثبت بنص أو إجماع كون الوصف علة للحكم، وهذا يكون على أربعة أنواع: الأول أن يظهر أثر عين ذلك الوصف في عين سؤر الهرة، فإنه ثبت بقوله عليه كون الطواف علة لعين ذلك الحكم، وهو عدم نجاسة سؤر الهرة. والثاني أن يظهر أثر عين ذلك الوصف في جنس الحكم كالصغر، فإنه ظهر كونه علة في ولاية المال بالإجماع، وولاية المال جنس الحكم النكاح فيصح جعل الصغر علة في ولاية النكاح أيضاً المجانسة. والثالث أن يظهر أثر جنس الوصف في عين ذلك الحكم ثبت كونه علة لإسقاط الصلاة بالنص، والجنون جنس للإغماء، فلما ثبت كون الجنون علة لسقوط الصلاة، فصح جعل الإغماء أيضاً علة لسقوطها. والرابع أن يظهر أثر جنس الوصف في جنس ذلك الحكم كمشقة السفر، فإنه ثبت بالنص كونها علةً لسقوط الركعتين، فالمشقة جنس للحيض، وسقوط الركعتين جنس لسقوط الصلاة، فلاعتبار المجانسة صح جعل الحيض علة لسقوط الصلاة وإن ثبت الحكم وهو سقوط الصلاة عن الحائض بالقرآن؛ لأنه لم يثبت بنص وإجماع كون الحيض علة لسقوط الصلاة، فهو إنما يجعل العلة باعتبار جنسه وهو المشقة وكلامنا في تعين العلة بنص وإجماع لا في إثبات الأحكام، وسواء ثبت كون الوصف علة للحكم في ذلك النص الذي ثبت فيه الحكم كالطواف فإنه وصف وهو علة لحكم عدم نجاسة الهرة فعليته لهذا الحكم تثبت في ذلك الحديث الذي ورد فيه ذلك الحكم أو في غيره كالسكر، فإنه علة لحكم حرمة الخمر، فحرمة الخمر ثبت من القرآن. وأما كون السكر علة هذه الحرمة فلم يثبت من القرآن بل من بعض الأحاديث، كقوله عليه: "كل مسكر حرام"، الترمذي رقم: ٤٣٤٣] وسواء ثبت كون الوصف علة بصراحة النص أو الإجماع بأن يقول: هذا حرام لأجل هذا، أو لأنه كذا، أو علته كذا، أو بالإشارة والكناية بأن يقرن بالحكم ما لو لم يكن هو أو نظيره التعليل لكان بعيدا، الإخالة: الإخالة عند الشافعية تعيين العلة في الأصل بمجرد إبداء المناسبة بينها وبين العلم من ذات الأصل، لا بنص ولا بغيره، والحاصل بمجرد وقوع خيال عليته في قلب المجتهد بغير نظر إلى نص وشاهد آخر يحكم بعليته.
Chapter of Qiyas. Pillar of Qiyas: So it resembles the virgin, and this is a reasoning with a suitable attribute because minority (sighar) has an effect in the guardianship of marriages due to the helplessness connected to it, just as the effect of tawaf (the cat's frequenting) due to the necessity connected to it in the ruling being reasoned – i.e., minority – in the impurity of the cat. His statement: 'The cat is not impure; it is only among those who go around you frequently, both male and female.' And it is not valid to act upon the attribute before suitability (mulaimah) because it is a matter of shari'ah. The attribute is not accepted by him (the opponent) due to the absence of the cause, while with us he (the guardian) exercises authority over her – i.e., the guardian marries her without her consent – so she resembles the virgin minor because the attribute of minority exists in both. So just as the virgin minor is under guardianship, so too the non-virgin minor, with a suitable attribute (mulaim) which is minority. For it is fitting that the guardianship of marriage be attributed to it. 'Guardianship of marriages' (wilayat al-manakih) is the plural of 'mankih' with damm on meem and fatha on kaf, it is a maSdar mimi from inkah, or with fatha on meem and kaf, it is a time or place adverbial, i.e., guardianship established at the time of marriage or its place. It is said: plural of mankuha, but this is weak because the qiyas is manakih. And that is because the guardianship of marriage is established due to the helplessness of the one under guardianship, and helplessness is actualized only in the minor; for she is incapable of managing herself and her wealth and cannot find the way, unlike the virgin adult; for the adult virgin knows her benefits and harms, so there is no need for guardianship over her. To this the author pointed by his saying: 'due to what is connected, etc.' – helplessness in managing. So this attribute is effective in the guardianship of marriage. The ruling being reasoned is the non-impurity of the cat; for it is a ruling established in his statement: 'The cat is not impure' reasoned by tawaf. So the cause of its non-impurity is tawaf as he said: 'It is only one of those who go around you frequently, male and female.' This sentence takes the position of reasoning. So the conclusion is that the cause of guardianship of marriage with us is minority, and it is in agreement with the attribute of tawaf with which the Prophet reasoned the non-impurity of the cat because both fall under one genus which is necessity. So just as tawaf in the cat became the cause for the non-impurity of the cat due to necessity – and here it is the difficulty of avoiding it and protecting vessels from it – so minority in the guardianship of marriage became the cause of guardianship here, which is helplessness. So this reasoning agrees with that reasoning. So just as in that reasoning the attribute of tawaf is suitable for the ruling of non-impurity, so the attribute of minority is suitable for guardianship. Both attributes are valid to be attributed to the ruling. And this is the meaning of acting upon the attribute: making it a cause for the ruling in the origin and establishing the ruling in the branch before suitability (mulaimah) – which is the first condition of the attribute. After it, the attribute depends on the second condition according to Abu Hanifa, which is effect (ta'thir), as will be explained, and on ikhala according to al-Shafi'i. And the secret of what I mentioned earlier, so remember it. It is a shari'ah matter because the shari'ah causes that establish rulings, which we are discussing, are only known to be valid from the side of the Lawgiver if they are in agreement with the causes transmitted from the predecessors before the appearance of this meaning. How is the attribute acted upon? Because this meaning – i.e., suitability in the attribute – is like the qualification of a witness; without qualification, his testimony is not accepted. So here too. Due to necessity, which is earlier, and it is like suitability. And when suitability is established, it is not necessary to act upon it except after probity (adala) according to us, which is the effect (athar) – because it is possible that it be rejected even with suitability. So its correctness is known by the appearance of its effect in some place, from the Lawgiver due to the attribute acting upon it – i.e., upon the suitable attribute. Rather, it is permissible in the sense that if he acts upon it, the action is valid according to us. As for the followers of al-Shafi'i, it is not necessary after suitability except through ikhala. That is because it is not necessary for a judge to give judgment based on the testimony of a man qualified for testimony whose probity is hidden until his trustworthiness appears. Yes, if he judges, it is valid. So the case is similar for the attribute: it is not necessary to act upon it until its probity appears, even if suitability is present. It is like a witness who may be rejected even with qualification – i.e., being sane, adult, free, Muslim – because some of the sane free adult Muslims are sinners, so his testimony is rejected. So too some attributes are suitable to be made a cause for a ruling, but they are not accepted by the Lawgiver, because an attribute is not a cause by itself; rather, the Lawgiver makes it a cause. A place (type) is that the attribute being a cause for the ruling is established by text or consensus. This occurs in four types: First – that the effect of the very attribute appears in the very same ruling, like tawaf: it is established by his statement that tawaf is the cause for the very same ruling, i.e., the non-impurity of the cat's leftovers. Second – that the effect of the very attribute appears in the genus of the ruling, like minority: it has appeared as a cause in guardianship of property by consensus, and guardianship of property is of the genus of the ruling of marriage, so it is valid to make minority a cause in the guardianship of marriage also due to congruence. Third – that the effect of the genus of the attribute appears in the very same ruling, like unconsciousness: it is established as a cause for the dropping of prayer by text, and insanity is a genus of unconsciousness. So when it is established that insanity is a cause for dropping prayer, it is valid to make unconsciousness a cause for its dropping. Fourth – that the effect of the genus of the attribute appears in the genus of that ruling, like the hardship of travel: it is established by text as a cause for dropping two rak'ats, so hardship is a genus for menstruation, and dropping two rak'ats is a genus for dropping prayer. So by considering congruence, it is valid to make menstruation a cause for dropping prayer, even if the ruling – i.e., dropping prayer for the menstruating woman – is established by the Quran; because it is not established by text or consensus that menstruation is a cause for dropping prayer. Rather, it is made a cause by considering its genus, which is hardship. Our discussion is about specifying the cause by text or consensus, not about establishing rulings. And it is the same whether the attribute being a cause for the ruling is established in the very text that established the ruling – like tawaf is an attribute and a cause for the ruling of non-impurity of the cat, so its causality is established in the hadith that mentioned that ruling – or in another text – like intoxication: it is a cause for the ruling of prohibition of wine, so the prohibition of wine is established from the Quran. As for intoxication being the cause of this prohibition, it is not established from the Quran but from some hadiths, like his statement: 'Every intoxicant is forbidden' (Tirmidhi no. 4343). And it is the same whether the attribute being a cause is established by express text or consensus – e.g., 'This is forbidden because of this' or 'because it is such' or 'its cause is such' – or by implication and allusion – e.g., when something is linked with a ruling such that if it or its like were not the reasoning, it would be far-fetched. Ikhala: According to the Shafi'is, ikhala is specifying the cause in the origin simply by showing the appropriateness between it and the ruling from the origin itself, not by text or anything else. The upshot is that merely the idea of its causality occurs in the heart of the mujtahid without looking to a text or another indicator that decides its causality.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the pillar of qiyas, specifically the conditions for accepting a descriptive attribute (wasf) as a valid legal cause (illa). The commentator begins by illustrating the principle of suitability (mulaimah) using the example of guardianship over a minor: a non-virgin minor is like a virgin minor in that both require a guardian because of the attribute of minority, which is suitable for guardianship. He then explains that suitability alone is not sufficient; the attribute must also have an effect (athar) that is evidenced by text or consensus. This is the Hanafi position: after establishing mulaimah, the second condition is 'athar' (also called 'ta'thir' or 'adala' – probity). The text compares this to a witness: a qualified witness (adult, free, Muslim) may still be rejected unless his trustworthiness is demonstrated; similarly, a suitable attribute may not be accepted as a cause until its effect is shown. On the other hand, the Shafi'is require only 'ikhala' (correlation), i.e., the mere appropriateness of the attribute to the ruling without requiring external evidence. The commentator then details the four types of evidence for athar: (1) same attribute in same ruling (e.g., tawaf for cat's purity), (2) same attribute in same genus of ruling (e.g., minority for guardianship of property, then used for marriage), (3) same genus of attribute in same ruling (e.g., insanity as genus for unconsciousness in dropping prayer), and (4) same genus of attribute in same genus of ruling (e.g., hardship as genus for menstruation for dropping prayer). He clarifies that this process is about specifying the cause (ta'yin al-illa) by text/consensus, not about proving the ruling itself. The passage thus establishes a key Hanafi usul principle: a cause must be 'manqula' (transmitted) from the Lawgiver, not merely derived by reason.

Key Terms
الملائمة (al-mulā'imah): The first condition for a valid descriptive attribute (wasf) as a cause (illa) in qiyas: the attribute must be suitable (mutanāsib) for the ruling, i.e., it is appropriate to be the cause based on its intrinsic relation to the ruling.
الأثر (al-athar): The second condition for a wasf to be a valid cause according to the Hanafis: a prior instance (nass or ijma) must demonstrate that the wasf has an effect (ta'thir) in a similar ruling, proving that the Lawgiver recognizes it as a cause.
الإخالة (al-ikhālah): Shafi'i method of specifying the cause: mere mental correlation (zann) that the attribute is suitable for the ruling, without needing textual or consensual evidence of its effect. The cause is identified by the mujtahid's perception of appropriateness.
الوصف (al-waṣf): The descriptive attribute in the original case (aṣl) that is considered as a potential cause (illa) for the ruling. It must be suitable (mulā'im) and, per Hanafis, have an effect (athar) to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following is the second condition (after mulaimah) for a descriptive attribute (wasf) to be accepted as a valid legal cause (illa) in qiyas?
A) Ikhālah (correlation) – the mere suitability of the wasf to the ruling
B) Athar (effect) – the wasf must be shown to have been a cause in a prior text or consensus
C) Qiyās (analogy) – the wasf must be derived from another qiyas
D) Istihsān (juristic preference) – the wasf must be deemed better by the mujtahid

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a suitable attribute for qiyas must also have an 'athar' – evidence of its effect from a previous text or consensus.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Requirement of 'Athar (Effect) for the Validity of 'Illa in Qiyas
Ruling on a condition for qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires a proven effect (athar) for an attribute to be accepted as 'illa in qiyas, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i reliance on mere suitability.

Core Idea
An attribute's suitability is insufficient; its effect must be proven by nass or ijma, just as a witness's integrity must be established.

Welcome to this lesson on the condition of 'athar for the validity of 'illa. In qiyas, the 'illa is the cause that links the original case to a new case. The Hanafi school insists that an attribute must not only be suitable but its effect must be demonstrated in at least one instance by nass or ijma. This lesson unpacks that requirement and contrasts it with the Shafi'i approach, which accepts mere imagination of suitability (ikhala). You will encounter the four ways in which effect can be established, along with concrete examples from the texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition
The passage states that establishing suitability (mulā'ama) does not obligate acting on the attribute as 'illa until its 'adāla (integrity) is known, which here refers to its effect (athar). This effect must be proven by nass (text) or ijma (consensus).
This is the foundational principle of the lesson.
2
Understand the witness analogy
Just as a judge does not accept a person's testimony until his actual reliability ('adāla) appears—even if he is generally qualified (sane, adult, free, Muslim)—so too an attribute, though suitable, is not accepted until its effect is shown.
The analogy highlights that suitability does not guarantee actual validity.
3
Explore the four types of established effect
The passage categorises how effect can be established: (1) exact attribute on exact ruling (e.g., tawaf for cat's saliva), (2) exact attribute on genus of ruling (e.g., childhood for guardianship of property analogised to marriage), (3) genus of attribute on exact ruling (e.g., insanity as genus for fainting in dropping prayer), (4) genus on genus (e.g., hardship of travel for menstruation in dropping prayer).
These categories show the scope of the condition.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school accepts 'ikhāla' (mere imagination of suitability) without requiring a proven effect. The Hanafi response is that just as a witness may be rejected despite apparent suitability, so too an attribute may be rejected until its effect is evident.
This disagreement leads to practical differences in accepting qiyas.
5
Apply the concept to a textual example
The hadith 'Every intoxicant is unlawful' (kull muskar haram) explicitly links intoxication to prohibition. For Hanafis, this nass proves that intoxication is the 'illa for the prohibition of wine and other intoxicants, fulfilling the condition of athar.
This demonstrates how a text can establish a proven effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القياس
ركن القياس
وإذا ثبت الملائمة لم يجب العمل به إلا بعد العدالة عندنا، وهي الأثر؛ لأنه يحتمل الرد مع قيام الملائمة، فيتعرّف صحته بظهور أثره في موضع من المواضع، من الشارع بسبب أي الوصف العمل به أي بالوصف الصالح، بل يجوز بمعنى إن عمل به نفذ العمل عندنا وأما عند أصحاب الشافعي فلا يجب العلم بعد الملائمة إلا بالإخالة، وذلك لأنه لا يجب للقاضي أن يقضي بشهادة رجل صالح للشهادة مستور الحال ما لم يظهر ديانته. نعم إن قضى جاز فكذا الحال في الوصف فلا يجب أن يعمل به ما لم يظهر عدالته قيام الملائمة كالشاهد يحتمل الرد مع قيام الصلاحية، وهي كونه عاقلاً بالغاً حراً مسلماً؛ إذ بعض من العقلاء الأحرار المسلمين البالغين فاسق، فهو مردود الشهادة، فكذا بعض الأوصاف صالح لأن يجعل علة للحكم، ولكنه غير مقبول عند الشارع؛ إذ الوصف لا يكون علة بنفسه بل يجعل الشارع. موضع من المواضع وهو أن يثبت بنص أو إجماع كون الوصف علة للحكم، وهذا يكون على أربعة أنواع: الأول أن يظهر أثر عين ذلك الوصف في عين ذلك الحكم، كالطواف فإنه ثبت بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام كون الطواف علة لعدم نجاسة سؤر الهرة. والثاني أن يظهر أثر عين ذلك الوصف في جنس الحكم كالصغر، فإنه ظهر كونه علة في ولاية المال بالإجماع، وولاية المال جنس لولاية النكاح فيصح جعل الصغر علة في ولاية النكاح أيضاً بالمجانسة. والثالث أن يظهر أثر جنس الوصف في عين ذلك الحكم كالإغماء، فإن الجنون ثبت كونه علة لإسقاط الصلاة بالنص، والجنون جنس للإغماء، فلما ثبت كون الجنون علة لسقوط الصلاة، فصح جعل الإغماء أيضاً علة لسقوطها. والرابع أن يظهر أثر جنس الوصف في جنس ذلك الحكم كمشقة السفر، فإنه ثبت بالنص كونها علةً لسقوط الركعتين، فالمشقة جنس للحيض، وسقوط الركعتين جنس لسقوط الصلاة، فلاعتبار المجانسة صح جعل الحيض علة لسقوط الصلاة وإن ثبت الحكم وهو سقوط الصلاة عن الحائض بالقرآن؛ لأنه لم يثبت بنص وإجماع كون الحيض علة لسقوط الصلاة، فهو إنما يجعل العلة باعتبار جنسه وهو المشقة وكلامنا في تعين العلة بنص وإجماع لا في إثبات الأحكام، وسواء ثبت كون الوصف علة للحكم في ذلك النص الذي ثبت فيه الحكم كالطواف فإنه وصف وهو علة لحكم عدم نجاسة الهرة فعليته لهذا الحكم تثبت في ذلك الحديث الذي ورد فيه ذلك الحكم أو في غيره كالسكر، فإنه علة لحكم حرمة الخمر، فحرمة الخمر ثبت من القرآن. وأما كون السكر علة هذه الحرمة فلم يثبت من القرآن بل من بعض الأحاديث، كقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "كل مسكر حرام"، [الترمذي رقم: ٤٣٤٣] وسواء ثبت كون الوصف علة بصراحة النص أو الإجماع بأن يقول: هذا حرام لأجل هذا، أو لأنه كذا، أو علته كذا، أو بالإشارة والكناية بأن يقرن بالحكم ما لو لم يكن هو أو نظيره التعليل لكان بعيدا، الإخالة: الإخالة عند الشافعية تعيين العلة في الأصل بمجرد إبداء المناسبة بينها وبين العلم من ذات الأصل، لا بنص ولا بغيره، والحاصل بمجرد وقوع خيال عليته في قلب المجتهد بغير نظر إلى نص وشاهد آخر يحكم بعليته.
Chapter of Qiyas. Pillar of Qiyas: When suitability is established, it is not obligatory to act upon it except after 'adala according to us, which is the effect; because it is possible to reject it despite suitability, so its validity is known by the appearance of its effect in one of the places from the Lawgiver, due to the attribute. Acting upon it means acting upon the suitable attribute; rather, it is permitted in the sense that if one acts upon it, it is effective according to us. As for the followers of al-Shafi'i, knowledge after suitability is not necessary except by ikhtila (mere imagination of suitability). That is because it is not required for a judge to pass judgment based on the testimony of a person fit for testimony whose state is concealed until his integrity appears. Yes, if he judges, it is valid. So is the case with the attribute: one should not act upon it until its reliability appears despite suitability, like the witness, it is possible to reject him despite his suitability, which is that he be sane, adult, free, Muslim; because some of the sane, free, adult Muslims are sinful, so his testimony is rejected. Similarly, some attributes are suitable to be made the cause of the ruling, but they are not accepted by the Lawgiver; because the attribute does not become a cause by itself, but the Lawgiver makes it so. The place (i.e., the condition) is that it be established by text or consensus that the attribute is a cause for the ruling. This is of four types: The first: that the effect of the exact attribute appears on the exact ruling, like tawaf, as it is established by his statement, peace be upon him, that tawaf is the cause for the non-impurity of the leftover water of a cat. The second: that the effect of the exact attribute appears on the genus of the ruling, like childhood: it appears to be a cause for the guardianship of property by consensus, and guardianship of property is a genus for guardianship of marriage, so it is valid to make childhood a cause for guardianship of marriage also by similarity. The third: that the effect of the genus of the attribute appears on the exact ruling, like fainting: insanity is established as a cause for dropping prayer by text, and insanity is the genus of fainting; so when insanity is established as a cause for dropping prayer, it is valid to make fainting also a cause for dropping it. The fourth: that the effect of the genus of the attribute appears on the genus of that ruling, like the hardship of travel: it is established by text as a cause for dropping two rak'ats; hardship is a genus for menstruation, and dropping two rak'ats is a genus for dropping prayer; by considering similarity, it is valid to make menstruation a cause for dropping prayer, even though the ruling (dropping prayer for the menstruating woman) is established by the Qur'an; because it is not established by text or consensus that menstruation is the cause for dropping prayer; it is only made a cause by considering its genus, which is hardship. Our discussion is about specifying the cause by text and consensus, not about establishing rulings. It is the same whether the attribute is established as a cause for the ruling in the same text in which the ruling is established, like tawaf: it is an attribute and a cause for the ruling of non-impurity of the cat's leftover, its causality for this ruling is established in that hadith in which that ruling came; or in other than it, like intoxication: it is a cause for the ruling of the prohibition of wine; the prohibition of wine is established from the Qur'an. As for intoxication being the cause of this prohibition, it is not established from the Qur'an but from some hadith, like his statement: 'Every intoxicant is unlawful' [Al-Tirmidhi no. 4343]. And it is the same whether the attribute is established as a cause by explicit text or consensus, such as saying: 'This is unlawful because of this', or 'because it is such', or 'its cause is such', or by indication and allusion, such as when it is connected to the ruling such that if it or its like were not the cause, it would be far-fetched. Al-Ikhala: Al-Ikhala according to the Shafi'is is specifying the cause in the original by merely presenting the suitability between it and the ruling from the original itself, not by text or otherwise; it is simply the occurrence of an imagined causality in the heart of the mujtahid without reference to a text or other evidence that confirms its causality.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on a condition for the validity of qiyas. It explains that for an attribute to be considered a valid 'illa (cause) for a legal ruling, it is not sufficient that it be suitable (munasib); rather, it must also have a proven effect (athar) in a particular instance established by nass (text) or ijma (consensus). This is the Hanafi position, which requires 'adala (integrity) of the attribute, likening it to a witness who, although possessing general qualifications (sanity, adulthood, freedom, Islam), may be rejected until his actual reliability is known. The text contrasts this with the Shafi'i school, which accepts mere ikhala (imagination of suitability) without requiring a proven effect. The text then details four ways in which the effect can be established: (1) the exact attribute's effect on the exact ruling, (2) exact attribute on genus of ruling, (3) genus of attribute on exact ruling, (4) genus of attribute on genus of ruling. Examples are given: tawaf (circumambulation) causing permissibility of using a cat's leftover water, childhood causing guardianship (over property and marriage), insanity/ fainting causing dropping of prayer, and hardship of travel causing reduction of prayer, analogically extended to menstruation causing dropping of prayer. The text emphasizes that proof of causality can come from the same text as the ruling or another, and can be explicit or implicit. This sets the Hanafi requirement of a specific evidentiary basis for the 'illa, stricter than the Shafi'i reliance on suitability alone.

Key Terms
الأثر (al-athar): The visible effect of a proposed 'illa in a specific instance, established by nass or ijma, proving its validity as a cause.
الإخالة (al-ikhala): The Shafi'i concept that a cause is specified by mere imagination of its suitability without needing text or other evidence.
الملائمة (al-mulā'ama): Suitability or compatibility of the attribute with the ruling; a necessary but not sufficient condition for 'illa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, what is required for a suitable attribute to be accepted as the 'illa (cause) in qiyas?
A) Mere suitability (munasaba)
B) Proven effect (athar) by nass or ijma
C) Consensus of all jurists
D) Explicit mention in the Quran

Key Takeaway
A suitable attribute must have its effect proven by nass or ijma to be accepted as 'illa in qiyas.

Qiyas vs Istihsan: The Case of Sujud al-Tilawah
Debates whether ruku' can substitute sujud in tilawah prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that hidden effect (athar batin) can outweigh apparent effect in preferring qiyas over istihsan, using the case of ruku' substituting for sujud in tilawah prostration.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a hidden but strong ‘illah can make qiyas preferable to istihsan, even when istihsan appears stronger at first sight.

This passage examines a classic usul dispute: when a person in prayer hears a verse requiring sajdat al-tilawah, can they bow (ruku‘) instead of prostrating (sujud)? One argument (qiyas) permits it because both acts express humility; the other (istihsan) forbids it because the law specifically commands sujud. The Hanafi text ultimately favors qiyas, revealing that the hidden rationale (athar batin) can be stronger than the apparent literal difference. Understanding this methodological preference is key to grasping how Hanafi jurists weigh conflicting evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting positions
State the qiyas position (ruku‘ substitutes for sujud) and the istihsan position (ruku‘ does not suffice). Note their initial apparent strengths.
The qiyas relies on a metaphorical reading of Quran 38:24; the istihsan relies on the literal command to prostrate.
2
Examine the apparent proofs
Read the dalil for each: the Quranic verse for qiyas, and the shar‘ command for istihsan. Note why istihsan appears stronger initially (literal meaning vs metaphor).
3
Analyze the hidden effect (athar batin)
Dig deeper: what is the true purpose of sajdat al-tilawah? The text argues it is not an intended act of worship (qurbah maqsudah) but mere humility. Both ruku‘ and sujud share the ‘illah of humility, making the qiyas internally strong despite its external weakness.
The hidden effect is derived from the fact that sajdat al-tilawah is not binding by vow.
4
Understand the classification of istihsan
The passage concludes by categorizing istihsan into four types: bi al-athar, bi al-ijma‘, bi al-darurah, and bi al-qiyas al-khafi. Here, the istihsan is based on qiyas khafi, which can be extended to other cases.
This shows that istihsan is not monolithic; its strength varies by type.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi may intentionally bow with the intention of sajdat al-tilawah and it suffices; the opposing view requires a separate prostration. This shows the real-world impact of the methodological preference.

باب القياس
الاستحسان
في صلاته أنه يركع بها قياساً؛ لأن النص قد ورد به، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وخر راكعاً و أناب﴾، وفي الاستحسان لا يجزئه؛ لأن الشرع أمرنا بالسجود والركوع خلافه أي لا يكفي وهو غاية التعظيم كسجود الصلاة، فهذا أثر ظاهر، فأما وجه القياس فمجاز محض لكن القياس أولى من الاستحسان بأثره الباطن بيانه أن السجود عند التلاوة لم يشرع قربةً مقصودة حتى لايلزم بالنذر، وإنما المقصود مجرد ما يصلح تواضعاً،
وجه القياس أن الركوع والسجود متشابهات في الخضوع، ولذا أطلق اسم الركوع على السجود في تلك الآية، وذلك لأن الخرور وهو أن يقع على الأرض لا يتحقق في حالة الركوع بل في حالة السجدة، فظهر أن المراد بالركوع في تلك الآية هو السجدة، فلما ثبت أن الركوع والسجود متشابهان في الخضوع، والمقصود في سجود التلاوة هو الخضوع، فيجوز الركوع قياساً على السجدة لاشتراك وصف الخضوع بينهما. خلافه أي دونه في التعظيم ولهذا لا ينوب أحدهما مقام الآخر في الصلاة، فكذا في سجدة التلاوة، وإلى هذا أشار بقوله: "كسجود الصلاة لا يتأدّى بالركوع إلخ." فهذا أي كون الركوع غير السجود وعدم كفاية عن الآخر أثر ظاهر في بادي النظر، وأما بنظر دقيق ففيه فساد، ولهذا رجّح القياس عليه، وأما القياس ففي بادي النظر فيه ضعف، ولذا سمي القياس المقابل له بالاستحسان وإليه أشار بقوله: "فأما إلخ." وجه القياس أي وجه ضعف القياس في بادي النظر "فمجاز محض" أي ثبوته بالمجاز؛ لأنه تعالى أقام الركوع مقام السجود باعتبار المشابهة في التقرب والمجاز في مقابلة الحقيقة ضعيف، وقد كان بناء القياس على المجاز، وبناء الاستحسان على الحقيقة، فهذا وجه ظهور أثر الاستحسان وفساد القياس في بادي الرأي. بأثره الباطن والحاصل إن كان القياس في بادي الرأي فاسداً والاستحسان صحيحا لكن بالنظر الدقيق القياس أولى من الاستحسان؛ لأن اثر القياس في الباطن قوي وأثر الاستحسان ضعيف، فبيّن الأول بقوله: "بيانه" أني بيان أثر الباطن للقياس. لا يلزم بالنذر: فلو كان قربة مقصودة لوجب بالنذر فهذا دليل على كونه غير قربة مقصودة ما يصلح تواضعاً ليتميّز المطيع المنقاد عن العاصي المتكبر كما يدل عليه آيات السجود، منها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ يَسْجُدُ مَنْ فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ طَوْعاً وَكَرْهاً﴾ (الرعد: ١٥)، ومنها قوله تعالى: ﴿أَلَمْ تَرَ أَنَّ اللَّهَ يَسْجُدُ لَهُ مَنْ فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَمَنْ فِي الْأَرْضِ﴾ (الحج:۱۸)، أي يتواضع له أهل السماء والأرض، فعلم أن المقصود من السجود في تلك المواضع التواضع.
وذلك: أي كون المراد من الركوع في آية السجدة.
والركوع في الصلاة يعمل هذا العمل بخلاف سجود الصلاة والركوع في غيرها، فصار الأثر الخفي مع الفساد الظاهر أولى من الأثر الظاهر مع الفساد الخفي، وهذا كما هو في القياس المذكور

وأما القسم الأول فأكثر من أن يحصى. ثم المستحسن بالقياس الخفي يصح تعديته
ووجه
هذا العمل: أي يحصل منه هذا المقصود، فيجوز أن ينوب أحدهما مناب الآخر، فجاز الركوع مقام السجود بنية التداخل لاشتراك العلة. وهي التواضع، فهذا أثر باطن للقياس، وأما ضعف الباطن للاستحسان فبينه بقوله: بخلاف إلخ. سجود الصلاة: بل هو قربة مقصودة حتى يلزم بالنذر، فلما كان قربة مقصودة فلايتأدّى بغيره. غيرها: أي الصلاة، حيث لا ينوب عن سجود التلاوة، وحاصله أن قياسكم لسجود التلاوة على سجود الصلاة حيث قلتم: "كما لا يتأدى سجود الصلاة بغيره" فكذا سجود التلاوة لايتأدى بغيره من الركوع، وكذا قياسكم للركوع في الصلاة على الركوع في غير الصلاة حيث قلتم كما أن الركوع في غير الصلاة لاينوب عن سجدة التلاوة فكذا الركوع في الصلاة ينبغي أن لاينوب عنها" فاسد في إمعان النظر وإن كان في بادي الرأي صحيحاً، الفساد أن السجود في الصلاة قربة مقصودة، وسجود التلاوة ليس على هذا الوصف، فكيف يصح أن يقاس أحدهما على الآخر في عدم أداء السجود بغيره، وإن الركوع في غير الصلاة ليس بعبادة، والركوع في الصلاة عبادة، والشرط فيما يتأدّى به السجود أن يكون عبادة، فكيف يصح أن يقاس أحد الركوعين على الآخر في أداء سجود التلاوة. به وهذا أي ترجيح القياس على الاستحسان. القسم الأول: وهو يترجح الاستحسان على القياس أن يحصى فمن شاء أن يطلع على أمثلته فليرجع إلى الهداية، فإنه مملوّ من هذا القسم، فلذا ما أوردنا مثالاً له اعلم أن الاستحسان دليل يعارض القياس الجلي، والدليل المعارض للقياس الجلي نص وإجماع وضرورة وقد يكون القياس الخفي، فيقال في الأول: الاستحسان بالأثر، وفي الثاني: الاستحسان بالإجماع، وفي الثالث: الاستحسان بالضرورة، وفي الرابع: الاستحسان بالقياس، وكما يثبت بالقياس الجلي حكم شرعي يثبت بكل واحد من تلك الأقسام الأربعة، لكن الحكم الثابت بالقياس الجلي يتعدى إلى غيره، وأما الحكم الثابت بتلك الأقسام فقد يتعدّى وقد لا، فأراد المصنف أن يبين المتعدّي وغير المتعدي فقال: ثم المستحسن بالفتح وهو الحكم الثابت بالاستحسان تعديته إلى غيره؛ لأنه قياس من كل وجوه، غير أن أثره القوي خفي.
عدم
Chapter of Qiyas (Analogy). Istihsan (Juristic Preference). Regarding his prayer, that he bows (rukū‘) in it by qiyās, because the text (naṣṣ) has mentioned it: Allah said: 'and he fell down bowing and repented' (Quran 38:24). And in istihsān it does not suffice, because the law (shar‘) commanded us to prostrate and bowing is different from it, i.e., it does not suffice, and it is the utmost veneration like the prostration of prayer; so this is a manifest effect (athar ẓāhir). As for the aspect of qiyās, it is pure metaphor (majāz maḥḍ). But qiyās is preferable to istihsān due to its hidden effect (athar bāṭin). Explanation: The prostration at the recitation was not legislated as an intended act of worship (qurbah maqṣūdah) such that it would be binding by vow (nadhr); rather, the purpose is mere humility (tawāḍu‘). The aspect of qiyās: bowing and prostrating are similar in humility, and for that reason the name 'bowing' was applied to prostration in that verse, because falling (khurūr), which means falling to the ground, is not realized in the state of bowing but in the state of prostration. So it appears that what is meant by 'bowing' in that verse is prostration. Since it is established that bowing and prostration are similar in humility, and the purpose in the prostration of recitation is humility, it is permissible to bow by analogy with prostration due to the shared attribute of humility. Its opposite, i.e., less in veneration, and thus one does not substitute for the other in prayer; likewise in prostration of recitation. This is what he indicated by saying: 'Like the prostration of prayer, it is not performed by bowing, etc.' So this (i.e., that bowing is not prostration and one does not suffice for the other) is a manifest effect in initial opinion. But upon precise examination, there is corruption in it, and therefore qiyās was preferred over it. As for qiyās, there is weakness in it at first glance, so the qiyās opposing it is called istihsān. He indicated this by saying: 'As for, etc.' The aspect of qiyās: i.e., the weakness of qiyās at first glance is 'pure metaphor' i.e., its establishment is via metaphor; because Allah Most High placed bowing in the position of prostration considering the similarity in drawing near, and metaphor is weak in contrast to literal meaning. Qiyās was built on metaphor, and istihsān was built on literal meaning; this is the aspect of the appearance of the effect of istihsān and the corruption of qiyās at first sight. By its hidden effect: The conclusion: If qiyās is corrupted at first sight and istihsān is sound, but upon precise examination, qiyās is preferable to istihsān because the effect of qiyās internally is strong and the effect of istihsān is weak. He explained the first by saying: 'Explanation' that is, an explanation of the hidden effect of qiyās. 'It is not binding by vow': if it were an intended act of worship, it would be obligatory by vow; this is evidence that it is not an intended act of worship, but mere humility to distinguish the obedient, submissive person from the disobedient, arrogant one, as indicated by the verses of prostration, including His saying: 'And to Allah prostrates whoever is in the heavens and the earth, willingly or unwillingly' (Quran 13:15), and His saying: 'Do you not see that to Allah prostrates whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on the earth' (Quran 22:18), i.e., the inhabitants of the heavens and earth humble themselves to Him. So it is known that the purpose of prostration in these contexts is humility. 'That': i.e., that what is meant by 'bowing' in the verse of prostration... And bowing in prayer accomplishes this action, unlike the prostration of prayer and bowing outside of it. So the hidden effect with apparent corruption is better than the apparent effect with hidden corruption, and this is like in the mentioned qiyās. The first category: it is rare that istihsān outweighs qiyās; let him who wishes to see examples refer to Al-Hidāyah, for it is full of this category, so we did not provide an example for it. Know that istihsān is an evidence (dalīl) that opposes manifest analogy (qiyās jalī). The evidence opposing manifest analogy is text (naṣṣ), consensus (ijmā‘), necessity (ḍarūrah), and it may be hidden analogy (qiyās khafī). So it is said in the first: istihsān bi al-athar (by textual evidence); in the second: istihsān bi al-ijmā‘ (by consensus); in the third: istihsān bi al-ḍarūrah (by necessity); in the fourth: istihsān bi al-qiyās (by analogy). And just as a legal ruling is established by manifest analogy, it is established by each of these four categories, but the ruling established by manifest analogy extends to other cases, while the ruling established by those categories may or may not extend. So the author wanted to explain the extendable and non-extendable, saying: 'Then the mustaḥsan (the ruling established by istihsān) may be extended to other cases because it is analogy in all respects, except that its strong effect is hidden.' Lack.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a technical discussion in Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh about the methodological conflict between qiyās (analogy) and istiḥsān (juristic preference). The specific case is whether, during prayer, a person who hears a verse requiring sajdat al-tilāwah (prostration of recitation) can substitute rukū‘ (bowing) for sujūd (prostration). The qiyās argument uses the Quranic verse 'wa kharra rāki‘an wa anāb' (Quran 38:24) where the word 'rāki‘' (bowing) is interpreted as meaning 'sājid' (prostrating) because falling to the ground (khurūr) is characteristic of prostration, not bowing. This is a metaphorical use (majāz), which is initially weak. The istiḥsān argument counters that the law requires prostration itself, and since bowing is a different act (one is lesser veneration), it cannot substitute. This is the ẓāhir (apparent) ruling with a strong initial effect. However, upon deeper analysis, the qiyās argument is found to be stronger because its hidden effect (athar bāṭin) is weighty: sajdat al-tilāwah is not an intended act of worship (qurbah maqṣūdah) as it is not binding by vow, but merely a display of humility (tawāḍu‘). Since bowing also expresses humility, it fulfills the same purpose. Thus, the hidden strength of qiyās (the shared attribute of humility) outweighs the apparent strength of istiḥsān (the difference in form). The passage concludes by categorizing istiḥsān into four types: bi al-athar (based on textual evidence), bi al-ijmā‘ (consensus), bi al-ḍarūrah (necessity), and bi al-qiyās al-khafī (hidden analogy). The author notes that rulings established by qiyās jalī (manifest analogy) are always extendable to new cases, while those established by istiḥsān may or may not be extendable. In this case, the istiḥsān is based on qiyās khafī (hidden analogy), so it is extendable. The Hanafi position here is that despite initial appearances, qiyās is preferred over istiḥsān, and the ruling that rukū‘ can substitute for sujūd in sajdat al-tilāwah during prayer is valid.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): A legal method where a ruling is preferred over the apparent qiyās due to a stronger evidence: text, consensus, necessity, or hidden analogy.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical deduction applying an effective cause ('illah) from an original case (aṣl) to a new case (far‘).
أثر باطن (athar bāṭin): The hidden effect or underlying rationale of a ruling, as opposed to its apparent aspect (athar ẓāhir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi text conclude that qiyās (analogy) is preferable to istihsān (juristic preference) in the case of substituting rukū‘ for sujūd in sajdat al-tilāwah?
A) Because the Quran explicitly commands rukū‘ in that context.
B) Because the hidden effect (athar bāṭin) of qiyās is stronger: both acts share the same effective cause ('illah) of humility, and the prostration is not an intended act of worship.
C) Because the apparent effect (athar ẓāhir) of istihsān is weak.
D) Because ijma‘ supports the qiyās.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the strength of a hidden effective cause can override the apparent weakness of a metaphorical proof, making qiyas preferable to istihsan.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

12 min
Takhsis al-Illa and Istihsan: A Usul Dispute
Usul dispute analysis with critical refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to EXPLAIN the dispute on takhsis al-illa, STATE the opposing arguments, and EVALUATE the Hanafi refutation that istihsan does not involve specification of the cause but rather invalidates the qiyas.

Core Idea
Istihsan does not specify the illa; it nullifies the illa by invalidating the underlying qiyas.

This passage presents a fundamental usul al-fiqh debate: can the effective cause (illa) of a qiyas be present but its ruling absent due to a preventer? Some scholars, including al-Karkhi and Malik, allow this (takhsis al-illa), citing the analogy of a wet cloud that does not always bring rain. The majority of Hanafis, along with the preferred Shafi'i view, reject it because legal causes are deemed to necessitate their rulings. A key argument for takhsis comes from istihsan: when a manifest analogy contradicts istihsan, the ruling of the analogy is abandoned, allegedly specifying its illa. The author of our text vigorously refutes this, arguing that istihsan invalidates the analogy entirely, so its illa is never operative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Dispute
Determine the exact issue: whether a legal cause (illa) can be specified (takhsis) meaning it exists but its ruling is absent due to a preventer.
This is not about specifying the range of the cause but about its necessary connection to the ruling.
2
State the Two Positions
First, list the scholars who allow takhsis (al-Karkhi, al-Razi, Malik, Ahmad, Mu'tazila) and their evidence: the wet cloud analogy. Then state the opposing view (majority Hanafis, preferred Shafi'i) and their argument that the illa is a decisive proof that cannot be separated from its ruling.
Pay attention to the author's alignment with the latter position.
3
Analyze the Istihsan Argument for Takhsis
Some Hanafis claimed that istihsan itself proves takhsis: in cases where istihsan (a hidden analogy) overrides a manifest qiyas, the manifest qiyas's illa is present but the ruling is absent. Trace how they derive this from the operation of istihsan.
This is the argument the author aims to refute.
4
Understand the Author's Refutation
The author argues that when istihsan opposes a manifest qiyas, the qiyas is invalid because its conditions (absence of stronger evidence) are not met. Thus, the illa is not actually present; the ruling's absence is due to the absence of a valid illa, not due to a preventer. Istihsan is not specification but annulment of the qiyas.
The author uses examples of istihsan based on nas, ijma, and necessity to show that in those situations the qiyas had no standing from the start.
5
Derive the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: if takhsis were allowed, then when istihsan is applied, the manifest analogy's illa would still be considered valid but blocked. If not allowed (the author's view), the analogy is simply invalid and its illa irrelevant.
This difference affects how one views the coherence of the usul system and the role of istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أنه اختلف العلماء في العلة المستنبطة، قال الشيخ أبو الحسن الكرخي وأبو بكر الرازي وكثير من العراقيين والإمام مالك وأحمد بن حنبل وعامة المعتزلة: جاز أن تكون العلة مخصصة بأن يوجد الوصف الذي نسميه علة في بعض المواضع، ولا يوجد الحكم لمانع؛ لأن العلة الشرعية أمارة على الحكم يجعل الجاعل وليست بموجبة بنفسها، فيجوز أن لاتكون في بعض المواضع أمارة كالغيم الرطب، إنه أمارة على المطر وقد لا يوجد المطر ويوجد الغيم، وهذا لايقدح في كونه أمارة، وقال أكثر مشايخ الحنفية قديماً وحديثاً وهو أظهر قولي الشافعي وهو المختار عند المصنف: لا يجوز؛ لأنه لا يخلو إما أن يتخلّف الحكم عن العلة لمانع أو لا، والثاني باطل لا يخفى بطلانه والأول أيضا باطل؛ لأن علل الشرع أمارات وأدلة على أحكام الشرع، بمعنى أينما وجد العلة كانت موجبة للحكم ودليلا عليه، فإذا تخلّف الحكم عنها كان مناقضة. ولما أجاز بعض مشايخنا تخصيص العلة وقال: هذا مذهب علمائنا الثلاثة مستدلاً بالاستحسان فإن عند علمائنا يجوز الاستحسان اتفاقاً، وهو قول بتخصيص لأن القياس ثبت في صورة الاستحسان الذي هو قياس خفيّ في مقابلة القياس الجلي، فإذا عمل بالاستحسان وترك القياس فقد خصصت العلة الموجودة في القياس حيث لم يثبت الحكم الموافق للقياس لمانع، وهل هذا إلا تخصيص العلة الذي هو عبارة عن تخلف الحكم عن العلة في بعض الصور لمانع، فردّ المصنّف بقوله: ثم الاستحسان إلخ.

في مقابلة النص إلخ والاستحسان يتحقق بالنص والإجماع والضرورة وفي مقابلة تلك الأمور لا عبرة للقياس؛ إذ من شروط صحته عدم النص، فإذا كان الاستحسان ،بالنص، فكيف يعتبر في مقابلة القياس لفوت شرطه، فإذا فات الشرط فات المشروط، وهو القياس هنا، فإذا فات القياس فأين العلة في القياس، وكذا لايصح القياس في مقابلة الضرورة مثل الكتاب والسنة فكما لا يصح القياس في مقابلة الكتاب والسنة؛ لأنهما نصان، فكذا لا يجوز في مقابلة الإجماع والضرورة؛ لأنهما في حكم النص، ولما كان يرد أن الاستحسان كما يثبت بالنص والإجماع والضرورة يثبت بالقياس أيضا، فهذا جوابكم في الاستحسان الثابت بالأمور الثلاثة جوابكم في الاستحسان الثابت بالقياس أشار المصنف إلى دفعه بقوله: وكذا إذا عارضه إلخ. الاستحسان الذي المرجوح الضعيف في مقابلة الراجح القوي ،معدوم، فكما لا يصح القياس في مقابلة تلك الأمور الثلاثة كذا لا يصح في مقابلة الاستحسان أيضا كما مرّ دليله ،آنفا فحاصل الردّ أن الاستحسان ليس من باب خصوص العلل، أي ليس بدليل مخصص للقياس، حتى يقال: إن عدم الحكم ثابت مع وجود العلة لمانع بل القياس في مقابلة الاستحسان غير صحيح كما مرّ بيانه آنفا، فإذا لم يصح القياس لايوجد العلة. قيام العلة: كما توهم بعض مشايخنا المستدلين على جواز تخصيص العلة بالاستحسان وكذا أي كما قلنا في القياس في مقابلة الاستحسان من أن عدم الحكم هنا لعدم العلة لا أن العلة موجودة وتخلف الحكم عنها. العلل المؤثرة: التي تخلّف أحكامها في بعض المواضع من أن تخلف الحكم في تلك المواضع لعدم العلة، لا أن العلة موجودة وتخلف الحكم عنها لمانع، كما يقول أصحاب التخصيص. وبيان ذلك: أي بيان أن عدم الحكم عندنا =
Know that scholars differed concerning the derived cause. Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, Abu Bakr al-Razi, many of the Iraqis, Imam Malik, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and the general body of the Mu'tazila said: It is permissible for the cause to be specified, such that the description we call cause is found in some instances but the ruling is absent due to a preventer, because the legal cause is a sign of the ruling placed by the Lawgiver, not inherently necessitating it. So it may not be a sign in some cases, like a wet cloud — it is a sign of rain, but rain may not occur while the cloud exists, and this does not detract from its being a sign. The majority of Hanafi scholars, early and later, and the more apparent of Imam al-Shafi'i's two opinions, and the choice of the author, said: It is not permissible; because either the ruling is absent from the cause due to a preventer or not. The second is obviously invalid, and the first is also invalid, because the causes of the law are signs and proofs for the rulings of the law, meaning wherever the cause is found, it necessitates the ruling and is a proof for it. If the ruling is absent from it, it would be a contradiction. And since some of our scholars permitted the specification of the cause and said: This is the madhhab of our three imams, using istihsan as evidence, because in our school istihsan is unanimously permissible, and it is a statement of specification, because analogy is established in the instance of istihsan, which is a hidden analogy in contrast to a manifest analogy. So when one acts on istihsan and leaves the analogy, the cause present in the analogy has been specified, as the ruling consistent with the analogy is not established due to a preventer. Is this anything other than specification of the cause, which is the absence of the ruling from the cause in some images due to a preventer? The author responded by saying: Then istihsan, etc. [The author's response:] Istihsan is not from the chapter of specification of causes; because the description is not made a cause in the face of a clear text, consensus, and necessity; because necessity is consensus, and consensus is like the Book and the Sunnah. Similarly, if istihsan opposes it, it necessitates its absence, so the absence of the ruling is due to the absence of the cause of the manifest analogy, not due to a preventer while the cause is present. And similarly we say about all effective causes. ... [continues] The summary of the refutation is that istihsan is not from the chapter of specification of causes, i.e., it is not a proof that specifies the analogy, such that it is said that the absence of the ruling is established in the presence of the cause due to a preventer. Rather, the analogy in the face of istihsan is invalid, as explained earlier. When the analogy is invalid, the cause does not exist. ...
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage addresses a fundamental usul al-fiqh dispute: whether the effective cause (illa) in qiyas can be specified (takhsis), meaning that the cause might be present but the ruling is absent due to a preventer (mani). One group, including al-Karkhi, al-Razi, Malik, Ahmad, and the Mu'tazila, allow it, analogizing to a wet cloud as a sign of rain that may not always produce rain. The majority of Hanafis and the preferred Shafi'i view, which is also the author's choice, do not allow it because legal causes are signs that necessitate the ruling; if the ruling is absent when the cause is present, it is a contradiction. Some scholars argued that istihsan itself is a proof for takhsis al-illa, since istihsan is a hidden analogy that overrides a manifest analogy, seemingly specifying the cause of the manifest analogy. The author refutes this by explaining that istihsan operates only when the manifest analogy is invalid due to the presence of a stronger evidence (nas, ijma, necessity, or even a stronger istihsan). In such cases, there is no valid cause in the manifest analogy because the analogy itself is invalid. Hence, the absence of the ruling is not due to a preventer while the cause remains; rather, there is no cause at all. The author concludes that istihsan does not belong to the chapter of takhsis al-illa; it is a separate principle that nullifies the analogy entirely.

Key Terms
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that justifies a ruling in qiyas; a description that is a sign (amara) of the ruling placed by the Lawgiver.
تخصيص العلة (takhsis al-illa): The idea that a legal cause may exist in some instances but its ruling is absent due to a preventer; i.e., the cause is not universally tied to its ruling.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; preferring a hidden analogy or textual evidence over a manifest analogy, often based on necessity, custom, or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's refutation, why does istihsan not constitute takhsis al-illa?
A) Because istihsan is a weaker source than qiyas and cannot override it.
B) Because when istihsan overrides a manifest qiyas, the qiyas is invalid and its illa is not present, so there is no cause to specify.
C) Because takhsis al-illa is only permitted in cases of necessity, not in istihsan.
D) Because the author agrees with takhsis but argues that istihsan is a different phenomenon.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority view holds that a legal cause cannot be specified; istihsan overrides not by blocking an operative cause but by invalidating the opposing qiyas altogether.

The Ruling of Qiyas: Transference and the Dispute over Ta'lil
Definition of hukm al-qiyas and the dispute on ta'diya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hukm al-qiyas, identify the dispute regarding ta'diya, and apply the distinction to evaluate when a cause is transmissible.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, a valid cause must transfer; a non-transmissible derived cause is invalid.

This passage defines the ruling (hukm) of qiyas and immediately confronts a foundational usul dispute: does causation (ta'lil) require transference (ta'diya) to be valid? The Hanafi school insists that a derived cause must extend to the branch, while al-Shafi'i and the majority allow causation without transference. This difference has real consequences for which rulings can be extended by analogy, especially in areas like riba. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to identify the effective cause in any usul analysis.

Guided Path
1
Define the ruling of qiyas
Identify the two key components: transference (ta'diya) and predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y). The passage states that hukm al-qiyas is the transference of the ruling from the text to a new case with predominant opinion and possibility of error.
2
Locate the dispute on ta'lil
Find the point of contention: is ta'diya necessary for valid causation? The passage contrasts 'according to us' (Hanafis) with 'according to al-Shafi'i'.
3
Understand the Hanafi position and its proof
Hanafis hold that transference is a necessary consequence of causation. A cause that does not transfer (illa qasira) is invalid if derived (mustanbata). The nature of qiyas is to extend, so a non-extending cause fails.
Distinguish between textually specified (muttafaq) and derived causes.
4
Understand the opposing position
Shafi'i and the majority (including some Hanafis, Ahmad, Baqillani) allow ta'lil without ta'diya. Causation is like other evidence; it can be specific and still valid.
The example of thamaniyya (medium of exchange) as a non-transmissible cause for riba.
5
Apply the dispute to a concrete example
Consider riba in gold and silver. Shafi'i cause: thamaniyya (specific to gold and silver). Hanafi cause: weight or measure (transmissible to other commodities). The difference in cause leads to different rulings on riba al-fadl in wheat.
This thamarah al-khilaf shows practical implications.
