منه،
إلا المعارضة فيه إشارة إلى أنه تجري فيها الممانعة، وهو ما قبلها هو القول بموجب العلة ولا يجرى فيها ما بعد الممانعة، : وهو فساد الوضع والمعارضة والمناقضة.
السنة أو الإجماع فكما أن الكتاب والسنة والإجماع لا يحتمل المناقضة وفساد الوضع كذا العلل الثابتة بكل واحد من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع لاتحتملهما. مثال ما ظهر أثره بالكتاب كالخارج من البدن، فإنه علة للحدث، فظهر تأثيره في الحدث مرة في السبيلين بقوله تعالى: ﴿أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِنْكُمْ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ (النساء: ٤٣)، ومثال ما ظهر تأثيره بالسنة كالطواف، فإنه علة لعدم نجاسة سؤر سواكن البيوت، فإنه ظهر تأثيره مرةً في سؤر الهرة لقوله عليه: "إنما هي من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات) [الترمذي رقم: ۹۲]، ومثال ما ظهر تأثيره بالإجماع كالإتلاف، فإنه علة لعدم قطع يد السارق في المرة الثالثة، فإن فيه تفويت جنس المنفعة على الكمال، وحد السرقة إنما شرع زاجراً لا مُتلفاً بالإجماع، فلو قطع يده في المرة الثالثة لزم الإتلاف الممنوع إجماعاً، فتلك العلل لا تحتمل فساد الوضع أصلا بأن لا تصلح علة؛ لأنه ظهرت عليتها مرةً من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، وأما المناقضة
فإنها تتجه عليها صورة وإن لم تتجه حقيقة. وإليه أشار بقوله لكنه إذا تصوّر إلخ: وهي الدفع بالوصف ثم
=
باب القياس
۲۲۲
العلل والممانعة والمناقضة
كما نقول في الخارج من غير السبيلين: إنه نجس خارج من بدن الإنسان، فكان حدثاً كالبول، فيورد عليه ما إذا لم يسل، فندفعه أولاً بالوصف وهو أنه ليس
بخارج؛ لأن تحت كل جلدة رطوبة وفي كل عرق دما، فإذا زال الجلد كان ظاهراً
أي فارق مكانه صار الدم ونحوه
لا خارجاً ثم بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف دلالةً، وهو وجوب غسل ذلك الموضع
للتطهير فيه صار الوصف حجةً من حيث أن وجوب التطهير في البدن باعتبار
هو الخارج النجس عليه
ما يكون منه لا يحتمل الوصف بالتجزي، وهناك لم يجب غسل ذلك الموضع، فانعدم في غير المسائل
الحكم لعدم العلة
=
وهو
عن
بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف ثم بالحكم ثم بالغرض والتفصيل يأتي انتظره. فبعض النقوض يدفع بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف، وبعضه بغيره من الأقسام الأربعة الخارج من غير السبيلين إلخ فالخارج النجس علة للحدث، وقد ثبت تأثيره مرةً في السبيلين بقوله تعالى: أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِنْكُمْ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ . عليه: أي على تعليلنا هذا بالنقض من قبل الشافعي له. إذا لم يسل : أي لم يتجاوز المخرج فإنه نجس خارج وليس بحدث، فقد تخلف الحكم الحدث هذه العلة وهي الخارج؛ لأن تحت كل جلدة رطوبة وفي كل عرق دماً. ظاهراً لا خارجاً فالحاصل أن الوصف الذي هو علة للحدث ليس بموجود في مادة التخلّف، فإن العلة هي الخارج النجس، وما لم يسل ليس بخارج بل هو باد. ثم بالمعنى الثابت إلخ أي ثم ندفعه ثانياً بعدم المعنى الثابت بالوصف الذي كان ثبوته بالوصف بالدلالة، وبسبب هذا المعنى كان ذلك الوصف علة للحكم، فإذا لم يوجد فيه ذلك المعنى لم يكن علة، فإذا لم يوجد العلة لم يتخلّف الحكم كما تقول في ذلك المثال لو سلّم أن وصف الخروج موجود لكنه لم يوجد فيه المعنى الذي كان بسبه علة. وهو وجوب إلخ: لأنه يزيل بخروج النجس الطهارة الحاصلة للبدن ،كله، فيجب أولاً غسل ذلك الموضع من النجاسة ثم غسل البدن كله، ولكن لما كان فيه حرج عظيم اقتصر على الأعضاء الأربعة دفعاً للحرج فيه: أي بسبب وجوب غسل ذلك الموضع. ما يكون منه أي ما يخرج منه، لا ما يكون من خارج، فإن النجاسة الخارجية يوجب غسل ذلك الموضع فقط. لا يحتمل إلخ: فلما وجب غسل ذلك الموضع وجب غسل كل البدن لا محالة لعدم العلة: فكأنه لم يوجد الخروج لعدم المعنى المذكور، فلم يوجد الحكم وهو الحدث، لا أن العلة موجود والحكم متخلف كما قال الخصم.
Chapter of Qiyas. The effective causes, countering, and inconsistency. These aspects force the proponents of descriptive attributes to claim effect. As for effective causes, the questioner has after countering no recourse except counter-analogy; because effective causes do not admit inconsistency and invalidity of basis after their effect has been shown by the Book, Sunnah, or Ijma. But if an inconsistency is imagined, it must be repelled in four ways. After the exit of impurity for the removal of purity: for the entire body becomes impure by the exit of any impurity, so this is intelligible. Thus the analogy would be to wash the entire body after the exit of impurity. For impurity that exits less, the ruling remains on analogy like semen. But for that which exits more like urine, it was limited to washing the four limbs which are the principles of the body in the boundaries and the occurrence of sins, to remove hardship; because washing the whole body each time is a great hardship. So restricting to the four limbs is not rationally based, and wudu is not such restriction that it be considered irrational requiring intention. As for the impurity of the body by the exit of impurity and its removal by water, it is a rational matter not requiring intention, unlike tayammum, for soil is itself contaminating, not purifying by nature, hence it requires intention. The four ways (countering, counter-analogy, invalidity of basis, inconsistency) are brought against descriptive causes. From it, except counter-analogy, it is indicated that countering applies to it, and what precedes it is the statement of the requisite of the cause, and what follows countering does not apply: namely invalidity of basis, counter-analogy, and inconsistency. For the Sunnah or Ijma: just as the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma do not admit inconsistency and invalidity of basis, likewise the causes established by each of the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma do not admit them. Example of what shows its effect by the Book: what exits from the body, for it is a cause of hadath, its effect appeared once in the two passages by His saying: 'Or if one of you comes from the privy' (4:43). Example of what shows its effect by the Sunnah: circumambulation, for it is a cause for the non-impurity of the leftover of domestic animals, its effect appeared once in the leftover of the cat by his saying: 'It is from those who go around you and go around' (Tirmidhi 92). Example of what shows its effect by Ijma: destruction, for it is a cause for not cutting the hand of the thief in the third instance, for it involves losing the full benefit, and the punishment for theft was prescribed as a deterrent, not destructive by Ijma. So if his hand were cut in the third instance, destruction prohibited by Ijma would occur. Those causes do not admit invalidity of basis at all as not being fit as a cause, because their causation appeared once from the Book, Sunnah, and Ijma. As for inconsistency, it applies to them in form though not in reality. And to that he referred with his saying 'But if it is imagined, etc.': it is repelling by the description then. Chapter of Qiyas. Effective causes, countering, and inconsistency. Just as we say regarding what exits from other than the two passages: it is impure exiting from a human, so it is hadath like urine. Then it is objected upon with the case when it does not flow. So we repel it first by the description: it is not an exit; because under every skin there is moisture, and in every vein blood. When the skin is removed, it becomes apparent (i.e., it leaves its place, blood and the like become apparent), not an exit. Then by the meaning established by the description by indication, which is the obligation to wash that spot for purification. In that the description becomes a proof in that the obligation of purification in the body is considered based on what comes from it (the impure exit). What comes from it does not admit division of the description, and there the washing of that spot was not obligatory, so the ruling is absent in other than those cases due to absence of the cause. By the meaning established by the description, then by the ruling, then by the purpose; the detail will come, so wait. Some inconsistencies are repelled by the meaning established by the description, and some by other of the four divisions: what exits from other than the two passages, etc. So the impure exit is a cause for hadath, and its effect has been established once in the two passages by His saying: 'Or if one of you comes from the privy'. Upon it: i.e., upon our causation this by inconsistency from al-Shafi'i. 'If it does not flow': i.e., does not exceed the exit, then it is impure exiting but not hadath, so the ruling of hadath is absent from this cause which is the exit. Because under every skin there is moisture, and in every vein blood. Apparent, not exiting. So the conclusion is that the description which is the cause for hadath is not present in the case where it is absent. For the cause is the impure exit, and what does not flow is not an exit but rather apparent. Then by the meaning established etc.: i.e., then we repel it secondly by the absence of the meaning established by the description by indication, and because of this meaning that description was a cause for the ruling. So if that meaning is not present in it, it is not a cause. So if the cause is not present, the ruling is not absent, as you say in that example: even if the description of exit is conceded, the meaning due to which it was a cause is absent. And that is the obligation etc.: because it removes by the exit of impurity the purity of the entire body, so first it is obligatory to wash that spot from impurity, then to wash the entire body. But because there is great hardship, it was limited to the four limbs to remove hardship. In it: i.e., due to the obligation to wash that spot. 'What comes from it': i.e., what exits from it, not what comes from outside, for external impurity requires washing only that spot. Does not admit etc.: so when washing that spot became obligatory, washing the entire body became inevitable, so it is as if the exit did not occur due to the absence of the mentioned meaning. So the ruling, which is hadath, is absent, not that the cause is present and the ruling is absent as the opponent says.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage discusses the defense of effective causes (al-‘ilal al-mu’aththira) in qiyas. The author distinguishes between descriptive causes and effective causes. Effective causes are those that have been proven to have an effect by the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma. Once an effective cause is established by one of these sources, it cannot be invalidated by inconsistency (naqd) or invalidity of basis (fasd al-wad‘); the only permissible objection is counter-analogy (mu‘arada). However, if an inconsistency is only imagined in form, it must be repelled by one of four methods: repelling by the description (daf‘ bi al-wasf), by the meaning established by the description (bi al-ma‘na al-thabit bi al-wasf), by the ruling (bi al-hukm), or by the purpose (bi al-gharad). The text provides examples: for the cause of exiting from the body as a cause of hadath, it was proven effective by the Quran for the two passages. For the cat's saliva, the Prophet's hadith established that cats are from those who go around, so their leftover is pure. For the thief's hand, Ijma established that destruction is a cause for not cutting in the third instance. Then the text addresses an objection from al-Shafi‘i regarding something exiting from a wound that does not flow. The Hanafi response uses the first two methods: first, by the description, the thing is not considered an exit because it remains under the skin; second, by the meaning, the intended meaning (obligation to wash the spot) is absent when the exit does not flow, so the cause (exit) does not exist. Thus, there is no genuine inconsistency.

Key Terms
العلة المؤثرة (al-‘illah al-mu’aththirah): An effective cause whose legal effect has been confirmed by a textual source (Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma) in at least one instance.
المناقضة (al-munaqadah): An inconsistency where the cause is present but the ruling is absent, or vice versa, used by opponents to invalidate a cause.
الممانعة (al-mumana‘ah): Countering: the opponent argues that the alleged cause is not effective by presenting a case where the cause exists but the ruling does not, or vice versa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi defense of the effective cause 'impure exit' against the challenge of non-flowing wound impurity, which two methods are applied?
A) Daf‘ bi al-wasf and daf‘ bi al-hukm
B) Daf‘ bi al-wasf and daf‘ bi al-ma‘na
C) Daf‘ bi al-ma‘na and daf‘ bi al-gharad
D) Daf‘ bi al-hukm and daf‘ bi al-gharad

Key Takeaway
Apparent inconsistencies against effective causes can be repelled by denying the description, the meaning, the ruling, or the purpose—ensuring the cause remains intact.
